- **Concept:** Removes the cascading effect of taxing dividend at each corporate layer by allowing a deduction for dividend received-and-redistributed within the specified window (reintroduced by Finance Act 2020 after DDT abolition).
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Only the dividend actually **received** and **redistributed by the due date** qualifies — dividend distributed after the due date does not count for the deduction, even if distributed within the same P.Y.
  - Deduction is claimed under **Chapter VI-A** against Gross Total Income, so it cannot exceed GTI and follows normal Chapter VI-A ordering rules.
  - The "dividend income received" limb of the Sec. 80M comparison is the amount actually **included in Gross Total Income**, i.e. dividend **net of the Sec. 57 interest deduction** (not the gross dividend received) — confirmed by the standard worked illustration where net dividend of ₹9,60,000 (after 20% interest deduction) is used, not the gross ₹12,00,000.
  - *Sree Rama Multi Tech Ltd. (2018, SC):* Interest earned on share-application money kept in a separate mandatory bank account (pending allotment) is incidental to a statutory compliance requirement, not an independent intention to earn interest — hence set off against public-issue expenses and not taxed as IFOS.

### References
1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sec. 56(2)(x), Sec. 57, Sec. 58, Sec. 2(22)(a)-(e), Sec. 80M, Sec. 43CA, Sec. 115BB (bare act text, incometaxindia.gov.in).
2. CBDT Notification No. 40/2020 — exemptions from Sec. 56(2)(x) (unauthorised colonies, NCLT resolution plans, Yes Bank scheme, strategic disinvestment).
3. CBDT Circular No. 19/2017 — trade advances excluded from Sec. 2(22)(e) deemed dividend.
4. Finance Act, 2020 — abolition of Dividend Distribution Tax and introduction of Sec. 80M; Finance Act, 2020 raising the Sec. 43CA/50C safe-harbour to 110%.
5. Case laws: *Manju & Co. (2011) Kerala HC*; *Dr. Ranjan Pai (2021) Kar HC*; *Vir Vikram Vaid (2014) Bom HC*; *Sree Rama Multi Tech Ltd. (2018) SC*.

## 03. Corporate Reorganisation: Liquidation, Buy-Back, Amalgamation & Demerger

> **Where it fits:** This chapter covers the capital-gains and deemed-dividend consequences when a company winds up (liquidation), buys back its own shares, merges with another company (amalgamation), or spins off an undertaking (demerger) — a recurring 6-10 mark area in CA Final DT, tested both as standalone theory and inside larger capital-gains problems.

### Liquidation

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - In the hands of the **company**: distribution of assets to shareholders on liquidation is deemed dividend to the extent of accumulated profits u/s **2(22)(c)**; but the distribution itself is **not a "transfer"** u/s **46(1)**, so the company has **no capital gains**.
  - In the hands of the **shareholder**, capital gain on liquidation:

$$
\text{FVOC} = \Big(\text{Money received} + \text{FMV of asset received on date of distribution}\Big) - \text{Amount already taxed as deemed dividend u/s } 2(22)(c)
$$

$$
\text{STCG/LTCG} = \text{FVOC} - \text{COA/ICOA of shares}
$$

  - Cost of the asset so received by the shareholder (for its subsequent sale) = **FMV on the date of distribution** [Sec. 55].
- **Concept:** Liquidation triggers two separate tax events — dividend taxation at the company/shareholder interface, and capital gains on the shareholder's *shares* (not on the underlying assets, which the company transfers tax-free under 46(1)).
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Do not tax the company on liquidation distribution — a common trap is applying capital gains at the company level.
  - Period of holding of shares = date of acquisition of shares to date of liquidation.
  - Capital gain is taxable in the shareholder's hands in the **year assets are actually received**, not the year the company goes into liquidation.
- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Deemed dividend u/s 2(22)(c) | Distribution on liquidation, to the extent of accumulated profits (whether capitalised or not), immediately before liquidation |
| FVOC | Full value of consideration for the shareholder's capital gains computation |

### Buy-Back — Unlisted/Foreign Shares & Other Specified Securities (pre-existing regime)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - No tax in the hands of the company on buy-back of shares/specified securities (other than domestic company shares covered below).
  - Shareholder — capital gains u/s **46A**:

$$
\text{STCG/LTCG} = \text{Buy-back price (FVOC)} - \text{COA/ICOA of shares}
$$

  - Period of holding = date of acquisition to date of buy-back.
- **Concept:** Sec. 46A treats buy-back as extinguishment of shareholder rights, taxed as capital gains at the buy-back price.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Where any part of the buy-back consideration is separately taxed as deemed dividend u/s 2(22)(f), FVOC for 46A purposes becomes **NIL** for that amount [inserted by Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024, w.e.f. 01-10-2024] — see next section for the current domestic-company regime.

### Buy-Back of Shares by a Domestic Company — w.e.f. 1 October 2024

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - No tax in the hands of the company (Sec. 115QA does **not** apply to buy-backs undertaken on or after 01-10-2024).
  - Entire buy-back consideration received by the shareholder is **deemed dividend u/s 2(22)(f)**, taxable under **IFOS** at normal slab/applicable rates (no deduction for cost of acquisition against this dividend income).
  - Simultaneously, u/s **46A**, buy-back is treated as extinguishment of rights, but FVOC is deemed **NIL**:

$$
\text{STCL/LTCL} = \text{NIL} - \text{COA of shares} = -(\text{COA of shares})
$$

  - This capital loss can be set off against any other STCG/LTCG (as applicable) and carried forward for **8 assessment years**.
  - TDS: company deducts tax at source on the deemed dividend u/s 194 (10% for residents, subject to threshold) / Sec. 195 for non-residents.
- **Concept:** Post 1-10-2024, buy-back proceeds are economically re-characterised as dividend (taxed at shareholder's slab rate) instead of the earlier company-level buy-back distribution tax u/s 115QA; the cost of the bought-back shares survives only as a capital loss.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - This is a favourite "current amendment" question — always split the answer into (a) deemed dividend under IFOS, and (b) capital loss under 46A with FVOC = Nil.
  - Do NOT let students deduct COA from the dividend income — COA is used only in the loss computation, never against the dividend.
  - Watch the exam date carefully: buy-backs **before** 01-10-2024 still follow the old 115QA (company-level buy-back tax, exempt in shareholder's hands) regime.
- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Sec. 2(22)(f) | Inserted by FA (No. 2) 2024; treats buy-back consideration paid by a domestic company (as per Sec. 68, Companies Act 2013) as deemed dividend |
| Sec. 46A | Capital gains on buy-back of shares/specified securities; extinguishment of rights |
| Sec. 115QA | Erstwhile company-level buy-back distribution tax; inapplicable to buy-backs on/after 01-10-2024 |

**Worked illustration (from source):** Mr. BB bought 1,000 shares of BBVL @ ₹50 (PY 20-21). BBVL buys back 300 shares @ ₹120 on 10-12-2025 (PY 25-26). Mr. BB sells the remaining 700 shares @ ₹200 on 15-07-2026 (PY 26-27).
- PY 25-26: ₹36,000 (300 × ₹120) taxed as deemed dividend u/s 2(22)(f) under IFOS; separately, LTCL of ₹15,000 (Nil − 300×₹50 COA) arising u/s 46A, carried forward.
- PY 26-27: LTCG on sale of 700 shares = (700×₹200) − (700×₹50) = ₹1,05,000; less b/f LTCL ₹15,000 = **net taxable LTCG ₹90,000** (AY 27-28).

### Amalgamation

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Sec. 2(1B)** defines amalgamation — requires: (i) all assets & liabilities of amalgamating company become those of amalgamated company, and (ii) shareholders holding **at least 75% in value** of shares in the amalgamating company become shareholders of the amalgamated company.
  - Shareholder — no capital gains on exchange of shares u/s **47**:

$$
\text{COA of shares in Amalgamated Co.} = \text{COA of shares in Amalgamating Co.} \quad \text{[Sec. 49(2)]}
$$

  - Period of holding (shareholder) = period held in amalgamating company + period held in amalgamated company.
  - Amalgamating company — no capital gains on transfer of assets to amalgamated company [Sec. 47].
  - Amalgamated company:

$$
\text{COA of asset to Amalgamated Co.} = \text{COA to Amalgamating Co. (cost to previous owner)} \quad \text{[Sec. 49(1)]}
$$

  Period of holding of the asset includes the period held by the amalgamating company.
- **Concept:** Amalgamation is structured as a tax-neutral reorganisation at all three levels (amalgamating company, amalgamated company, shareholders) provided the 2(1B) conditions are met.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - The 75% test is by **value of shares**, not by number of shareholders.
  - PGBP business losses and unabsorbed depreciation of the amalgamating company can be carried forward and set off by the amalgamated company subject to Sec. 72A conditions (see below) — do not assume automatic, unconditional carry-forward.
- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Amalgamating company | The company that ceases to exist / merges |
| Amalgamated company | The company into which merger takes place |

### Demerger

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Sec. 2(19AA)** — demerger conditions (illustrated: Titan Ltd. demerges Tanishq Jewellery undertaking into Tanishq Ltd.):
    - (a) All assets & liabilities of the transferred undertaking become those of the resulting company.
    - (b) Transfer is at **book value** (revaluation ignored) — this condition does not apply where the resulting company records assets/liabilities at a different value to comply with Ind-AS.
    - (c) Resulting company issues shares to shareholders of the demerged company on a **proportionate basis**, except where the resulting company is itself a shareholder of the demerged company.
    - (d) Shareholders holding **at least 75% in value** of shares in the demerged company become shareholders of the resulting company.
    - (e) Transfer of the undertaking is on a **going concern basis**.
  - Shareholder — no capital gains u/s **47** on receipt of resulting-company shares; period of holding of resulting-company shares includes period held in demerged company [Sec. 2(42A)].
  - **Sec. 49(2C)** — COA of shares in the Resulting Company:

$$
\text{COA (Resulting Co. shares)} = \text{COA of shares held in Demerged Co.} \times \frac{\text{Net worth of the demerged undertaking immediately before demerger}}{\text{Net worth of the demerged company immediately before demerger}}
$$

  where **Net worth = Paid-up share capital + General reserves** (as appearing in the books of the demerged company immediately before demerger).

  - **Sec. 49(2D)** — COA of shares retained in the Demerged Company:

$$
\text{COA (Demerged Co. shares)} = \text{COA of original shares in Demerged Co.} - \text{COA of shares in Resulting Co. [per 49(2C)]}
$$

  - Resulting company: COA of asset received = COA to the demerged company (carryover basis); demerged company has no capital gains u/s 47 on transfer of the undertaking.
- **Concept:** Demerger is a tax-neutral "vertical split" of a company — assets/liabilities move at book value with a proportionate cost-splitting mechanism between demerged and resulting company shares for the shareholder.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Do not confuse the 49(2C) apportionment ratio: it uses **net worth of the undertaking transferred** over **net worth of the demerged company as a whole**, not turnover or asset value.
  - PGBP losses & unabsorbed depreciation relating to the transferred undertaking can be carried forward and set off by the resulting company, subject to Sec. 72A conditions.
  - ⚠️ VERIFY — the precise statutory wording of "net worth" for Sec. 49(2C)/2(19AA)(iv) purposes; some formulations reference Explanation 1 to Sec. 2(19AA), confirm exact phrase ("paid-up share capital and general reserves as appearing in the books of account of the demerged company immediately before demerger") against the bare Act before quoting verbatim in an answer.
- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Demerged company | Company transferring the undertaking (e.g., Titan Ltd.) |
| Resulting company | Company receiving the undertaking (e.g., Tanishq Ltd.) |
| Net worth (Sec. 49(2C)) | Paid-up share capital + General reserves of the demerged company, immediately before demerger |

### Sec. 72A — Carry Forward of Losses on Amalgamation/Demerger

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):** PGBP losses and unabsorbed depreciation of the amalgamating company (on amalgamation) / relating to the transferred undertaking (on demerger) are allowed to be carried forward and set off by the amalgamated/resulting company, subject to prescribed conditions (nature of amalgamating companies, continuity of business, retention of a specified % of fixed assets, minimum period of holding, etc.) — refer to the Set-off & Carry Forward chapter for the full condition checklist.
- **Concept:** Without Sec. 72A, losses of the predecessor entity would lapse on reorganisation; this section preserves them for the successor, subject to anti-abuse conditions.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - **Case law — CIT v. KBD Sugars and Distilleries Ltd. [(2023) 454 ITR 800 (SC)]**: the Supreme Court affirmed the Karnataka High Court that "transfer of the undertaking on a going concern basis" [Sec. 2(19AA)(v)] means the *manner of transfer* must be as a going concern — it does **not** require that the undertaking itself be a profitable/functioning ("going concern") unit as on the date of demerger. A dysfunctional/loss-making unit can still be validly demerged and the resulting company remains entitled to carry forward losses u/s 72A(4).
  - This case is frequently tested as a theory/case-law question — remember the core holding: "manner of transfer," not "status of the unit."

### Sec. 94 — Bonus Stripping, Dividend Stripping & Bond Washing (allied anti-avoidance provisions)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Sec. 94(1) — Bond washing transactions:** Where securities are sold before the interest due date and reacquired after, and the result is that interest becomes receivable by the transferee instead of the transferor, such interest is **deemed to be income of the transferor**. Exceptions apply where there is no tax avoidance (e.g., transferee taxable at the same rate) or the transaction was an isolated one with no avoidance in the preceding 3 years.
  - **Sec. 94(7) — Dividend/interest stripping:** Applies where a person:
    1. buys/acquires securities or units within **3 months prior to the record date**; and
    2. sells/transfers such — (a) **securities within 3 months** after the record date, or (b) **units within 9 months** after the record date; and
    3. the dividend/income on such securities/units is exempt (or, per current law, taxable but the loss-restriction principle applies to the extent of income received).

$$
\text{Loss allowed to be recognised} = \text{Actual loss} - \text{Income/dividend received (to the extent exempt/received)}
$$

    i.e., the loss is **ignored to the extent of the income/dividend** received on those securities/units.
  - **Sec. 94(8) — Bonus stripping:** Applies where a person:
    1. buys/acquires units or securities within **3 months prior to the record date**;
    2. is allotted **bonus units/securities** on account of holding the original units/securities; and
    3. sells/transfers the **original** units/securities within **9 months from the record date**, while continuing to hold all or any of the bonus units/securities.
    Consequence: loss on transfer of the original units/securities is **completely ignored** (not merely restricted) and is instead **added to the cost of acquisition of the bonus units/securities** that remain unsold as on the date of transfer of the originals.
  - Note: the loss ignored u/s 94(7)/94(8) need not be a capital loss — it could equally be a business loss.
- **Concept:** These are anti-avoidance provisions preventing investors from engineering artificial short-term losses around dividend/bonus record dates while retaining economic exposure.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - 94(7): the after-record-date holding period differs by asset type — **3 months for securities/shares**, **9 months for units** (mutual fund/UTI units) — a very common exam trap if the two are swapped.
  - 94(8): only the **loss on original shares** is disallowed and shifted to bonus-share cost; if bonus shares themselves are later sold at a loss/gain, that is computed normally (loss on bonus shares is NOT covered by 94(8), only original-share loss is redirected).
  - "Record date" = date fixed by the company/MF/UTI/Business Trust/AIF for determining entitlement to dividend, income, or additional securities/units without consideration.
- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Record date | Date fixed for determining shareholder/unit-holder entitlement to dividend/bonus |
| Bond washing | Sale-and-buy-back of an interest-bearing security around the interest due date to shift interest income |
| Dividend/bonus stripping | Buying just before, and selling just after, a record date to book an artificial loss while retaining bonus units/securities |

**Worked illustration pattern (from source, bonus stripping u/s 94(8)):** Saloni buys 1,000 shares of ITC @ ₹200 (16-07-25); company allots 700 bonus shares on record date 16-09-25; Saloni sells all 1,000 original shares @ ₹120 on 14-02-26 (within 9 months of record date, continuing to hold bonus shares) → STCL of ₹80,000 on original shares is **not allowed to be set off/carried forward**; instead it is added to the cost of the 700 bonus shares (i.e., ₹80,000/700 per share, apportioned pro-rata on partial subsequent sale of bonus shares). If, instead, all bonus shares are also sold within the same transaction as the originals (before the 9-month bonus-stripping condition can apply to defer any bonus shares), the ₹80,000 loss remains an ordinary STCL available for set-off against the gain on bonus shares, since no bonus shares are "left out" for cost-shifting.

### References

1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sections 2(1B), 2(19AA), 2(22)(c), 2(22)(f), 46(1), 46A, 47, 49(1), 49(2), 49(2C), 49(2D), 55, 72A, 94(1), 94(7), 94(8), 115QA — bare Act text, via IndianKanoon and incometaxindia.gov.in.
2. Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024 — insertion of Sec. 2(22)(f) and consequential Sec. 46A amendment (FVOC deemed Nil), effective 1 October 2024 — summarised in MNCL, Treelife, and S&R Associates commentaries on buy-back taxation post-October 2024.
3. CIT v. KBD Sugars and Distilleries Ltd., (2023) 454 ITR 800 (SC), affirming Karnataka HC (2022) 220 DTR 483 — on "going concern" transfer under Sec. 2(19AA) and Sec. 72A(4) carry-forward eligibility.
4. ICAI CA Final DT Study Material / BB Sir (CA Bhanwar Borana) Concept Book — for problem-format and computation layout of liquidation, buy-back, amalgamation, demerger and Sec. 94 illustrations (source OCR, lines 1680-1893).

## 04. Profits & Gains of Business or Profession (PGBP)

> **Where it fits:** Computes taxable business/professional income under Sections 28–44DB — the charging section (28), computation machinery (30–43D), specified deductions/disallowances (36, 37, 40, 40A, 43B), deemed income (41), and presumptive-taxation shortcuts (44AD/ADA/AE and NR presumptive sections) that let small assessees skip full books/audit.

### Sec 28 — Charging Section: What Is Taxable as PGBP

- **Key rule(s):**
  - Profits of any business/profession; profit on sale of import entitlement licences; cash compensatory support/duty drawback; profit on sale of DEPB/DFRC.
  - Any sum received under a **Keyman insurance policy**.
  - Any gift/benefit/perquisite (cash or kind) arising from business/profession.
  - Partner's interest/salary/bonus/commission from the firm — taxable only **to the extent allowed to the firm u/s 40(b)**.
  - **Non-compete fees** (for not carrying on an activity / not sharing know-how, patent, copyright, trademark, etc.).
  - Income of a trade/professional association from specific services rendered to members.
  - FMV of inventory on the date it is converted into a capital asset.
  - Any compensation (revenue **or capital**) on termination/modification of a business contract.
  - **Exception:** income from letting out a residential house (or part) by the owner is **not** PGBP — it is taxed under "Income from House Property" [Explanation inserted by FA 2024 w.e.f. AY 2025-26].
- **Concept:** Sec 28 is the charging section; Sec 29 mandates that PGBP be computed per Secs 30–43D.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - The FA 2024 residential-letting carve-out means *Chennai Properties & Investments Ltd (SC)* (letting as main object → PGBP) now survives **only for commercial properties**, not residential.
  - Speculative business (contracts settled otherwise than by actual delivery) is a **separate, distinct business** — its loss can be set off/carried forward only against speculative income. Hedging contracts, forward contracts, and exchange-traded derivatives (incl. CTT-paid commodity derivatives) are **not** speculative transactions.

### Sec 30/31 — Rent, Rates, Repairs, Insurance (Building, P&M, Furniture)

- **Key rule(s) — Building [Sec 30]:**

| | Rent | Rates & Taxes | Insurance | Revenue Repair | Capital Repair |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Owner | Not allowed | Allowed | Allowed | Allowed | Not allowed |
| Tenant | Allowed | Allowed | Allowed | Allowed | Not allowed |

  - **Key rule(s) — P&M/Furniture [Sec 31]:** Rent (owner: not allowed; tenant: allowed), Insurance (allowed both), Revenue repair (allowed both), Capital repair (not allowed to either).
- **Concept:** Capital repairs are never a straight deduction — they are capitalised into the cost of the asset (added to the block for depreciation); a tenant's capital repair creates a **"deemed building"** on which the tenant claims depreciation.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Deduction under Secs 30/31/32 applies only to assets **used for business/profession**.
  - If a firm occupies premises owned by a partner, rent paid is allowed only to the extent it is **reasonable and not excessive**.

### Sec 32 — Depreciation: Conditions & Block System

- **Key rule(s) — Conditions to claim:**
  - Asset must be used for business/profession (active **or passive** use suffices).
  - Assessee must be the **owner** (wholly or partly) — beneficial ownership is enough.
  - Lease: depreciation is **always claimed by the lessor**, whether finance or operating lease [CBDT Circular]; confirmed in *ICDS Ltd v CIT (2013, SC)*.
  - Hire-purchase: buyer can claim depreciation from the start, treated as owner from inception even though legal title passes only on last instalment.
  - Standby machinery/emergency spares: depreciation allowed even if kept ready for use but not actually used.
- **Key formula(s)/rule(s) — WDV computation (block of assets):**

$$
\text{Closing WDV} = \text{Opening WDV} + \text{Actual cost of assets acquired during PY} - \text{Money payable (sale value/scrap)} - \text{Depreciation actually allowed}
$$

  - "Money payable" = sale price/insurance compensation of assets sold, discarded, demolished or destroyed + scrap value. **Actual** sale price is reduced, never FMV (Building: SDV applies only if Sec 50 attracted).
  - **Block can go to Nil but never negative.**
- **Concept:** Under the WDV method, assets of the same class **and** same rate form one "block of asset"; depreciation is computed on the block, not asset-by-asset (SLM/individual-asset system applies only to power units that opt for SLM).
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Asset acquired but **not put to use** in the year gets no depreciation that year but is still added to the block (WDV).
  - If a slump sale transfers some block assets, reduce the WDV of transferred assets (computed assuming it were the only asset in the block).

### Sec 32 — Depreciation Rates (WDV, Block of Asset System)

- **Key rule(s)/rates:**

| Block | Assets | Rate |
|---|---|---|
| Building | Residential use (except hotels) | 5% |
| Building | Other use (business/commercial) | 10% |
| Building | Temporary/wooden structure | 40% |
| Furniture & Fittings | Incl. electrical fittings (fans, wires, switches) | 10% |
| Plant & Machinery | Motor cars (general) | 15% |
| P&M | Motor cars acquired & put to use 23.08.2019–31.03.2020 | 30% |
| P&M | Motor vehicles (lorries/buses/taxis) in hire business (general) | 30% |
| P&M | Above, acquired & put to use 23.08.2019–31.03.2020 | 45% |
| P&M | Ships, vessels, speed boats | 20% |
| P&M | Aeroplanes, aeroengines | 40% |
| P&M | Computers & computer software (incl. accessories: UPS, printer, scanner) | 40% |
| P&M | Books (annual publications / used in libraries) | 40% |
| P&M | Pollution control equipment | 40% |
| P&M | Windmills & equipment installed before 01.04.2014 | 15% |
| P&M | Windmills & equipment installed on/after 01.04.2014 | 40% |
| P&M | Renewable energy devices (incl. E-vehicles) | 40% |
| P&M | Oil wells | 15% |
| P&M | Other P&M (residual/general rate) | 15% |
| Intangibles | Know-how, patents, copyrights, trademarks, licences, franchises, similar commercial rights (excl. goodwill of business/profession) | 25% |

- **Concept:** These are current Appendix-I (Income-tax Rules) rates applicable for AY 2026-27 (FY 2025-26).
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - EPABX and mobile phones are **not** "computers" — 40% rate is **not** available; general P&M rate (15%) applies.
  - Depreciation is **mandatory** for all assessees (cannot be foregone to save WDV).
  - Sec 43(3): "plant" includes ships, vehicles, books, scientific apparatus & surgical equipment used for business/profession, but **excludes** tea bushes, livestock, buildings, furniture.
  - Depreciation is allowed only when the asset is **actually put to use**, not merely "ready to use" (standby machinery is the sole express exception).

### Sec 32 — 180-Day Rule, Additional Depreciation & Actual Cost

- **Key rule(s) — Proviso to Sec 32(1) (180-day rule):**
  - If an asset is put to use for **less than 180 days** in the **year of acquisition**, depreciation is restricted to **50% of the normal rate**; from the following year, full rate applies. The restriction applies only in the year of acquisition, never in later years.
- **Key rule(s) — Sec 32(1)(iia) Additional Depreciation:**
  - Eligible assessee: engaged in **manufacture of an article** or in **generation/transmission/distribution of power**.
  - Rate: **20% of actual cost** of new P&M (10% if put to use for less than 180 days in the year of acquisition, with the balance 10% allowed in the immediately succeeding year).
  - Not available on: second-hand P&M; P&M installed in office premises/residential accommodation; ships, aircraft, transport vehicles; P&M eligible for 100% deduction elsewhere.
  - Available only under the **WDV method** (not to power units opting SLM).
  - Printing/printing-and-publishing is treated as a **manufacturing business** for this purpose [CBDT]. Forklift trucks used in a factory are **not** "transport vehicles", hence eligible.
- **Key formula(s)/rule(s) — Sec 43(1) Actual Cost:**

$$
\text{Actual Cost} = \text{Purchase price} + \text{Installation} + \text{Transport} + \text{Trial-run expenses} + \text{Non-creditable taxes/duties} + \text{Interest till date first put to use} - \text{Sale proceeds of trial-run output} - \text{Govt. subsidy/grant related to the asset}
$$

  - Any expenditure for acquiring an asset paid to a single person in a single day otherwise than by account-payee cheque/DD/ECS, exceeding **₹10,000**, is excluded from actual cost.
- **Concept:** "Actual cost" (Sec 43(1)) feeds both the depreciation block and cost of acquisition for capital gains on depreciable assets.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Interest on borrowed funds **up to** the date the asset is first put to use is capitalised into actual cost; interest **after** that date is a revenue deduction.

### Sec 43(1) — Actual Cost in Special Cases (Explanation)

- **Definitions:**

| Case | Actual Cost |
|---|---|
| Asset earlier used for scientific research, now brought into business | NIL (deduction already claimed u/s 35) |
| Stock converted into capital asset, used in business | FMV on date of conversion |
| Acquired by gift/will/inheritance | Cost to previous owner **less** depreciation already allowed to him |
| Acquired mainly to claim higher depreciation | Amount determined by AO with JC's approval (usually FMV) |
| Re-acquisition of asset sold | WDV at time of sale, or reacquisition cost — as prescribed |
| Sale-and-leaseback to same person | WDV to the previous owner (lessee) |
| Holding ↔ 100% subsidiary transfer [Sec 47(iv)/(v)] | Cost/opening WDV to transferor company |
| Amalgamating Co. → Amalgamated Co. | Cost/opening WDV to amalgamating company |
| Demerged Co. → Resulting Co. | Cost/WDV (at demerger) to demerged company |
| Asset brought into India by a non-resident | Actual cost **less** notional depreciation at rates in force, as if used in India since acquisition |
| Asset on which Sec 35AD deduction claimed, later transferred to non-specified business after 8 years | Actual cost for transferee = NIL |

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** In agriculture-cum-manufacture cases (tea/coffee/rubber, Rule 8: 40% business income), WDV must be reduced by the **full** depreciation computed on 100% PGBP basis (deemed "actually allowed"), not just the 40% portion — per Explanation 7 to Sec 43(6).

### Sec 32 — Sale of Depreciable Assets (Block System) & Balancing Charge

- **Key rule(s):**
  - **Block ceases to exist** (all assets sold): result is always **STCG/STCL** — Full value of consideration **less** cost of acquisition (opening WDV + additions); no depreciation for the year, block closes to Nil.
  - **Some assets sold, block survives:** sale value is simply deducted from WDV of block; if resulting WDV is negative, the excess is **STCG**, and WDV is taken as Nil; depreciation continues on the surviving block.
  - **Power units on SLM (individual asset system):** on sale, Sale value − WDV of that asset:
    - Loss → **terminal depreciation** u/s 32(1)(iii), debited to P&L.
    - Profit up to original cost → **balancing charge** u/s 41(2), taxable as PGBP.
    - Profit beyond original cost → the "up to cost" portion is balancing charge u/s 41(2); excess over cost is capital gain.
- **Concept:** Depreciable-asset sales under the block (WDV) system generate only **short-term** capital gain/loss — never long-term — regardless of holding period.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** "Block can be Nil but never negative" — memorise this for MCQs.

### Sec 32 — Depreciation in Amalgamation/Demerger/Succession & Partial Business Use

- **Key rule(s):**
  - Depreciation is first computed normally for the full year, then **apportioned between predecessor and successor in the ratio of number of days each used the asset** — applicable to amalgamation, demerger, and "succession" (firm/proprietorship → company [Sec 47(xiii)/(xiv)], company → LLP [Sec 47(xiiib)], or any other succession other than by death).
  - **Sec 32(2) Unabsorbed depreciation:** If PGBP is insufficient to absorb depreciation, the unabsorbed amount is added to next year's depreciation allowance and carried forward **indefinitely**; it can be set off against income under any head **except Salaries**, even after the business itself ceases to exist.
  - **Order of set-off:** current year depreciation → brought-forward business loss → unabsorbed depreciation.
  - **Partial business use [applies to Secs 30, 31, 32]:** if an asset is not exclusively used for business, deduction is restricted to a proportion determined by the AO; only the **allowed** (business-use) portion of depreciation reduces the block's closing WDV.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Unlike a normal business loss (8-year carry-forward limit), unabsorbed depreciation has **no time limit** for carry-forward.

### Sec 33AB / 33ABA — Tea/Coffee/Rubber & Petroleum Deposit-Linked Deductions

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

$$
\text{Sec 33AB deduction} = \min\left(\text{Actual amount deposited},\ 40\% \text{ of PGBP (before this deduction)}\right)
$$

$$
\text{Sec 33ABA deduction} = \min\left(\text{Actual amount deposited},\ 20\% \text{ of PGBP (before this deduction)}\right)
$$

- **Definitions:**

| | Sec 33AB (Tea/Coffee/Rubber) | Sec 33ABA (Petroleum & Natural Gas) |
|---|---|---|
| Deposit account | NABARD | State Bank of India (Site Restoration A/c) |
| Deposit deadline | Due date of ROI filing, or 6 months from end of PY, whichever is earlier | End of the PY |
| Governing body for utilisation | Tea/Coffee/Rubber Board | Ministry of Petroleum & Natural Gas |

- **Concept:** Encourages ploughback of profits into NABARD/site-restoration deposits by growers/manufacturers of tea, coffee, rubber, and petroleum/natural gas businesses.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Mis-utilised deposits, or withdrawals not utilised in the year of withdrawal, are taxable as PGBP.
  - Asset sold/transferred within **8 years** from end of the year of acquisition (funded from this deposit) triggers PGBP taxation of the deduction-relatable portion — exceptions for transfer to Government/local authority/statutory corporation, and firm-to-company succession with identical shareholders.
  - Audit report required in **Form 3AC (33AB) / 3AD (33ABA)**, at least 1 month before the Sec 44AB due date.

### Sec 35 — Scientific Research Expenditure

- **Key rule(s):**
  - **In-house research [Sec 35(1)]:** revenue and capital expenditure (except land) on scientific research related to the assessee's own business is deductible.
  - **Sec 35(2AB)** (in place of 35(1)) — **100%** deduction on all revenue & capital expenditure **except land & building**, if: assessee is a **company**, engaged in **manufacturing or bio-technology** business, and research is approved by the prescribed authority. Building expenditure is separately allowed 100% under Sec 35(1)(iv); land gets no deduction.
  - **Donations to outside institutions [Sec 35(1)(ii)/(iia)/(iii), 35(2AA)]:** deduction (rate depends on sub-clause and recipient — approved research association/university/college/company/national laboratory) for contributions to approved scientific research bodies.
- **Concept:** Sec 35 rewards R&D spend either directly (in-house) or via approved third-party research institutions.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Deduction is **not denied** merely because the donee institution's approval is later withdrawn (after the assessee's payment).
  - **No depreciation** is separately allowed on assets for which Sec 35 deduction has been claimed.
  - Weighted deduction of 150% under 35(1)(ii)/35(2AA)/35(2AB) stood withdrawn — restricted to 100% **from AY 2021-22** onward.
  - Composite land + building purchase: bifurcate cost by FMV (land portion never deductible).
  - **Sec 35(1A) compliance:** donee must file **Form 10BD** (statement) with PDGIT(Systems) by **31st May** of the following FY, and issue **Form 10BE** (certificate) to the donor by the same date — else deduction to the payer may be denied.
  - Unabsorbed capital scientific-research expenditure is set off/carried forward exactly like unabsorbed depreciation.

### Sec 35ABB / 35ABA — Telecom Licence & Spectrum Fees

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

$$
\text{Annual deduction} = \frac{\text{Fee paid}}{\text{No. of relevant PYs from year of payment (or commencement) to year of expiry}}
$$

- **Concept:** Licence/spectrum fee is amortised evenly over its useful life — from the year business commences (if licence pre-paid before commencement) or from the year fee is paid (if paid after commencement), through to the year the licence/spectrum expires.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - No depreciation u/s 32 is allowed on telecom licence/spectrum — Secs 35ABB/35ABA are self-contained amortisation codes.
  - On **full sale**: Sale proceeds less un-amortised cost → loss allowed as deduction; profit up to cost taxable as PGBP; profit beyond cost is capital gain (not PGBP).
  - On **part sale**: excess of un-amortised cost over sale value is spread **evenly over the remaining licence life** as future deduction (rather than an immediate loss).
  - Sec 35ABA (spectrum) follows the same mechanics as 35ABB (licence) by cross-reference.
  - On amalgamation/demerger, remaining deduction passes to the amalgamated/resulting company exactly as it would have applied to the amalgamating/demerged company.

### Sec 35CCC/35CCD, 35D, 35DD, 35DDA, 35E — Other Specific Deductions

- **Key rule(s)/thresholds:**
  - **35CCC** — 100% deduction (excl. L&B per CBDT notification) for notified agricultural extension projects; available to **all assessees**.
  - **35CCD** — 100% deduction (excl. L&B) for notified skill development projects; available **only to companies**. Reimbursed/reimbursable expenditure is not eligible under either section.
  - **35D Preliminary expenses** (feasibility study, market survey, engineering services, MOA/AOA drafting, legal fees, share/debenture issue expenses) — allowed to a **resident assessee**, before commencement or for extension/new unit, in **5 equal annual instalments**:

$$
\text{Deduction (Indian company)} = \min\left(\text{Actual preliminary expenses},\ 5\% \text{ of } \max(\text{COP},\ \text{CE})\right)
$$

$$
\text{Deduction (other residents)} = \min\left(\text{Actual preliminary expenses},\ 5\% \text{ of COP}\right)
$$

  - COP (Cost of Project) = fixed assets invested (books value, last day of PY) for the new project/extension/unit; CE (Capital Employed) = share capital + debentures + long-term borrowings for the project (Reserves & Surplus, incl. securities premium, **excluded**).
  - **35DD** — Amalgamation/demerger expenses: only to an **Indian company**, in 5 equal instalments.
  - **35DDA** — VRS expenditure: to **all assessees**, in 5 equal instalments.
  - **35E** — Mining (coal/limestone/iron/zinc etc.) prospecting/development expenditure: incurred in the year of commercial production and the **4 years immediately preceding**, deductible over **10 years** from the year commercial production begins; restricted to PGBP of the mining business; carried-forward unabsorbed balance is allowed with next year's instalment (within the 10 years).
- **Concept:** These are staggered (instalment-based) deductions for capital-nature setup/restructuring/exit costs that would otherwise be non-deductible capital expenditure.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - On amalgamation/demerger, the remaining unclaimed instalments under 35D/35DDA pass to the amalgamated/resulting/successor entity.
  - Tax audit is compulsory in the year the 35D expenditure is incurred (except for companies/co-operative societies) — audit report by the Sec 44AB due date; details also to be furnished in **Form 3AF**, 1 month before the Sec 139(1) due date.
  - 35E audit is mandatory only for the **first year** deduction is claimed.

### Sec 35AD — Deduction for Specified Businesses

- **Key rule(s):**
  - **100% deduction on capital expenditure** (this section is **optional**) for notified "specified businesses" — cold chain facility, warehousing (agri-produce/sugar), cross-country pipeline (natural gas/petroleum), 2-star-plus hotel, 100+ bed hospital, slum/affordable housing projects, fertilizer production, container freight station/ICD, bee-keeping, semiconductor wafer fab units, new infrastructure facility, etc. (commencement dates for each vary from 01.04.2009 to 01.04.2017).
  - Excluded from deduction: **land**, **goodwill**, **financial instruments**; and cash payments >₹10,000/day to a single person (otherwise than a/c payee cheque/DD/ECS).
  - **Depreciation is not separately allowed** on assets for which Sec 35AD deduction is claimed.
  - New business (not a splitting/reconstruction of an existing one); P&M must be new — **except** imported second-hand P&M with no prior Indian depreciation claim, and up to **20% of total P&M value** may be old.
- **Concept:** Front-loads 100% capital-cost deduction to incentivise infrastructure/social-priority sectors, in lieu of normal depreciation.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - **On sale of an asset on which Sec 35AD deduction was claimed, the entire sale price is taxable as PGBP** u/s 28 (not just the profit).
  - Loss of a specified business can be set off **only against specified-business income** (of the same or another specified business), and carried forward **indefinitely** — even against a specified business not itself eligible for 35AD deduction.
  - Claiming Sec 35AD deduction bars deduction under Secs 80-IA to 80RRB and Sec 10AA.
  - Asset must be used exclusively for the specified business for a minimum of **8 years** from year of acquisition; premature diversion triggers PGBP taxation of (deduction claimed − notional depreciation that would otherwise have applied).
  - *Ceebros Hotel (P.) Ltd (2018, Mad. HC)*: deduction cannot be denied merely because star-category approval was granted in the following year — Sec 35AD is a beneficial provision, interpreted liberally.

### Sec 36 — Specific Deductions (Selected)

- **Key rule(s)/thresholds:**
  - **36(1)(i)** Insurance premium on stock-in-trade — allowed.
  - **36(1)(ib)** Health insurance premium for employees — allowed **only if paid in a mode other than cash**.
  - **36(1)(ii)** Bonus/commission to employees — allowed subject to Sec 43B; **no cap** tied to the Payment of Bonus Act limit (*Shasun Chemicals & Drugs Ltd (2016, SC)* — bonus routed through a trust before payout to employees is still allowable).
  - **36(1)(iii)** Interest on borrowed capital for business — allowed; interest on loan taken to **pay income-tax** is disallowed (personal liability); interest on loans to sister concerns for **commercial expediency** is allowed.
  - **Zero Coupon Bonds discount** — pro-rata amortised over the life of the bond in calendar months:

$$
\text{Monthly discount} = \frac{\text{Issue price} - \text{Face value... (i.e., total discount)}}{\text{Life of ZCB in calendar months}}
$$

    Rounding convention: a part-month of **15 days or more** counts as a full calendar month; less than 15 days is ignored.
  - **36(1)(iv)/(v)** Employer's contribution to SPF/RPF/Approved Superannuation Fund/Approved Gratuity Fund — allowed, subject to Sec 43B.
  - **36(1)(iva)** Employer's contribution to NPS (Sec 80CCD):

$$
\text{Deduction} = \min\left(\text{Actual contribution},\ 14\% \text{ of salary (Basic + DA, if under terms of employment)}\right)
$$

    (Enhanced from 10% to **14%**, subject to Sec 43B — Finance Act 2024 w.e.f. AY 2025-26.)
  - **36(1)(va)** Employees' contribution to PF/superannuation/ESI collected by employer — deductible **only if deposited by the due date under the respective welfare-fund Act** (e.g., PF due date = 15th of the following month); late deposit is taxable as PGBP income of the employer and **never** allowed as a deduction — this "due date" is the fund's own due date, not the Sec 139(1) ROI due date (clarified by FA 2021).
  - **36(1)(vi)** Loss of animals used in business (not stock-in-trade) = cost of animal − scrap value, on death/permanent uselessness; no Sec 32 depreciation on animals.
  - **36(1)(vii)** Bad debts — written off in the books in the PY of claim; debt must have been taken into income of the current or an earlier PY; **no need to prove the debt is actually bad** (assessee's bona fide write-off suffices, post *T.R.F. Ltd*).
  - **36(1)(viii)** Provision for bad debts of specified banks/financial institutions — a scheduled/computed percentage of income (subject to detailed limits per entity type); once claimed under (viii), no separate deduction for actual bad debts under (vii) — actual bad debts are first debited to this provision account.
  - **36(1)(ix)** Family-planning promotion expenses (employees) — **company assessees only**; revenue 100% deductible; capital in **5 equal instalments**.
  - **36(1)(xv)/(xvi)** STT/CTT — allowed only if shares/units/commodities are held as **stock-in-trade**.
  - **36(1)(viii)** [Special Reserve — long-term finance corporations]:

$$
\text{Deduction} = \min\Big(\text{Actual transfer to Special Reserve},\ 20\% \text{ of core-business PGBP},\ 200\%(\text{Share capital}+\text{General reserve}) - \text{Opening balance in reserve}\Big)
$$

  - **36(1)(xvii)** Sugarcane purchase by a co-operative sugar-manufacturing society, at price ≤ Government-fixed price — allowed.
  - **36(1)(xviii)** Mark-to-market/expected losses computed as per **ICDS** — allowed; otherwise disallowed under Sec 40A(13).
- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Balancing charge (Sec 41(2)) | On sale of a power-unit's individual (SLM) asset, profit up to original cost is taxed as PGBP |
| Sec 41(4) | Recovery of bad debts earlier allowed as deduction is taxable as PGBP in the year of recovery, even if the business has since discontinued |

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Sec 41(4) does **not** apply if the recovering assessee differs from the one who claimed the deduction (e.g., firm claims bad debt, firm dissolves, a partner personally recovers it later — not taxable u/s 41(4)).
  - *T. Veerabhadra Rao (SC)*: on succession, the successor can write off as bad debt even if the predecessor had already included the debt in income.
  - Withdrawal from the Special Reserve is taxable as PGBP u/s 41(4A).

### Sec 37(1) — General/Residual Deduction

- **Key rule(s):**
  - Deductible only if the expense: (i) is **not** covered by Secs 30–36; (ii) is incurred **wholly and exclusively** for business/profession; (iii) is **revenue** in nature; (iv) is **not personal**; (v) is **not illegal** (bribes, "hafta", secret commissions, offences under any law in India or outside, benefits/perquisites given in violation of law/rules e.g. freebies to doctors, or amounts paid to compound an offence/settle notified contravention proceedings [inserted by FA 2024 w.e.f. AY 2025-26] — all expressly disallowed by Explanations to Sec 37(1)).
  - **CSR expenditure** under Companies Act, 2013 is **not** a deductible business expense.
- **Concept:** The residual "catch-all" deduction for genuine revenue business expenditure not specifically dealt with elsewhere.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips (illustrative allowability):**
  - Political-party advertisement in souvenirs/newspapers — **not allowed** u/s 37, but an **Indian company** may claim it as a deemed donation under **Sec 80GGB** (per Companies Act, 2013, Sec 182).
  - Gifts to employees, and customary festival expenses (Diwali/New Year puja) — allowed.
  - Direct tax (tax/surcharge/cess), its interest, and **all** penalties — never allowed; GST/indirect-tax **principal and interest** allowed (subject to Sec 43B), but indirect-tax **penalty** disallowed.
  - IPO/FPO/rights-issue expenses (capital account, change in capital) — disallowed; buyback/bonus-issue/debenture and loan-raising expenses (no change in capital) — allowed as revenue.
  - Registration fee on increase of authorised share capital — **not allowed** (capital expenditure).
  - Cash embezzlement by an employee — allowed in the year of **discovery**, as incidental to business.
  - Expenditure on an abandoned project unrelated to the existing business — not allowed; on a project related to the **existing** business that is abandoned without creating an enduring asset — allowed as revenue (*Priya Village Roadshows*, *Orient Ceramics*, *Adaadyn Technologies*).
  - Retrenchment compensation: closure of the **entire** business — capital expenditure; closure of **some units** only — revenue expenditure.
  - *Bank of Rajasthan v CIT (2024, SC)*: "broken-period" interest on securities held as **stock-in-trade** (AFS/HFT category) is revenue expenditure/deductible; not so for HTM (investment) securities.
  - *Mahle Anand Filter Systems (2023, SC)*: forgoing a security deposit to settle a lease dispute retains its **capital** character — not deductible as revenue merely because paid to settle a dispute.
  - *Shanti Bhushan (2011, Del HC)*: a lawyer's heart-surgery cost is neither repair to "plant" u/s 31 nor allowable u/s 37 — no direct nexus to professional efficiency.

### Sec 40/40A — Amounts Not Deductible

- **Key rule(s)/thresholds:**
  - **40(a)(i)** — Payment to a non-resident/foreign company without TDS deduction, or TDS deducted but not deposited by the ROI due date: **100%** disallowed.
  - **40(a)(ia)** — Same default on a payment to a **resident**: **30%** disallowed (not 100%).
  - Cure: if TDS is deposited (even late) before the due date of that year's return — full deduction is allowed in the year TDS is actually paid to Government; alternatively, under the **Form 26A** CA-certificate route (payee has filed ROI, included the sum in income, and paid tax on it), the payer is deemed compliant from the date the payee files return, though interest u/s 201(1A) @ 1% p.m. still applies on the TDS shortfall period.
  - *Palam Gas Service (2017, SC)*: "payable" u/s 40(a)(ia) includes amounts **actually paid**; the disallowance applies under both mercantile and cash systems.
  - **40(a)(iii)** — Salary payable outside India / to a non-resident, without TDS or with TDS deposited late (even by a single day) — **not allowed**.
  - **40A(2)** — Payments to specified/related persons: AO may disallow the **excessive/unreasonable** portion.
  - **40A(3)** — Cash payment exceeding **₹10,000** to a single person in a single day (otherwise than by account-payee cheque/DD/ECS/other prescribed digital modes) — **entire expenditure disallowed**; limit is **₹35,000** for payments to a **transporter (goods carriage)**.
    - **40A(3A)** — expense claimed on accrual basis in an earlier year, later paid in cash exceeding the limit — deduction earlier allowed is withdrawn and taxed as PGBP in the year of such payment.
  - **40A(7)** — Provision for gratuity — **not allowed**, except contribution to an **approved gratuity fund**, or gratuity that has actually become payable during the year.
- **Definitions:**

| Assessee | "Specified persons" (relatives) under Sec 40A(2) |
|---|---|
| Individual | Spouse, Mother, Father, Brother, Sister, Lineal Ascendant, Lineal Descendant |
| HUF | Members & their relatives |
| Firm/LLP | Partners & their relatives |
| Company | Directors & their relatives |
| AOP/BOI | Members & their relatives |

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Rule 6DD exceptions to Sec 40A(3) include: payments to RBI/LIC/banks/Government; NEFT/RTGS/debit-credit card/UPI/BHIM/ECS; book-entry adjustments; payments to producers of agricultural/forest/poultry/fish/livestock produce; retirement benefits up to ₹50,000; salary to an employee posted away from normal duty station for 15+ days; areas with no banking facility; payments by/to agents for cash disbursement on the principal's behalf; authorised money-changers dealing in forex; cottage-industry (no-power) product purchases.
  - Commission agent's own cash purchases (not on behalf of principal) **are** subject to Sec 40A(3).
  - *Maruti Suzuki India Ltd (2018, Del HC)*: payment to a NR agent with no India-assessable income is not disallowable u/s 40(a)(i) merely for skipping a Sec 195(2) nil-TDS application.

### Sec 43B — Deductions Allowed Only on Actual Payment

- **Key rule(s)/thresholds:** The following are deductible **only if actually paid** by the due date of filing return u/s 139(1) (else allowed in the year of actual payment):
  - (a) any tax, duty, cess, fee; (b) employer's contribution to SPF/RPF/Approved Gratuity Fund/Approved Superannuation Fund/NPS/any statutory welfare fund; (c) bonus/commission to employees; (d) interest on loans from specified financial institutions/scheduled banks/State Financial/Industrial Investment Corporations; (e) leave encashment to employees; (f) sums payable to Indian Railways for use of railway assets; (g) interest on loans/borrowings from CG-notified NBFC classes.
  - **(h) [inserted by FA 2023, w.e.f. AY 2024-25]** — any sum payable to a **Micro or Small enterprise** beyond the time limit under **Sec 15 of the MSMED Act, 2006**: deductible **only** if paid within that time limit; otherwise allowed **only in the year of actual payment** (irrespective of the Sec 139(1) due date — note this clause has **no** "before the return due date" saving unlike (a)–(g)).
- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Sec 15, MSMED Act, 2006 time limit | Agreed date in writing (max **45 days** from acceptance of goods/services); if no written agreement, **15 days** from acceptance/deemed acceptance |
| Micro enterprise | Investment in P&M/equipment up to ₹2.5 crore **and** turnover up to ₹10 crore |
| Small enterprise | Investment in P&M/equipment up to ₹25 crore **and** turnover up to ₹100 crore |

- **Concept:** Sec 43B converts these otherwise accrual-based deductions into a payment-basis regime to curb deferral of statutory dues and MSME payment delays.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Converting unpaid interest into a fresh loan/debenture/other instrument is **not** treated as "actual payment" — deduction follows actual repayment of the new instrument.
  - Clause (h) applies only to goods/services from **manufacturer/service-provider micro-small enterprises** registered under MSMED (not traders); interest on delayed MSME payment is itself never deductible.

### Sec 41 — Deemed Income (Recoupment Provisions)

- **Key rule(s):**
  - **41(1) Recovery/remission of trading liability:** if a deduction (expenditure/loss/trading liability) was allowed in an earlier year, and in the current year the assessee **recovers, or the liability is remitted/ceases** (incl. unilateral write-off without creditor's consent), the recovered/remitted amount is taxable as PGBP — even if that business has since been discontinued.
  - A **time-barred** liability is taxable u/s 41(1) only if the assessee **chooses to write it off**; if not written off, Sec 41(1) does not apply.
  - **41(2) Balancing charge:** on sale of a power-unit's (SLM/individual-asset) asset, sale value in excess of WDV, up to original cost, is taxed as PGBP.
  - **41(4) Bad-debt recovery:** subsequent recovery of a bad debt earlier allowed as deduction is taxed as PGBP in the year of recovery, even if the business is discontinued — but **only** if the person who recovers is the **same** assessee who claimed the deduction.
- **Concept:** Sec 41 recaptures into PGBP any benefit that reverses an earlier allowed deduction, ensuring the deduction/income match is not permanently lost.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Firm claims bad debt → firm dissolves → a partner personally recovers the amount → **not** taxable u/s 41(4) (different assessee).

### Sec 43CB, 43C, 43D, 43A, 43AA — Other Special Computation Provisions

- **Key rule(s):**
  - **43CB** (with ICDS III/IV): construction contracts follow **Percentage of Completion Method (POCM)**; service contracts follow **Project Completion Method** if duration ≤ **90 days**, **Straight Line Method** if an indeterminate number of acts occur over a specified period, else **POCM**. Contract revenue includes retention money; contract cost is **not** reduced by incidental interest/dividend/capital-gain income.
  - **43C**: where a capital asset is converted to stock-in-trade under amalgamation/gift/HUF-partition/will/irrevocable trust, cost of the stock = cost to previous owner + cost of improvement by transferor & transferee + transfer expenses of the transferor.
  - **43D**: for scheduled banks/PFIs/State Financial/Industrial Investment Corporations/NBFCs, interest on RBI-prescribed NPA categories is taxable only when **credited to P&L or actually received, whichever is earlier**.
  - **43A**: forex gain/loss on repayment of a loan/supplier's credit taken to acquire a foreign asset is adjusted against the **block of assets**, only at the time of **actual payment** (gain reduces block; loss increases it); gain/loss on a related hedging contract is treated similarly.
  - **43AA**: forex fluctuation gain/loss (per ICDS) on monetary/non-monetary items, financial-statement translation of foreign operations, forward contracts, and translation reserves is recognised as PGBP income/loss.
- **Concept:** These sections align tax computation of long-duration contracts and forex exposure with prescribed ICDS methodology.

### Sec 44AA / 44AB — Compulsory Books of Account & Tax Audit

- **Key rule(s)/thresholds — Sec 44AA:**
  - **Specified professions** (medical, engineering, legal, accountancy, technical consultancy, IT, architecture, interior decoration, company secretary, authorised representative, film artists): must maintain prescribed books (Rule 6F) if gross receipts exceed **₹1,50,000** in each of the preceding 3 years (or likely to exceed, if newly set up).
  - **Other businesses:** must maintain books if PGBP income > **₹1,20,000** or turnover/gross receipts > **₹10,00,000** in any of the preceding 3 years — for **Individuals/HUF**, the limits are **₹2,50,000** (income) and **₹25,00,000** (turnover/gross receipts).
  - Special cases: assessee declaring lower income than u/s 44AD/44ADA (with NTI > basic exemption), or lower income u/s 44AE/44BB/44BBB.
  - Books must be retained for **6 years** from the end of the relevant AY; failure attracts penalty of **₹25,000** u/s 271A.
- **Key rule(s)/thresholds — Sec 44AB (Tax Audit):**
  - **Business:** turnover/gross receipts > **₹1 crore** (raised to **₹10 crore** if cash receipts and cash payments **each** do not exceed 5% of total receipts/payments — non-account-payee cheque/DD counts as cash).
  - **Specified profession:** gross receipts > **₹50 lakh**.
  - Not applicable to a person declaring income u/s 44AD/44ADA, or deriving income under Sec 44B (shipping) / 44BBA (aircraft).
  - Audit report (Form 3CA/3CB with 3CD) must be furnished **1 month before** the Sec 139(1) due date.
  - **Penalty u/s 271B** for failure: lower of **0.5% of turnover/gross receipts** or **₹1,50,000**.
- **Concept:** These thresholds decide whether an assessee must keep formal accounts and get them audited before claiming deductions computed on an actual basis.

### Sec 44AD / 44ADA — Presumptive Taxation for Residents (Business/Profession)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s) — Sec 44AD:**

$$
\text{Presumptive PGBP} = \text{Turnover/Gross receipts} \times 8\%\ \big(\text{or } 6\%\text{ for receipts via account-payee cheque/DD/ECS/digital modes up to the ROI due date}\big)
$$

  - Eligible assessee: **Resident** Individual/HUF/Firm (**excluding LLP**), not claiming deduction u/s 10AA or 80-IA to 80RRB.
  - Applies to any business (except Sec 44AE goods-carriage business, agency business, commission/brokerage business) with turnover up to **₹2 crore** — raised to **₹3 crore** if cash receipts do not exceed **5%** of total turnover/gross receipts of the year (non-account-payee instruments = cash) [FA 2023, w.e.f. AY 2024-25].
  - If declared income is not per Sec 44AD in a year (after having opted in), the assessee loses eligibility for the **next 5 consecutive AYs**; if in that period NTI exceeds the basic exemption limit, books must be maintained and audited.
  - 100% advance tax may be paid in a single instalment by **15th March** of the PY.
- **Key formula(s)/rule(s) — Sec 44ADA:**

$$
\text{Presumptive PGBP} = \text{Gross receipts} \times 50\%
$$

  - Eligible assessee: **Resident** Individual or resident firm (**excluding LLP**) in a Sec 44AA-specified profession, with gross receipts up to **₹50 lakh** — raised to **₹75 lakh** if cash receipts do not exceed **5%** of gross receipts of the year [FA 2023, w.e.f. AY 2024-25].
- **Concept:** Both sections let small resident businesses/professionals declare a flat presumptive percentage of turnover/receipts as taxable income, dispensing with detailed books and audit.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Under both sections, **deductions under Secs 30–38 are deemed already allowed** (cannot claim separately); notional depreciation must still be tracked to compute WDV for the next year.
  - Partners' remuneration/interest u/s 40(b) are **not** further deductible from the presumptive income (44AD); but for **44AE**, partner's remuneration/interest **is** separately deductible.
  - Declaring income **below** the presumptive rate, with NTI exceeding the basic exemption limit, mandates books (Sec 44AA) and audit (Sec 44AB).

### Sec 44AE — Presumptive Taxation for Goods-Carriage Transporters

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

$$
\text{Heavy goods vehicle: PGBP} = ₹1{,}000 \times \text{gross vehicle weight (in tons, or unladen weight)} \times \text{No. of months (or part) owned}
$$

$$
\text{Other vehicle: PGBP} = ₹7{,}500 \times \text{No. of months (or part) owned}
$$

- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Heavy goods vehicle | Goods carriage with Gross Vehicle Weight exceeding **12,000 kg (12 tons)** |

- **Concept:** Applies if the assessee owns **not more than 10** goods carriages at any time in the year (owning more than 10 at any time takes the assessee outside Sec 44AE entirely); income is computed even if a vehicle is idle, so long as owned.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Higher income may voluntarily be declared and will then be accepted as the assessee's income.
  - Unlike 44AD/44ADA, partners' remuneration/interest u/s 40(b) **is** deductible from Sec 44AE presumptive income.
  - CBDT clarification: use **Gross Vehicle Weight (GVW)**; if unavailable, use unladen weight.
  - Declaring lower income mandatorily triggers books (44AA) and audit (44AB).

### Presumptive Taxation for Non-Residents — Sec 44B / 44BBA / 44BB / 44BBB / 44BBC / 44BBD

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

| Section | Business | Assessee | Presumptive rate |
|---|---|---|---|
| 44B | Shipping (other than cruise ships) | Non-resident | **7.5%** of specified sum |
| 44BBA | Operation of aircraft | Non-resident | **5%** of specified sum |
| 44BB | Services/facilities/plant hire for prospecting/extraction/production of mineral oil | Non-resident | **10%** of specified sum |
| 44BBB | Civil construction/erection/testing/commissioning of turnkey power projects (CG-approved) | Foreign company only | **10%** of specified sum |
| 44BBC [FA 2024, w.e.f. AY 2025-26] | Operation of cruise ships (conditions per Notification 09/2025) | Non-resident | **20%** of specified sum |
| 44BBD [FA 2025, w.e.f. AY 2026-27] | Providing services/technology for setting up electronics-manufacturing facilities in India | Non-resident | **25%** of specified sum |

- **Concept:** "Specified sum" = amounts paid/payable in India + amounts received/deemed received in India, for the respective activity (carriage of passengers/cargo, services, or construction).
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Lower actual profits may be claimed only under **44BB/44BBB** (with mandatory books u/s 44AA and audit u/s 44AB) — not under 44B, 44BBA, 44BBC, or 44BBD.
  - Set-off of brought-forward losses/unabsorbed depreciation is **allowed** under 44B/44BBA/44BBC, but **disallowed** if income is declared per 44BB/44BBB on a presumptive basis, and **not allowed at all** under 44BBD.
  - Notification 09/2025 conditions for 44BBC: ship capacity > 200 passengers or length ≥ 75 m, for leisure/recreation, scheduled voyage touching ≥ 2 Indian sea ports (or same port twice), primarily passenger-carrying (not cargo), per Tourism/Shipping Ministry guidelines.

### Sec 44C / 44DA — Foreign Company Branch & NR Royalty/FTS Taxation

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s) — Sec 44C (Head Office expenses of a foreign company's Indian branch):**

$$
\text{HO expense deduction} = \min\left(5\% \text{ of Adjusted Total Income (ATI)},\ \text{Actual HO expenses attributable to Indian business/profession}\right)
$$

  - ATI = total income before giving effect to brought-forward depreciation, brought-forward family-planning expenditure, brought-forward losses, and Chapter VI-A deductions; if ATI computes as a loss, the **average ATI of the preceding 3 years** is used instead.
- **Key rule(s) — Sec 44DA (Royalty/FTS of a non-resident/foreign company through a PE):**
  - Applies where royalty/FTS income arises under an agreement entered **after 31.03.2003**, business is carried on through a **Permanent Establishment** in India (or profession from a **Fixed Place of Profession**), and the underlying right/property/contract is **effectively connected** with that PE.
  - Disallowed: expenditure not wholly/exclusively for the PE's business in India; and any amount paid by the PE to its Head Office (other than reimbursement of actual expenses).
- **Concept:** These provisions govern how much expense a foreign company's Indian branch/PE may claim against India-sourced income.

### Sec 44A — Trade/Professional Association (Principle of Mutuality)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

$$
\text{Deficiency} = \text{Subscription/other receipts from members (excl. specific-service receipts)} - \text{Expenditure for protection/advancement of members' common interest}
$$

$$
\text{Deduction for deficiency (Sec 44A)} \le 50\% \text{ of Total Income (before this deduction)}
$$

- **Definitions:**

| Receipt type | Tax treatment |
|---|---|
| General service to members (subscription) | Exempt (mutuality); loss allowed as "deficiency" u/s 44A — an exception to mutuality |
| Specific service to members | Taxable as PGBP u/s 28(iii); loss allowed |
| Other receipts | Taxable under IFOS |

- **Concept:** Sec 44A grants a deduction for the "deficiency" of a mutual trade/professional association even though its normal member-subscription income is otherwise exempt under mutuality.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Applies only to associations **not** exempt u/s 10(23A), and only if they do **not distribute income** among members (except grants to affiliated bodies).
  - Brought-forward allowances/losses are set off **first**, before computing the Sec 44A deficiency deduction; in the absence/inadequacy of PGBP income, the deficiency deduction may be claimed from other heads.

### References

1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sections 28 to 44DB (charging section, computation, deductions, disallowances, presumptive taxation), as amended by the Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024 and Finance Act, 2025 — incometaxindia.gov.in.
2. Depreciation rates (Appendix I, Income-tax Rules, 1962) for AY 2026-27 — ClearTax, "Depreciation Rates for FY 2025-26 Under Income Tax Act" (cleartax.in/s/depreciation-income-tax-act) and TaxHeal, "Depreciation as per Income-tax Act AY 2026-27" (taxheal.com).
3. Presumptive taxation Secs 44AD/44ADA turnover/receipt thresholds and rates (₹2cr/₹3cr @ 8%/6%; ₹50L/₹75L @ 50%) — ClearTax, "Section 44AD – Presumptive Scheme for Businesses" (cleartax.in/s/section-44ad-presumptive-scheme); as amended by Finance Act 2023 w.e.f. AY 2024-25.
4. Sec 43B(h) MSME 45-day/15-day payment rule (Finance Act 2023, w.e.f. AY 2024-25) and MSMED Act, 2006, Sec 15 timelines — IndiaFilings, "MSME 45 Days Payment Rule: Section 43B(h) Compliance" (indiafilings.com).
5. Sec 36(1)(iva) employer's NPS contribution cap raised from 10% to 14% of salary — Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024, w.e.f. AY 2025-26 — TaxGuru, "Increased Employer Pension Contribution Deduction under Section 36 & 80CCD" (taxguru.in).
6. ICAI, Final Course Study Material — Direct Tax Laws & International Taxation, Chapter on "Profits and Gains of Business or Profession", for current syllabus (May/Nov 2026 attempts).

## 05. Income Computation & Disclosure Standards (ICDS)

> **Where it fits:** The tax-law bridge between book income (computed per AS/Ind-AS) and taxable income under "Profits & Gains of Business or Profession" (PGBP) and "Income from Other Sources" (IFOS) — 10 standards notified u/s 145(2), tested heavily as adjustment-based numericals.

### Sec. 145(1)/(2) — Method of Accounting & Applicability of ICDS

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - Sec. 145(1): Income under PGBP/IFOS shall be computed as per the **cash or mercantile system of accounting** regularly employed by the assessee.
  - Sec. 145(2): CG has notified **10 ICDS**, applicable from **AY 2017-18** onwards, to be followed by **all assessees (other than an individual or HUF not required to get accounts audited u/s 44AB)** following the **mercantile system**, for computing income under PGBP/IFOS.
  - **Conflict rule:** where ICDS conflicts with the Income-tax Act, 1961/Rules, the **Act/Rules shall prevail**.
  - Applies to **presumptive taxation** schemes too (44AD, 44ADA, 44AE, 44BB, 44BBB etc.) — e.g., ICDS-III/IV govern how "turnover/receipts" is determined even for presumptive assessees.
  - Applies **irrespective of AS or Ind-AS** followed for books.
  - **MAT (Sec. 115JB):** computed on book profit (net profit per P&L as per Companies Act, adjusted) → **ICDS does NOT apply**.
  - **AMT (Sec. 115JC):** computed on adjusted total income derived from regular total income → **ICDS DOES apply**.
  - Applies to gross-basis taxation of non-residents too (Royalty/FTS/Interest taxable u/s 115A on gross basis).
  - **Disclosure:** net effect of ICDS on income to be disclosed in the Return of Income; detailed disclosures required in **tax audit report Form 3CD**; no separate disclosure requirement for assessees not liable to tax audit.
- **Concept:** ICDS standardises *when and how much* income/expense is recognised for tax purposes, independent of the accounting policy chosen for statutory books.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Classic trap: MAT → book profit → no ICDS; AMT → adjusted total income → ICDS applies. Do not mix these up.
  - ICDS never overrides a specific section of the Act/Rules — always check the Act first.
- **Definitions:**

| ICDS | Subject |
|---|---|
| I | Accounting Policies |
| II | Valuation of Inventories |
| III | Construction Contracts |
| IV | Revenue Recognition |
| V | Tangible Fixed Assets |
| VI | Effects of Changes in Foreign Exchange Rates |
| VII | Government Grants |
| VIII | Securities |
| IX | Borrowing Costs |
| X | Provisions, Contingent Liabilities & Contingent Assets |

### ICDS-I: Accounting Policies

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - Recognises fundamental assumptions: **Going Concern, Consistency, Accrual**. Does **NOT** recognise **Prudence** or **Materiality**.
  - Treatment/presentation of transactions shall be governed by their **substance over legal form**.
  - MTM loss / expected loss is **not to be recognised** unless permitted by some other ICDS (and, per CBDT clarification, this principle applies **mutatis mutandis to MTM gains/expected profits** too).
  - Change in accounting policy permitted only for a **"reasonable cause"** (an existing, evolved concept under the Act).
  - **Disclosure:** all significant accounting policies, any change therein, and any fundamental assumption not followed must be disclosed.
- **Concept:** Sets the baseline philosophy — no conservatism bias (prudence/materiality dropped) so that neither losses nor gains are selectively deferred.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Because "prudence" is dropped, an anticipated loss cannot be booked merely on grounds of conservatism unless another ICDS specifically sanctions it.
  - ICDS-I principles apply only for computing income under PGBP/IFOS, not for maintenance of books.

### ICDS-II: Valuation of Inventories

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
$$
NRV = \text{Estimated Selling Price} - \left(\text{Estimated Cost of Completion} + \text{Estimated Cost Necessary to Make the Sale}\right)
$$
  - Inventories valued at **lower of Cost or NRV**.
  - On **dissolution of a firm/AOP/BOI** (whether business continued or not), inventories valued at **NRV** on the date of dissolution.
  - Cost formula: **FIFO**, **Weighted Average Cost**, or **Standard Cost** method (Retail Method allowed only where impracticable to use others, typically retail trade).
  - **Raw material**: valued at **cost only**, not NRV — *unless* the finished goods into which it will convert are expected to sell below cost, in which case RM is valued at NRV (= its **replacement cost**).
  - Sec. 145A valuation of securities (not covered by ICDS-VIII, e.g. for banks/PFI purposes):

| Security type | Valuation |
|---|---|
| Normally | Lower of actual cost or NRV |
| Unlisted, or listed but not regularly quoted | Actual cost initially recognised |
| Listed & regularly quoted | Lower of actual cost or NRV |
| Held by scheduled bank / PFI | As per ICDS after considering RBI guidelines |

  - Sec. 145A also mandates that value of purchase/sale of goods/services and inventory **includes any tax, duty, cess or fee** actually paid/incurred to bring the goods/services to their location & condition.
  - **Not covered by ICDS-II:** WIP under construction contracts (ICDS-III), shares/securities held as SIT (ICDS-VIII), producers' inventories of livestock/agriculture/forest products/mineral oils/ores/gases measured at NRV, machinery spares covered under ICDS-V.
- **Concept:** Standard lower-of-cost-or-NRV valuation, but tax law overlays Sec. 145A for tax-inclusive costing and category-specific security valuation.
- **Cost of inventories includes:**

| Component | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Purchase cost | Purchase price + duties/taxes + freight inwards + other direct purchase costs − trade discounts/rebates |
| Service cost | Labour & personnel costs directly engaged in providing the service |
| Conversion cost | Costs directly related to units of production incl. allocated fixed overhead converting RM→FG; joint products allocated rationally; by-product/scrap/waste NRV deducted from main product cost |
| Other cost | Interest/borrowing cost, only if permitted under ICDS-IX |

- **Cost of inventories excludes:** abnormal wastage of material/labour/production costs; storage costs (unless necessary before a further production stage); administrative overheads not bringing inventory to present location/condition; selling costs.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Category-wise (not item-wise) cost-vs-NRV comparison is a recurring theme across ICDS-II/VIII — do not compare security-by-security.
  - RM "replacement cost" trigger is a favourite trick question — RM stays at cost unless the FG will sell below cost.

### ICDS-III: Construction Contracts

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - Contract revenue and costs recognised on **Percentage of Completion Method (POCM)**.
  - Where the outcome cannot be reliably estimated in the **early stages**, revenue is recognised only to the extent of costs incurred; "early stage" **shall not extend beyond 25% of the stage of completion**.
  - **Sec. 145B:** escalation claims in a contract, or export incentives, are deemed income of the **P.Y. in which reasonable certainty of realisation is achieved** (not necessarily the year of accrual per the original contract terms).
  - **Disclosure:** amount of contract revenue recognised as revenue in the period, methods used to determine stage of completion of contracts in progress, etc.
- **Concept:** Aligns tax recognition of long-duration contracts with the economic progress of the contract rather than final completion, while capping the "wait-and-watch" window at 25% completion.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - The **25%** early-stage ceiling is a specific numeric threshold frequently tested — memorise it exactly.
  - Sec. 145B (escalation/export incentive) is a cross-reference — don't confuse with Sec. 43CB (service/construction contract computation method).

### ICDS-IV: Revenue Recognition

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):** Recognition criteria by transaction type:

| Transaction | Recognition rule |
|---|---|
| Sale of goods | Significant risks & rewards of ownership transferred AND reasonable certainty of ultimate collection |
| Service transactions | Percentage Completion Method / Straight Line Method / Project Completion Method — governed by **Sec. 43CB** |
| Interest | Accrues on a **time basis** |
| Interest on refund of tax/duty/cess | Recognised in the P.Y. in which such interest is **received** |
| Royalties | Accrue as per terms of the relevant agreement, unless another systematic & rational basis is more appropriate |
| Dividend | Recognised as per Sec. 8 of the Act |

  - **CBDT clarification:** interest (time basis) and royalty (contractual terms) **must be recognised even without reasonable certainty of subsequent collection**; any later non-recovery is claimable as a bad debt deduction u/s 36(1)(vii).
  - **Disclosure:** amount of revenue from service transactions recognised during the P.Y., method used to determine stage of completion, details of service transactions in progress at year-end, etc.
- **Concept:** Codifies when revenue "arises" for tax purposes across the four common ordinary-activity revenue streams (goods, services, use-of-resources income, and passive income).
- **Worked example (interest accrued-but-not-received, carried into a later capital gains computation):** interest of ₹1,000 accrues each 6 months (Dec/June); ₹500 accrued for 3 months to 31/03 is taxed as interest income on accrual basis even though received only on 30/06, after the security is sold on 30/04. On sale:
$$
\text{Capital Gains} = \text{Full Value of Consideration} - \text{Cost of Acquisition} - \text{Interest already taxed on accrual basis}
$$
  giving, on the illustrative figures, FVC ₹12,000 − COA ₹10,000 = ₹2,000, less interest already taxed ₹500 = **CG ₹1,500**. This confirms that interest already offered to tax on accrual basis (but not yet received) is deducted while computing capital gains on the sale of the interest-bearing security.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Interest/royalty accrual is **not conditional on collectability** — a frequently misapplied "prudence" instinct that ICDS-IV expressly rejects.
  - Interest on tax refund is an exception: taxed only on **receipt**, not accrual.

### ICDS-V: Tangible Fixed Assets

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
$$
\text{Actual Cost} = \text{Purchase Price} + \text{Duties/Taxes (non-recoverable)} + \text{Directly Attributable Expenditure} - \text{Trade Discounts/Rebates}
$$
  - **Machine spares:** normally charged to revenue as consumed; **capitalised** only if usable solely in connection with a tangible fixed asset (TFA) and expected use is **irregular**. Stand-by/servicing equipment is always capitalised.
  - Admin/general overheads not relating to a specific TFA are **excluded** from cost; expenses specifically attributable to construction/acquisition/bringing the TFA to working condition are **included**.
  - Start-up & commissioning expenses (incl. test runs, experimental production) → **capitalised**. Expenses after **commercial production begins** → **revenue expenditure**. Expenses between test-run/experimental production and commencement of commercial production → **capital expenditure**.
  - Where a TFA is acquired in **exchange for another asset/shares/securities**, its actual cost = **FMV of the asset so acquired**.
  - **Disclosure:** description of asset/block, rate of depreciation, actual cost/WDV, additions/deductions with dates, depreciation allowable, closing WDV.
- **Concept:** Fixes what enters the "actual cost" (and hence the depreciation base) of tangible fixed assets for tax purposes, with special rules for spares and start-up costs.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - The commercial-production cut-off (test run → capital; post-commercial-production → revenue) is a classic MCQ/numerical trap.

### ICDS-VI: Effects of Changes in Foreign Exchange Rates

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Initial recognition** of a foreign currency transaction: **actual rate at transaction date**, OR a weekly/monthly average rate approximating the actual rate (not usable if exchange rates fluctuate significantly).
