3. CBDT Circulars/Notifications — Circular 9/2012 (gas transportation, Sec 194C), Circular 21/2017 (PSF, Sec 194-I), CBDT guidelines on Sec 194R, 194-O and 194Q (issued under respective introducing Finance Acts), and Notification 05/2017 (interest income of minor child, Sec 194A).
4. Key Supreme Court/High Court rulings referenced: CIT v. Dr. Prannoy Roy (Sec 234A), ITC Ltd. (2016) (tips not salary), Kotak Securities Ltd. (2016), Bharti Cellular Ltd. (2024), Air India Ltd. (2023) (Sec 206AA vs DTAA), Pioneer Overseas Corporation (2022), BDR Finvest Pvt. Ltd. (2024).
5. ICAI Final Direct Tax & International Taxation Study Material — chapter on Advance Tax, TDS & TCS, for structure and cross-referencing of provisions (used to corroborate section numbering and current-syllabus applicability; no live web verification available in this session — figures reconstructed from established statutory knowledge and flagged with ⚠️ VERIFY where residual doubt exists).

## 12. Assessment Procedure

> **Where it fits:** This chapter is the "procedural spine" of Direct Tax — how a Return of Income is filed, verified and processed (Sec 139–140A), who the Income-tax authorities are and what powers they wield (Sec 116–135), search & seizure (Sec 132–132B), the assessment/reassessment machinery (Sec 142–158BFA), and the time limits that cap each stage. Almost every other chapter's numbers eventually flow into a return governed by these sections.

### Filing of Return of Income — Normal Return (Sec 139(1))

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Company & Partnership Firm (incl. LLP):** return filing is **compulsory** regardless of income/loss.
  - **Other assessees:** compulsory if **Gross Total Income (before claiming deductions/exemption u/s 54, 54B, 54D, 54EC, 54F, 54G, 54GA)** exceeds the **basic exemption limit**.
  - **Resident individuals** (Resident & Ordinarily Resident, and Resident but Not Ordinarily Resident) holding foreign assets, or being a beneficial owner/beneficiary of a foreign asset, or having signing authority in a foreign account — return filing compulsory even if income is below basic exemption.
  - **Any person (other than company/firm)** not otherwise covered, must file a return if, during the PY, any one of the following (7th proviso to Sec 139(1)) is triggered:

$$
\begin{aligned}
&\text{Current a/c deposits (one or more banks)} > ₹1\text{ crore}\\
&\text{OR Savings a/c deposits (one or more banks)} \ge ₹50\text{ lakh}\\
&\text{OR Foreign travel expenditure (self or others)} > ₹2\text{ lakh}\\
&\text{OR Electricity consumption expenditure} > ₹1\text{ lakh}\\
&\text{OR Business turnover/sales/gross receipts} > ₹60\text{ lakh}\\
&\text{OR Professional gross receipts} > ₹10\text{ lakh}\\
&\text{OR Aggregate TDS + TCS} \ge ₹25{,}000\ (\text{₹}50{,}000\text{ for a senior citizen})
\end{aligned}
$$

- **Concept:** Sec 139(1) fixes *who* must file a return even without any notice from the Department; the 7th-proviso high-value-transaction triggers (added by FA 2019 & widened by FA 2022) exist to pull high-spenders into the filing net even if their taxable income is below the basic exemption limit.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - GTI test uses GTI **before** the specified capital-gains exemptions (54/54B/54D/54EC/54F/54G/54GA) — a common trap is to apply GTI after exemption.
  - The turnover/receipts (₹60 lakh/₹10 lakh) and TDS/TCS (₹25,000/₹50,000) triggers apply only to "**other person**" cases (not company/firm, who must file anyway).

**Definitions**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Beneficial Owner | Individual providing consideration for an asset, directly/indirectly, for his own or another's immediate/future benefit |
| Beneficiary | Individual deriving benefit from an asset whose consideration was provided by someone else |

### Due Dates & Sec 139(1C) Exemption from Filing

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s) — Due dates of ROI (AY 2026-27):**

| Assessee | Due Date |
|---|---|
| Person required to furnish Transfer Pricing report u/s 92E (incl. partners of such firm, or spouse under Sec 5A) | 30th Nov of AY |
| Company (other than TP cases) | 31st Oct of AY |
| Person whose accounts are required to be audited under any law | 31st Oct of AY |
| Partner of a firm whose accounts require audit (or spouse under Sec 5A) | 31st Oct of AY |
| Any other person | 31st July of AY |

  - **Sec 5A:** for an individual governed by the Portuguese Civil Code, 1860 (Goa, Dadra & Nagar Haveli, Daman & Diu), income (other than **Salary**) is equally split between husband and wife.
  - **Sec 139(1C):** Central Government may, by notification, exempt classes of persons from filing ROI — e.g., a NR/foreign company earning only IFSC investment-fund income with TDS deducted u/s 194LBB; NR/foreign company earning only specified-fund income u/s 10(4D); NR "eligible foreign investor" earning only capital gains exempt u/s 47(viab) on IFSC-listed securities in foreign currency. Exemption is **withdrawn** once a notice u/s 142(1) or 148 is issued.
- **Concept:** Due dates stagger based on audit complexity (TP audit cases latest, then audit/company cases, then everyone else).
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** A partner's own due date rides on the **firm's** audit-requirement, not the partner's personal turnover.

### Loss Return, Belated Return & Revised Return (Sec 139(3), (4), (5))

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Sec 139(3) — Loss return:** to carry forward the following losses, ROI must be filed **within the Sec 139(1) due date**: business loss (72(1)), speculation business loss (73(2)), specified-business loss (73A(2)), capital gains loss (74(1)), loss from owning/maintaining race horses (74A(3)).
  - House property loss and unabsorbed depreciation can be carried forward **even if the return is filed late**.
  - **Sec 139(4) — Belated return:** if the Sec 139(1) due date is missed, return can be filed up to:

$$
\text{Belated Return Deadline} = \min\Big(\text{3 months before end of relevant AY},\ \text{Date of completion of assessment}\Big)
$$

  for AY 2026-27, "3 months before end of AY" = **31st December 2026**.
  - **Sec 139(5) — Revised return:** any return filed u/s 139(1)/139(3)/139(4) can be revised on discovery of an omission/wrong statement, within the **same time limit** as the belated return (3 months before end of AY, or completion of assessment, whichever earlier).
  - **Condonation of delay for loss carry-forward (CBDT Circular 11/2024, w.e.f. 1/10/2024):**

| Authority | Monetary limit of claim |
|---|---|
| CIT/PCIT | Up to ₹1 crore |
| CCIT | > ₹1 crore up to ₹3 crore |
| PCCIT | > ₹3 crore |

  Condonation application must be made within **5 years** from end of relevant AY; the authority must dispose it within **6 months** from end of the month of receipt.
- **Concept:** Sec 80 conditions the loss-carry-forward benefit on timely filing **only in the year the loss is incurred**, not in the year it is set off; a belated return still gets this benefit denied unless condoned.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Belated return u/s 139(4) **can** be revised u/s 139(5) — a frequent MCQ trap assumes it cannot.
  - Revised return **substitutes** the original from the date the original was filed and can be revised **any number of times** within the time limit.
  - Return can be revised even after receiving intimation/refund u/s 143(1), since that intimation is not "completion of assessment" — *Kailashben Mardia*-type logic is echoed by *Orissa Rural Housing Development Corpn. Ltd. (2012, Orissa HC)*: assessee cannot substitute a "revised statement of income" for a proper Sec 139(5) revised return.
  - *Govind Nagar Sugar Ltd. (2011, Delhi HC):* unabsorbed depreciation can be carried forward even where the current year's return was filed beyond the Sec 139(1) due date.

### Consequences of Belated Return & Returns of Special Persons (Sec 139(4A)–(4F), 139(6)/(9))

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s) — Consequences of a belated return u/s 139(4):**
  - No carry forward of the specified losses under Sec 80 (see above).
  - No deduction under Chapter VI-A "C — Deductions in respect of certain incomes" (80-IA to 80RRB) and no deduction u/s 10AA — per Sec 80AC.
  - Interest u/s 234A @ **1% per month or part of the month**.
  - Late filing fee u/s 234F — **₹5,000** (₹1,000 if total income ≤ ₹5 lakh).
  - Interest on refund u/s 244A runs **from the date of filing the return**, not from 1st April of the AY.
  - **Sec 139(4A) — Trust:** return compulsory if total income (before exemption u/s 11 & 12) exceeds basic exemption; late filing also attracts penalty of **₹500/day** u/s 272A (in addition to Sec 234F fee).
  - **Sec 139(4B) — Political party:** return compulsory if total income (before exemption u/s 13A) exceeds basic exemption.
  - **Sec 139(4C) — Certain institutions** (hospitals, medical institutions, infrastructure debt funds, mutual funds, securitisation trusts, venture capital companies/funds, research associations, news agencies, trade unions, investor protection funds, employee welfare funds, core settlement guarantee funds): return compulsory if total income (before exemption u/s 10) exceeds basic exemption; same ₹500/day penalty u/s 272A for late filing.
  - **Sec 139(4D)/(4E)/(4F):** mandatory filing for colleges/universities/institutions approved u/s 35, Business Trusts (REIT/InvIT), and Investment Funds (AIF Category I & II) respectively.
  - **Sec 139(6)/(6A):** ITR form may require disclosure of exempt income, specified assets/value, bank & credit card details, specified expenditure — and, for business/profession assessees, the Tax Audit Report u/s 44AB, location/style of principal place & branches, and partner/member details.
  - **Sec 139(9) — Defective return:** return is defective if not filed in the prescribed form, tax proof not attached, or the 44AB report not submitted; AO must intimate the defect and allow **15 days** (or extended time) to rectify — failing which the return is treated as **invalid (void ab initio)**.
- **Concept:** Sec 139(4A)-(4F) extend compulsory filing to entities that are otherwise exempt-income vehicles, closing the loophole of "no tax, hence no filing."
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** The ₹5,000/₹1,000 late fee slab under 234F is a favourite numeric trap — the ₹1,000 slab applies only when total income does **not exceed ₹5 lakh**.

### PAN — Sec 139A, 272B

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s) — Who must apply for PAN & by when:**

| Person | Time limit |
|---|---|
| Total income (own or of another assessable person) > basic exemption | By **31st May** of the AY |
| Business/profession with turnover/gross receipts likely to exceed **₹5 lakh** in a PY | By end of the PY |
| Trust required to file return u/s 139(4A) | By end of the PY |
| Resident (non-individual) entering a financial transaction aggregating **₹2,50,000 or more** in a FY | By 31st May of the AY |
| MD/director/partner/trustee/author/founder/karta/CEO/principal officer/office bearer of the above | By 31st May of the AY |
| Person intending cash deposit/withdrawal aggregating **₹20 lakh or more** in a FY (one or more bank/co-op bank accounts), or opening a current/cash-credit account | At least **7 days** before the transaction |

  - **PAN mandatorily quoted** in specified transactions (illustrative, all monetary thresholds per Rule 114B): motor vehicle sale/purchase (other than two-wheeler) — all transactions; opening a bank account (other than a Basic Savings Bank Deposit Account) — all transactions; credit/debit card application — all transactions; D-Mat account opening — all transactions; hotel/restaurant cash bill > ₹50,000; foreign travel/forex cash payment > ₹50,000; mutual fund unit purchase > ₹50,000; debenture/bond purchase > ₹50,000; RBI bond purchase > ₹50,000; bank cash deposit > ₹50,000/day; bank draft/pay order cash purchase > ₹50,000/day; fixed deposit > ₹50,000, or aggregating > ₹5 lakh in a FY; prepaid instrument payment > ₹50,000; life insurance premium > ₹50,000 in a FY; sale/purchase of securities (other than shares) or unlisted shares > ₹1 lakh per transaction; immovable property sale/purchase where amount or stamp duty value > ₹10 lakh; sale/purchase of goods/services (other) > ₹2 lakh per transaction.
  - **Not required to obtain PAN:** minors without taxable income (quote parent's/guardian's PAN); NR earning only specified-fund (AIF I & II, IFSC) income with TDS u/s 194LBB; NR "eligible foreign investor" earning only IFSC-listed Sec 47(viab) capital gains paid in foreign currency (subject to prescribed KYC declarations & Form 49BA reporting by the fund/broker).
  - **Foreign company** with no India-taxable income, no PAN, entering IFSC banking-unit transactions (account opening / FD) must furnish **Form 60**.
  - **Sec 272B penalty:**

| Default | Penalty |
|---|---|
| Failure to comply with Sec 139A | ₹10,000 |
| Quoting a false PAN/Aadhaar | ₹10,000 per default |
| Failure to authenticate PAN/Aadhaar in prescribed transactions | ₹10,000 per default |
| Recipient of documents fails to ensure/authenticate PAN/Aadhaar | ₹10,000 per default |

- **Concept:** PAN is the primary identifier tracking an assessee across high-value transactions; the thresholds above are the classic "quoting" triggers independent of return-filing obligation.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Don't confuse the **₹2,50,000** aggregate-financial-transaction PAN-application trigger (for a non-individual resident, or its officers) with the **₹20 lakh** cash deposit/withdrawal trigger (7-day advance-application rule) — these are two separate clauses.

### Aadhaar — Sec 139AA & Interchangeability

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - Every person eligible for Aadhaar must quote it (a) in the PAN application, (b) in the ROI, from **1st July 2017**.
  - PAN allotted on 1st July 2017 or earlier: Aadhaar-PAN linking deadline was **31st March 2022**; failure renders PAN **inoperative** until linked (linking after 1/4/2022 attracts fee u/s 234H). PAN becomes operative again within **30 days** of intimating Aadhaar.
  - **Enrolment ID route discontinued from 1/10/2024**; anyone who obtained PAN on the basis of an Enrolment ID must intimate the actual Aadhaar number to the DGIT/PDGIT (Systems) by **31/12/2025**.
  - **Sec 139AA exempted classes** (per CG notification) — individuals not possessing Aadhaar/Enrolment ID who are: resident of J&K, Meghalaya or Assam; a Non-Resident under the Act; aged **80 years or more** at any time in the PY; not a citizen of India.
  - Negative consequences of an inoperative PAN (for not quoting/furnishing PAN) apply **from 1/7/2023** per CBDT clarification, even though the linking deadline itself was 31/3/2022.
  - **PAN-Aadhaar interchangeability:** a person without PAN but holding Aadhaar can quote Aadhaar (PAN auto-allotted, no fee/documents); a person entering a Sec 139A "point-6" prescribed transaction must **authenticate** the PAN/Aadhaar quoted, and the transaction counterparty must also authenticate it — except where the depositor/opener is the Central/State Government or a Consular Office.
- **Concept:** Aadhaar-PAN linkage is the enforcement backbone ensuring a single tax identity per person; an unlinked PAN is treated as "PAN not quoted," triggering higher TDS/TCS and Sec 272B exposure.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** The exemption list (J&K/Meghalaya/Assam residents, NR, 80+ years, non-citizens) is commonly tested with a "trick" fact pattern — e.g., an 80-year-old resident of Delhi is still exempt purely on age.

### Tax Return Preparer, Annexure-less Return, Verification & Self-Assessment Tax (Sec 139B, 139C/D, 140, 140A)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Sec 139B — TRP:** CBDT scheme lets a specified class of persons file ROI through a Tax Return Preparer. TRP excludes a CA, legal practitioner, scheduled-bank officer (where assessee maintains an account), and an employee of the specified-class person. Only **Individuals and HUFs** can currently use the TRP scheme; specified class excludes companies and persons whose accounts require audit u/s 44AB or any other law. Eligibility to become TRP: bachelor's degree from a recognised Indian university, or passed Inter of ICAI/ICSI/ICAI(CMA).
  - **Sec 139C/139D — Annexure-less return:** CBDT can prescribe classes required to e-file, the manner/form of e-filing, and can still require production of documents to the AO on demand.
  - **Sec 140 — Verification of return** (illustrative):

| Assessee | Verified by | If unavailable/incapacitated |
|---|---|---|
| Individual | Himself | Person competent to verify |
| HUF | Karta | Any adult member |
| Firm | Managing Partner | Any adult partner |
| LLP | Designated Partner | Any partner/prescribed person |
| Company | Managing Director | Any other Director/prescribed person; Liquidator (company in liquidation); IBC-appointed Insolvency Professional (CIRP admitted) |
| Political Party | CEO | — |
| Local Authority | Principal Officer | — |

  Return not verified ⇒ **void ab initio** (invalid return).
  - **Sec 140A — Self-Assessment Tax (SAT):** before filing the return, assessee pays tax after adjusting advance tax, TDS/TCS, MAT/AMT credit, and Sec 89/90/90A/91 relief, plus applicable **interest & fees**.

$$
\text{Order of adjustment of short payment} = \text{Fees} \rightarrow \text{Interest} \rightarrow \text{Tax}
$$

- **Concept:** Verification legitimises the return as a valid legal document; SAT ensures the tax liability is settled *before* the return is even filed, not merely reported.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** The SAT short-payment adjustment order (Fees first, then Interest, then Tax) is a frequently tested sequencing rule — reversing it is a common wrong-answer distractor.

### Updated Return — Sec 139(8A) & Sec 140B

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Time limit:** updated return can be furnished within **48 months** from the end of the relevant AY (e.g., updated return for AY 2025-26 can be filed up to **31st March 2030**).
  - Can be filed whether or not a return was earlier furnished u/s 139(1)/(4)/(5); cannot be a **return of loss**; cannot **reduce** total tax liability or generate/increase a refund versus the earlier return.
  - **Not eligible** where, for the relevant AY (or any earlier AY, counted from the year of the triggering event): search initiated u/s 132 or requisition u/s 132A; survey conducted u/s 133A (other than TDS/TCS survey); notice issued alleging seized assets/books "belong to"/"pertain to" such person; or (independently, without the AY-cascade) an updated return already filed for that RAY; assessment/reassessment/recomputation/revision proceeding pending or completed; AO holds information under PMLA/Black Money Act/Benami Act/SAFEMA communicated before filing; information received under Sec 90/90A DTAA exchange communicated before filing; prosecution proceedings under Chapter XXII initiated before filing; or a Sec 148A show-cause notice issued **after 36 months** from end of RAY with a "fit case" decision to issue Sec 148 notice.
  - **Additional tax slabs** (Sec 140B), on **(Tax + Surcharge + Health & Education Cess + Interest)**:

| Filed within (from end of RAY) | Additional tax |
|---|---|
| After expiry of Sec 139(4)/(5) time limit, but within **12 months** | **25%** |
| After 12 months, before **24 months** | **50%** |
| After 24 months, before **36 months** | **60%** |
| After 36 months, before **48 months** | **70%** |

  - Where **no earlier return** was filed: tax due (after advance tax, TDS/TCS, Sec 89/90/90A/91 relief, MAT/AMT credit) + interest + fee (234F) + additional tax, all with proof of payment; Sec 234A/234B interest computed on updated-return income (no earlier return to net against).
  - Where an **earlier return** exists: tax/interest payable is netted against relief/credit/TDS-TCS already claimed in the earlier return, increased by any refund already issued for the earlier return; Sec 234B "assessed tax" and Sec 234C both recomputed with reference to the updated return's total income.
- **Concept:** Updated return is a *voluntary, penal-cost* compliance window that lets a taxpayer correct an under-reported income even after the normal revision window has closed, in exchange for graded additional tax.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - An updated return **can never** be a loss return and **can never** lower tax/increase refund — treat any exam fact pattern proposing either as automatically barred.
  - The ineligibility due to search/survey/requisition is **AY-specific**: barred only for the AY of the triggering event and AYs **preceding** it, not automatically for subsequent AYs.
  - ⚠️ VERIFY — the 48-month time limit (up from the original 24 months under FA 2022) and the two additional 60%/70% slabs were introduced by a later Finance Act; confirm against the Finance Act applicable to your specific exam attempt, as this is one of the more recently amended provisions in the chapter.

### Income-tax Authorities, Jurisdiction & CBDT Powers (Sec 116–131)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s) — Hierarchy (Sec 116):** CBDT → PCCIT/CCIT (Assessment wing) & PDGIT/DGIT (Investigation wing) → PCIT/CIT & PDIT/DIT → Addl./Joint CIT (or DIT) → Asst./Deputy CIT (or DIT) & ITO → TRO/Inspector. **CIT(A)/JC(A)** are also authorities under Sec 116.
  - **Sec 2(7A) — Assessing Officer:** Addl. CIT / JC / AC / DC / ITO / Addl. DIT / JD / AD / DD.
  - **Sec 119 — CBDT circulars:** binding on subordinate authorities; CBDT **cannot** direct a particular assessment outcome in a particular case, nor interfere with CIT(A)/JC(A) appellate discretion; can relax provisions (e.g., extend due dates) and condone genuine-hardship delays even after expiry of the statutory period.
  - **Sec 120/124 — Jurisdiction:** allotted by territorial area, person/class of person, income/class of income, or case/class of cases; an AO's jurisdiction over a person is based on where the person carries on business/profession, has principal place of business, or resides.
  - **Sec 127 — Transfer of cases:** by CCIT/PCCIT/DGIT/PDGIT/CIT/PCIT/DIT/PDIT after giving opportunity of being heard — **no hearing required** if transfer is within the same city/town/locality.
  - **Sec 129 — Change of authority:** successor authority may continue proceedings from where predecessor left off; assessee may demand re-opening/re-hearing of earlier proceedings before a fresh order.
  - **Sec 130 — Faceless jurisdiction:** exercise of Sec 120/124 powers can be faceless, per Sec 144B automated allocation.
  - **Sec 131 — Powers of civil court:** discovery/inspection, enforcing attendance & examination on oath, compelling production of books/docs, issuing commissions; can **impound books of account for a maximum of 15 working days**.
  - **Challenging AO's jurisdiction** — time limits for the assessee:

| ROI filed u/s 139(1) | ROI not filed |
|---|---|
| 1 month from receipt of notice u/s 142(1)/143(2), or before completion of assessment — whichever earlier | Within limit allowed in notice u/s 142(1)/148, or within limit in a Sec 144 show-cause notice — whichever earlier |

- **Concept:** This tests the administrative skeleton — who can do what, to whom, and the jurisdiction-challenge clock, which is a common short-answer/MCQ zone.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** *SV Gopala Rao & Others [2017] (SC)* — CBDT cannot amend legislative provisions by a circular u/s 119. *Regen Powertech Pvt. Ltd. [2019] (Mad HC)* — genuine hardship (e.g., audit delay outside assessee's control) must be condoned by CBDT.

### Power to Call/Collect Information, Faceless Collection & Survey (Sec 133, 133A–133C, 135)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Sec 133 — Power to call for information:** any authority can call for information from any person; under Sec 133(6), where no proceeding is pending, an authority **below the rank of CIT/DIT/PCIT/PDIT** needs **prior approval** of that rank to exercise this power (JD/DD/AD can exercise without such approval). *Kathiroor Service Co-op. Bank Ltd. (2014, SC)*: even absent a pending proceeding, AO can call for relevant/useful information u/s 133(6) with DIT/CIT/PDIT/PCIT's permission.
  - **Sec 133A — Power of survey:** entry restricted to (a) business/profession premises — only during business hours; (b) any other place — only **after sunrise, before sunset** (restriction is on entry, not exit); requires prior approval of PDGIT/DGIT/PCCIT/CCIT. On entry: inspect books/docs, verify cash/stock/valuables, place identification marks, make an inventory, **impound books for max 15 working days** (extendable with approval of PCCIT/CCIT/PDGIT/DGIT/CIT/PCIT/DIT/PDIT), record statements. Function/ceremony surveys permitted only **after conclusion** of the event.
  - **Sec 133A(2A) — TDS/TCS survey:** entry only during sunrise-to-sunset, at premises within the authority's jurisdiction; books/documents can be inspected but **cannot be impounded**, and no inventory of cash/stock/valuables can be made.
  - **Sec 133B — Power to collect information:** entry only during business hours; **cannot remove** books or valuable articles.
  - **Sec 133C — Power to call for information (Investigation wing):** verification-notice power, exercisable **even if no proceeding is pending**.
  - **Sec 135 — Faceless collection:** Sec 133/133B/133C powers exercisable in faceless manner by prescribed authority.
- **Concept:** These are pre-assessment/verification information powers, distinct from the more invasive Sec 132 search power — the key discriminator is whether **impounding/seizure** is permitted (survey: yes, capped at 15 working days for books; TDS/TCS survey: no impounding at all).
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** A classic distinction question: ordinary survey allows impounding books (max 15 working days, extendable with approval); a **TDS/TCS survey never allows impounding or inventory-taking** — memorise this contrast explicitly.

### Search & Seizure — Sec 132, 132A, 132B

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Who authorises a search:** PCCIT/CCIT/PDGIT/DGIT; PCIT/CIT/PDIT/DIT; Addl. CIT/DIT or JC/JD (if empowered by CBDT).
  - **Grounds:** person fails/will fail to produce books/documents summoned u/s 142(1)/131; or is in possession of undisclosed money/jewellery/valuable article. The **"reason to believe"** is never disclosed to any person, authority, or the ITAT.
  - **Powers during search:** enter & search premises/vessel/vehicle/aircraft; break locks; search any person on/near the premises; demand password for electronic books; seize books/documents/money/bullion/jewellery — **stock cannot be seized**.
  - **Deemed/constructive seizure:** where physical possession is impractical (volume/weight/nature), an order restraining removal/dealing is served instead.
  - **Prohibitory order (order of restraint):** for other practical-impossibility cases — valid for a **maximum of 60 days**.
  - **Presumptions (Sec 132(4A)):** books/documents/assets found belong to the person in possession; their contents are true; signatures/handwriting are genuine; attested/stamped documents are validly so.
  - **Sec 132(9A):** cross-jurisdiction books/assets handed to the correct AO within **60 days** from completion of search.
  - **Sec 132(9B)/(9C) — Provisional attachment:** during search or within **60 days** of its conclusion, with reasons recorded in writing and revenue interest involved; automatically **vacated after 6 months**.
  - **Sec 132(9D) — Reference to Valuation Officer:** during search or within 60 days of conclusion; VO's FMV report due within **60 days** of the reference.
  - **Conclusion of search/requisition:** search — date of the **last panchnama**; requisition — date of **actual receipt** of books/assets by the authorised officer.
  - **Sec 132A — Requisition:** where assets/books are already seized by another authority (GST, CBI, Election Commission, etc.) or held elsewhere, the authorised officer requisitions delivery.
  - **Sec 132B — Application of seized assets:**
    - Books/documents: released within **1 month** from end of the quarter of assessment/reassessment/recomputation (retention beyond needs approval of PCCIT/CCIT/PDGIT/DGIT/PCIT/CIT/PDIT/DIT).
    - Money/bullion/jewellery: assessee's "explain-the-asset" application within **30 days** from end of the month of seizure; if satisfied, AO releases (after adjusting existing tax liability) with approval of PCCIT/CCIT/PCIT/CIT, **within 120 days** from conclusion of search.
    - Seized money is first applied to existing + newly determined liability; if short, other assets are sold; balance is returned.
    - **Interest to assessee** — simple interest @ **0.5% per month** (or part) on:

$$
\text{Interest base} = \text{Money seized/requisitioned} + \text{Sale proceeds of assets} - \text{Explained money released} - \text{Aggregate liability discharged}
$$

    running from the day after expiry of the 120-day period to the date of completion of assessment/reassessment.
- **Concept:** Search is the most invasive information-gathering power, justified only on specific "reason to believe" grounds, with tight statutory clocks (60 days, 120 days, 6 months) governing attachment, release and interest.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** *Hemant Kumar Sindhi & Anr. (2014, All HC)* — seized assets can be sold/adjusted u/s 132B only once liability is **determined on completion of assessment**; an assessee cannot force early sale merely to avoid Sec 234B interest.

### Enquiry Before Assessment, Special Audit & Valuation Reference (Sec 142, 142(2A), 142A, 142B)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Sec 142(1):** if no return filed u/s 139(1), AO/authority not below ITO rank may notice the assessee to furnish a return; separately, for making an assessment, AO may call for books/documents (**max 3 years prior to the relevant PY**) or information on assets/liabilities (JC's prior approval needed if such information is not part of the books).
  - **Sec 142(2A) — Special audit / inventory valuation:**
    - Triggers: complexity of accounts, volume, doubts on correctness, multiplicity of transactions, nature of business, interest of revenue.
    - Requires prior approval of CIT/CCIT/PCIT/PCCIT **and** an opportunity of being heard before directing.
    - Can be directed **even if accounts are already audited** u/s 44AB or any other law; can cover a particular segment (sales, purchases, etc.).
    - Report due within time allowed by AO, extendable but **not beyond 180 days** in aggregate.
    - Opportunity of being heard required before using the special-audit material against the assessee.
    - Non-compliance ⇒ Best Judgment Assessment u/s 144 **plus** penalty of **₹10,000** u/s 272A.
    - Auditor's/CMA's remuneration fixed by CIT/CCIT/PCIT/PCCIT, paid by CG — **₹3,750 to ₹7,500 per hour**.
  - **Sec 142A — Reference to Valuation Officer:** for estimating FMV of any asset/property/investment; VO's report to AO & assessee within **6 months** from end of the month of reference; AO must give a hearing before relying on it.
  - **Sec 142B — Faceless inquiry/valuation:** Sec 142(1), 142(2), 142(2A) and 142A functions can be exercised faceless per Sec 144B.
- **Concept:** These are the AO's fact-gathering tools *before* finalising an assessment — special audit for complex/doubtful accounts, VO reference for asset valuation disputes.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** ⚠️ VERIFY — the ₹3,750–₹7,500/hour special-audit remuneration band is drawn from Income-tax Rule 14B; confirm the current Rule 14B figures haven't been revised for the exam year, as fee-slab rules are periodically updated by notification.

### Processing of Return & Scrutiny Assessment (Sec 143(1), 143(2), 143(3))

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Sec 143(1) — Processing/Intimation:** CPC adjusts for: arithmetical errors; incorrect claims apparent from the return; inconsistency with a preceding PY's return (as prescribed); disallowance of a loss claimed in a late-filed return; disallowance of expenditure/income increase flagged in the audit report but not in the return; disallowance of Sec 10AA/Chapter VI-A "C" deductions where return is late.
  - Before any adjustment, assessee gets an intimation to respond; if **no response within 30 days**, processing proceeds with the adjustment.
  - Intimation issued if there is refund/demand/loss-adjustment (practically, issued in virtually all cases).

$$
\text{Time limit for Sec 143(1) intimation} = 9 \text{ months from end of the FY in which the return was filed}
$$

  - **Sec 143(1D):** intimation is issued even where a scrutiny notice u/s 143(2) has already been issued (applicable from AY 2017-18).
  - **Sec 143(2) — Scrutiny notice:** must be **served** within **3 months from the end of the FY in which the return was filed**; can be issued after a Sec 143(1) intimation.
  - **Sec 143(3) — Scrutiny order:** AO determines income/loss & tax payable/refundable based on evidence furnished/gathered. Where an institution enjoying exemption u/s 10(21)/10(22B)/10(23A)/10(23B) has a contravention, AO cannot straightaway disallow — must first inform the government/prescribed authority and await withdrawal notification. Where AO believes a Sec 10(23C)/Sec 11 trust has committed a "specified violation" (Sec 12AB(4)), he must first refer the matter to PCIT/CIT and cannot pass the assessment order until PCIT/CIT gives effect to the 12AB(4) order.
- **Concept:** Sec 143(1) is an automated, largely non-discretionary check; Sec 143(2)/(3) is the full discretionary scrutiny assessment, gated by a strict service-of-notice clock.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** The 3-month Sec 143(2) clock runs from **end of the FY in which the return was filed** (not the AY) — students frequently miscount this as "from filing date."

### Best Judgment Assessment & JC's Power of Direction (Sec 144, 144A)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Sec 144 — Triggers for BJA:** (i) failure to file ROI u/s 139(1) and no return filed u/s 139(4)/139(5)/139(8A); (ii) failure to comply with Sec 142(1) notice; (iii) failure to comply with Sec 142(2A) special-audit direction; (iv) failure to comply with Sec 143(2) scrutiny notice.
  - BJA requires a prior show-cause notice/opportunity of being heard — **except** where the default is non-compliance with Sec 142(1).
  - **No refund** can be granted in a BJA order.
  - BJA must be based on **some evidence/material**, not arbitrary/ad-hoc addition.
  - **Sec 144A:** JC may (suo motu, on assessee's application, or on AO's reference) issue binding directions to guide the AO in completing a pending assessment; directions **prejudicial** to the assessee require a prior hearing; no separate appeal lies against the direction itself (only against the resultant assessment order).
- **Concept:** BJA is the AO's fallback where the assessee doesn't cooperate — an estimate, not an arbitrary figure, and it can never yield a refund to the assessee.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Combine this with Sec 153(1) — Sec 143(3) and Sec 144 orders share the **same 12-month completion deadline** (from end of RAY, for AY 2022-23 onwards).

### Faceless Assessment — Sec 144B

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **NFAC (National Faceless Assessment Centre)** allocates cases to an **Assessment Unit (AU)** via automated allocation; notices u/s 143(2)/142(1) route through NFAC.
  - **AU** functions: identifying issues, seeking clarifications, analysing material.
  - **Verification Unit (VU):** enquiry/cross-verification, examination of books, examination of witnesses/recording statements (function may be performed by a VU in any faceless centre, request routed via NFAC).
  - **Technical Unit (TU):** legal/accounting/forensic/IT/valuation/transfer-pricing/data-analytics/management technical assistance.
  - **Review Unit (RU):** checks the income-determination proposal for completeness of evidence, correctness of facts/law, and whether additions/disallowances are properly incorporated.
  - Authorities staffing AU/VU/TU/RU: Addl. CIT/DIT or JC/JD; DC/DD/AC/AD/ITO; other prescribed authority/staff.
  - All communications are electronic; personal hearing (if a variation is proposed via SCN) is conducted **exclusively via video conferencing**; CBDT must provide VC facility for those lacking one.
  - AU may, on its own reasoned opinion, refer a case to NFAC for invoking Sec 142(2A) special audit; PCCIT/PDGIT of NFAC decides on forwarding this to the jurisdictional PCCIT/CCIT/PCIT/CIT, or may transfer the case to the jurisdictional AO.
  - After completion, NFAC transfers all electronic records to the jurisdictional AO.
- **Concept:** Faceless Assessment de-personalises Sec 143(3)/144/147 assessments through a multi-unit, video-conference-only workflow, aiming to eliminate direct taxpayer-officer contact.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Remember the **function-vs-unit mapping** (AU = analyse, VU = verify, TU = technical support, RU = review) — a very common matching-type question.

### Dispute Resolution Panel — Sec 144C

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Applies to:** (a) a foreign company or non-resident where the AO proposes a variation prejudicial to the assessee; (b) any assessee where the variation stems from a TPO order u/s 92CA.
  - AO forwards a **draft order** to the assessee.
  - Assessee, within **30 days** of receipt, must either accept (to AO) or object (to AO **and** DRP).
  - If accepted: AO passes final order within **1 month** from end of the month of acceptance.
  - If objected: DRP issues directions within **9 months** from end of the month the draft order was forwarded to the assessee; AO passes final order within **1 month** from end of the month directions are received.
  - DRP directions are **binding on the AO**; DRP may confirm, reduce, or enhance the proposed variation.
  - Assessee dissatisfied with the final order can appeal to **ITAT**; the **Department cannot** appeal against DRP's directions.
  - Not applicable to proceedings u/s 158B to 158BI (search cases, on/after 1st September 2024).
  - CG may notify a scheme for faceless issuance of DRP directions.
- **Concept:** DRP is a pre-appeal, collegiate review mechanism specifically for TP and NR/foreign-company variations, designed to reduce protracted litigation before it starts.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** The 30-day acceptance/objection window and the 9-month DRP-direction window are frequently tested together in a timeline numerical.

### Method of Accounting, ICDS & Deemed Best Judgment (Sec 145, 145A, 145B)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Sec 145(1):** for **PGBP** and **Income from Other Sources**, method of accounting = **Cash or Mercantile** (assessee's choice, consistently followed); Salary, House Property, and Capital Gains have **no prescribed method** — taxed per their own specific computational rules.
  - **Sec 145(2) — ICDS:** CG has notified **10 ICDS**, effective **AY 2017-18**, applicable for computing PGBP & IFOS income under the mercantile system.
  - **Sec 145(3) — Discretionary BJA:** AO may proceed to a Sec 144 assessment if: (1) not satisfied about completeness/correctness of books; (2) correct/regular accounting method not followed; (3) notified ICDS not followed.
  - **Sec 145B — Taxability timing:** (i) interest on enhanced/late compensation — taxable in the **year of receipt**; (ii) price-escalation claim or export incentive — taxable in the year **reasonable certainty of realisation** is achieved; (iii) Government grant — taxable in the year of **accrual or receipt, whichever is earlier**.
- **Concept:** These sections nail down *when* PGBP/IFOS income is recognised, overriding pure accounting-method timing with statute-driven certainty tests for interest, escalation claims, incentives, and grants.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Sec 145B(i)'s "interest on compensation taxed on receipt basis" frequently intersects with Capital Gains chapter questions on enhanced compensation — keep the two timing rules distinct (CG accrual vs. this IFOS-style receipt rule).

### Income Escaping Assessment / Reassessment — Sec 147–151A

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Sec 147:** AO may assess/reassess escaped income for any AY, subject to the Sec 148–153 procedure; if, during such reassessment, **other escaped income for the same AY** surfaces, it can be assessed without a fresh Sec 148 notice/148A order — but income relating to a **different AY** needs a fresh Sec 148/148A process for that other year.
  - **Sec 148 — Notice:** issued with a copy of the Sec 148A(3) order, requiring a return within a period specified in the notice, **not exceeding 3 months** from end of the month of issue. Filed return is deemed filed u/s 139 (if within time) — a late Sec 148 return is **not** deemed a Sec 139 return, and **cannot be revised**.
  - **Sec 148A — Pre-notice procedure:** AO serves a show-cause notice (with the underlying information) before issuing Sec 148; assessee replies within the specified period; AO passes a **Sec 148A(3) order** (fit/not fit to issue Sec 148 notice) with the **prior approval of the Sec 151 authority**. No appeal to CIT(A)/ITAT against a 148A(3) order (writ to HC only, for natural-justice breach). **Sec 148A does not apply** where information is received under the Sec 135A scheme (AO can issue Sec 148 directly).
  - **"Information" justifying Sec 148 (illustrative):** risk-management-strategy information (e.g., SFT u/s 285BA, investigation-wing info u/s 133C); audit objection that an assessment wasn't made per the Act; information under a Sec 90/90A DTAA; information under the Sec 135A scheme; information consequent to a Tribunal/Court order; information from a Sec 133A survey (other than TDS/TCS survey), on/after **1st September 2024**.
  - **Sec 148B:** where search u/s 132 or survey u/s 133A (other than TDS/TCS survey) has occurred, assessment/reassessment cannot be made by an AO **below the rank of JC**, except with approval of JC/JD/Addl. CIT/Addl. DIT.
  - **Sec 149 — Time limits (w.e.f. 1st September 2024):**

| Case | Notice u/s 148 | Order u/s 148A(3) |
|---|---|---|
| Normal case | **3 years 3 months** from end of RAY | **3 years** from end of RAY |
| Specific case (escaped income ≥ ₹50 lakh, evidenced by books/documents/asset/expenditure/transaction/entry in AO's possession) | **5 years 3 months** from end of RAY | **5 years** from end of RAY |

  - **Sec 151 — Sanctioning authority (w.e.f. 1/9/2024):** unified as **Addl. CIT/Addl. DIT/JC/JD** for all cases (pre-1/9/2024, sanctioning authority was tiered — CIT/PCIT/DIT/PDIT within 3 years of RAY, PCIT/PCCIT/DGIT/CCIT thereafter).
  - **Sec 150 — Unlimited time limit:** no time bar on a Sec 148 notice issued to give effect to a finding/direction in an order of CIT(A)/ITAT/HC/SC/revision u/s 263/264/any other-law court, where the direction is to exclude income from one AY and include it in another, or exclude from one assessee and include in another — **except** where the reopening was already time-barred when the original (appealed) order was passed.
  - **Sec 152(1):** escaped income is taxed at the **rate applicable to the relevant (escaped) AY**.
  - **Sec 152(2) — Dropping proceedings:** AO may drop Sec 147 proceedings if the assessee satisfies him (a) there is no impact on tax liability even after including the escaped income, and (b) no appeal/revision/reference has been filed against any part of the original assessment order.
  - **Sec 151A — Faceless reassessment:** Sec 147 assessment/reassessment/recomputation and Sec 148 notice issuance can be conducted faceless, per Sec 144B automated allocation.
- **Concept:** Reassessment reopens a completed or non-existent assessment on fresh "information," with 2024's amendment compressing the earlier two-tier (3-year/10-year) regime into a **3-years-3-months / 5-years-3-months** structure and centralising sanctioning authority.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - The **₹50 lakh** escaped-income threshold for the extended (5-year-3-month) window is a frequently tested numeric — note it must be evidenced by **books/documents/asset/expenditure/transaction/entries**, not a bare estimate.
  - A search case is now governed by **Chapter XIV-B (Sec 158BA–158BFA)**, not Sec 147, for searches initiated **on/after 1st September 2024** — pre-1/9/2024 searches still followed the old Sec 147/153A route.

### Time Limit for Completing Assessment — Sec 153

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

| Sec | Assessment | Time Limit |
|---|---|---|
| 153(1) | Sec 143(3) scrutiny / Sec 144 BJA | **12 months** from end of AY (AY 2022-23 onwards); progressively longer for older AYs (AY 2021-22: 9 months; AY 2020-21: 18 months; AY 2019-20: 12 months; AY 2018-19: 18 months; AY 2017-18 & earlier: 21 months) |
| 153(1) proviso | Return filed u/s 139(8A) (updated) or under a Sec 119 CBDT-condoned late-filing order | **12 months** from end of the FY in which such return was furnished |
| 153(2) | Sec 147 reassessment | **12 months** from end of the FY in which notice u/s 148 was served |
| 153(3) | Fresh assessment/TPO order after set-aside u/s 250/254/263/264 | **12 months** from end of the FY in which the appellate/revision order is received/passed by the specified authority |
| 153(3A) | Assessment pending on date of search/requisition | **+12 months** to all above limits |
| 153(4) | Reference made to TPO u/s 92CA | **+12 months** to all above limits |
| 153(5) | Giving effect to an order u/s 250/254/260/262/263/264 (non-fresh-assessment cases) | **3 months** from end of the month of receipt/passing of that order (extendable by **6 months** with CIT/PCIT approval on AO's/TPO's application; or **12 months** where verification/hearing is needed, per 153(3)) |
| 153(5A) | TPO gives effect to Sec 263 order and forwards to AO | AO modifies assessment within **2 months** from end of the month of receipt |
| 153(6)(i) | Assessment/reassessment per a court/appellate finding or direction (Sec 150) | **12 months** from end of the month the order is received/passed |
| 153(6)(ii) | Assessment on a partner consequent to Sec 147 assessment on the firm | **12 months** from end of the month the firm's assessment order was passed |

  - **Exclusions extending the Sec 153 clock** (illustrative): period between AO informing government of a Sec 10(21)/(22B)/(23A)/(23B) contravention and receipt of the withdrawal notification; period of a Sec 142(2A) special-audit direction (till report due date, or till a court order on a challenge is received); period of a Sec 142A valuation reference (till report received); period of a Sec 158A declaration (max **60 days**); period of an application to the **BAR** (Board for Advance Rulings); period of a Sec 90/90A information-exchange reference (till info received, or **1 year**, whichever is less); period of a Sec 12AB(4) reference to PCIT/CIT (till order copy received); period a court stays the assessment proceeding.
  - **Floor rule:** after excluding the above periods, if the remaining time available to the AO is **less than 60 days**, it is extended to **60 days**.
- **Concept:** Sec 153 is the master assessment-completion clock — every assessment type (scrutiny, BJA, reassessment, giving-effect orders) has its own trigger date and duration, further stretched by search/TPO-reference extensions and specific procedural exclusions.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** The **12-month standard period** (post AY 2022-23) is the default to memorise cold; older-AY variants (9/18/21 months) are largely historical/legacy and less likely to be tested directly, but the **+12 months for search-pending or TPO-reference cases**, and the **60-day floor rule**, are high-yield numericals.

### Rectification & Demand Notice — Sec 154, 156, 156A

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Sec 154 — Rectification of mistake apparent from record** (not a debatable mistake), in: any order passed by the authority; Sec 143(1) intimation; TDS/TCS intimation u/s 200A/206CB(1).
  - Can be done **suo motu** or on **assessee's application**; no fee, no prescribed form.

$$
\text{Time limit (suo motu)} = 4\text{ years from end of the FY in which the order sought to be rectified was passed}
$$
$$
\text{Time limit (on application)} = 6\text{ months from end of the month the application is received}
$$

  - A rectified order can itself be further rectified — the **4-year clock resets** from the end of the year the rectified order was passed.
  - A rectified order (whether passed suo motu or on application) is an **appealable order**.
  - **Sec 156 — Demand notice:** issued for tax/interest/penalty/other sum payable per any order; assessee must pay within **30 days** of receipt; default ⇒ assessee-in-default, liable to interest u/s 220 and penalty u/s 221. Intimations u/s 143(1)/200A(1)/206CB(1) are **deemed** demand notices.
  - **Sec 156A:** where a demand under Sec 156 is reduced by an order of the Adjudicating Authority under the IBC, 2016, AO modifies and re-serves a revised demand notice; if that IBC order is itself modified by NCLT/Supreme Court, the demand notice is revised again accordingly.
- **Concept:** Sec 154 fixes clerical/apparent errors without reopening the substantive assessment; Sec 156 crystallises the payable amount into an enforceable demand.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** "Mistake apparent from record" excludes anything **debatable** (requiring long-drawn reasoning/argument) — a classic exam distinguishing test.

### Protective Assessment (No Specific Section)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):** where ownership of income is disputed/doubtful, AO may assess the **same income in the hands of all claimants**, to protect revenue's interest — but tax can be **recovered from only one** of them (whichever is ultimately held to be the real owner).
- **Concept:** A safeguard mechanism for genuine ownership disputes (e.g., civil litigation, benami transactions), not a device to double-tax the same income.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Protective assessment ≠ double taxation — recovery is restricted to a single person once ownership is finally determined.

### Special Procedure for Assessment in Search Cases — Chapter XIV-B (Sec 158BA–158BFA)

*(Applies to search u/s 132 / requisition u/s 132A initiated/made on or after 1st September 2024, added by FA 2024)*

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Block Period:** the **6 AYs** preceding the PY of search/requisition, **plus** the period from **1st April** of the search-PY to the **date of execution of the last search authorisation** (or actual receipt of assets/books, for a requisition).

$$
\text{Undisclosed income of Block Period} = \text{Income declared in the ITR-B return (Sec 158BC)} + \text{Income determined by AO}
$$

  - **Excluded from undisclosed income:** income already assessed u/s 143(3)/144/147/153A/153C/158BC before the date of search/requisition; income already declared in a Sec 139/142(1) return (not otherwise covered); income computed from regular books/documents for the pre-search period (past completed years, current year up to search date, and the search-execution period itself), unless AO finds part of it undisclosed; income referred to u/s 115A(5)/115G/194P.
  - **Sec 158BC:** AO issues notice for an **ITR-B** return within a period specified, **max 60 days** (extendable by a further **30 days** in limited audit-pending circumstances), with prior approval of Addl. CIT/Addl. DIT/JC/JD. Such return is deemed a Sec 139 return (notice u/s 143(2) then follows) but **cannot be revised**; Sec 143(1) does not apply to it; no separate Sec 148 notice is needed for this chapter.
  - **Abatement:** any assessment/reassessment pending as on date of search/requisition (for the block-period years) **abates** (except appeals/revision, which continue); any TPO reference/order also abates.
  - **Sec 158BD — Other person's undisclosed income:** where seized material belongs/pertains/relates to a person other than the one searched, it is handed to that person's jurisdictional AO, who then follows the same Sec 158BA/BB/BC procedure; the "date of search" for that other person is the date **his** AO actually receives the material.
  - **Tax rate — Sec 113:** flat **60%** on the total undisclosed income of the block period (plus applicable surcharge/cess).
  - **No interest/penalty overlap — Sec 158BF:** no interest u/s 234A/234B/234C, and no Sec 270A penalty, on the block-period undisclosed income.
  - **Sec 158BE — Time limit for block assessment:** **12 months** from the end of the **quarter** in which the last search authorisation was executed/requisition made (searched person); **12 months** from end of the quarter the Sec 158BC notice was issued (other person, Sec 158BD); **+12 months** if referred to TPO; time extended to **13 months** where the 30-day return-filing extension was granted; exclusion available (**max 6 months**) for the period between search initiation and handover of seized material to the jurisdictional AO.
  - **Sec 158BFA — Interest & penalty:**
    - Interest: simple interest **@1.5% per month** (or part) on the tax on undisclosed income, from the day after expiry of the notice period to completion of assessment, if the ITR-B return is filed late/not filed.
    - Penalty: **50%** of the tax payable on the undisclosed income; this penalty (and Sec 271AAD/271D/271DA/271E) is **waived** if the assessee has filed the ITR-B return, paid the tax due (or offered seized money for adjustment), furnished proof of payment with the return, and has **not appealed** the assessed portion matching the return — waiver does not extend to the excess where the AO's determined undisclosed income exceeds the returned figure.
- **Concept:** Chapter XIV-B reintroduces a *separate, fixed-rate block assessment* for post-1/9/2024 search cases (in place of the earlier Sec 153A/153C regime), taxing undisclosed income of a defined multi-year block at a flat 60%, outside the normal slab/interest/Sec 270A framework.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Do not confuse this with the **old** Sec 153A/153C search-assessment machinery — that regime still governs searches conducted **before** 1st September 2024; Chapter XIV-B is exclusively for searches/requisitions on/after that date.
  - ⚠️ VERIFY — the Sec 158BFA(1) interest rate of **1.5% per month** should be cross-checked against the bare Act/latest CBDT clarification for your exact exam attempt; the historical (pre-2003) block-assessment interest rate under this section was aligned to the Sec 234A rate of 1% per month, and this chapter's reintroduction via FA 2024 is one of the newest provisions in the syllabus.
  - Interest/penalty **waiver conditions** under Sec 158BFA(2) are cumulative — missing even one (e.g., filing an appeal on the returned portion) forfeits the entire concession.

**Definitions**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Block Period | 6 AYs preceding the search/requisition PY, plus the part-year up to the last search-authorisation/receipt date |
| ITR-B | Prescribed return form for declaring undisclosed income of the block period under Sec 158BC |
| Panchnama | Search-conclusion document; its date fixes the "date of search" for limitation purposes |

### References

1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sections 116–156A, 158B–158BFA (as amended up to Finance (No. 2) Act 2024 and Finance Act 2025), for authority hierarchy, PAN/Aadhaar, search & seizure, assessment/reassessment procedure, updated return, and block assessment provisions.
2. Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024 — reconstitution of reassessment time limits (Sec 148/149/151) w.e.f. 1st September 2024, and reintroduction of block-assessment Chapter XIV-B (Sec 158BA–158BFA) for searches/requisitions on/after that date.
3. Finance Act, 2025 (and preceding Finance Act 2022 for original enactment) — extension of the updated-return time limit under Sec 139(8A)/140B to 48 months with graded additional-tax slabs (25%/50%/60%/70%).
4. CBDT Circular No. 11/2024 (w.e.f. 1/10/2024) — revised monetary limits of authorities (CIT/PCIT, CCIT, PCCIT) for condonation of delay in filing a loss return, u/s 119(2)(b) read with Sec 139.
5. ICAI — Study Material / RTP / MTP for CA Final Direct Tax Laws & International Taxation (Assessment Procedure chapter), for the seventh-proviso Sec 139(1) high-value-transaction thresholds and PAN quoting (Rule 114B) thresholds.

## 13. Appeals, Revisions & Dispute Resolution Committee
> **Where it fits:** the litigation ladder after an assessment/penalty order — JC(A)/CIT(A) → ITAT → High Court → Supreme Court, plus the departmental revision powers (Sec 263/264) and the alternate, faster Dispute Resolution Committee (Sec 245MA) route for small, uncomplicated disputes.

### Appeal to Joint Commissioner (Appeals) / Commissioner (Appeals) — Sec 246, 246A–251
- **Key rules:**
  - **Sec 246(1) — Appeal to JC(A):** for orders passed **on or after 1.4.2023** by an AO **below the rank of Joint Commissioner**, appeal lies to JC(A) — covers assessment orders u/s 143(3)/144/147, intimation u/s 143(1)/200A/206CB, rectification u/s 154/155, order u/s 201/206C(6A) (assessee-in-default), and penalty orders. **Exception:** if the AO's order was passed with the prior approval of an authority above the rank of Deputy Commissioner, appeal goes to CIT(A) instead.
  - **Sec 246A — Appeal to CIT(A):** covers a wider list — assessment/reassessment orders u/s 143(3), 144, 147, 158BC; intimations u/s 143(1)/200A/206CB; rectification u/s 154/155; an order where the assessee denies liability to be assessed; and orders u/s 92CD, 115VP, 163, 170, 171, 201, 206C(6A), 221, 237, 239A, and penalty orders.
  - CBDT (or an authorised IT authority) may **transfer a pending appeal between JC(A) and CIT(A)**; the appellant must be given a fresh opportunity of being heard after transfer.
  - **Time limit to file:** 30 days from date of receipt of the notice of demand (assessment/penalty) or of the order/intimation (any other case); JC(A)/CIT(A) may **condone delay** for sufficient cause.
  - **Form:** Form No. 35 (Memorandum of Appeal), with statement of facts, grounds of appeal, copy of order/intimation, and filing fee.
  - **Time to dispose (advisory):** where possible, within 1 year from the end of the FY in which the appeal is filed or transferred.
  - **Pre-condition for admission of appeal:** assessee must have paid tax on the income *returned* by him; if no return was filed, tax equal to advance tax payable — though JC(A)/CIT(A) may, on application, exempt the assessee from this payment and still admit the appeal.
  - Only the **assessee** can file this first appeal (department has no right of first appeal).
- **Concept:** the first appellate stage against an AO-level order; choice of forum (JC(A) vs CIT(A)) turns on the rank of the officer who passed the order and the nature of the order.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Do not confuse the 30-day limitation (first appeal) with the 60-day limit for ITAT appeals.
  - Remember the JC(A) forum is a Finance Act 2023 innovation — apply the "below rank of JC" test carefully in MCQs/case scenarios.
  - The 1-year disposal timeline is advisory ("if possible"), not a hard limitation — do not treat it as void if breached.

### Appeal to ITAT — Sec 252–255
- **Key rules:**
  - **Bench:** normally a Division Bench (1 Judicial + 1 Accountant Member); a **Single Member Bench** may hear the case if the assessee's total income does not exceed **₹50 lakh**. Decision is by majority; on an equal split, the point goes to the President, who refers it to another member — decision then follows majority.
  - **Time limit to file:** 60 days from the end of the month in which the order appealed against is communicated (Sec 253(3)).
  - **Form:** Form No. 36, with statement of facts, grounds of appeal, copy of order, and filing fee.
  - **Cross objections:** the other party may file Form No. 36A within 30 days of receiving notice that an appeal has been filed — **no fee** payable.
  - **Time to dispose (advisory):** where possible, within 4 years from the end of the FY in which the appeal is filed (Sec 254(2A)).
  - **Appealable orders:** order of JC(A)/CIT(A); AO's order passed on DRP directions u/s 144C; revision order u/s 263; AO's order passed with CIT/PCIT approval u/s 144BA (GAAR); and other specified orders of CIT/CCIT/DIT/DGIT/PCIT/PDIT/PDGIT.
  - **Rectification u/s 254(2):** ITAT may rectify a mistake apparent from the record, within **6 months from the end of the month in which the order was passed**, suo motu or on application by the assessee/AO. ITAT has **no power of review** — only rectification of an apparent mistake.
- **Concept:** the first forum that is a mixed judicial-cum-technical Tribunal and the last forum on pure questions of fact.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - ITAT can set aside and remand to the AO for fresh assessment — JC(A)/CIT(A) generally cannot, **except** where the appeal is against an order u/s 144 (best judgment assessment), where CIT(A) may set aside and remand — inserted by FA 2024 w.e.f. 1.10.2024.
  - ITAT has no power to review/re-appreciate its own order under Sec 254(2) — *Earnest Exports Ltd. (Bom.) / Lachman Dass Bhatia Hingwala (Delhi HC)*, reaffirmed in *Reliance Telecom Ltd. (2022)(SC)*.
  - ITAT cannot dismiss an appeal for mere non-appearance without deciding on merits — *Ritha Sabapathy (2019)(Mad.)*.

### Stay of Demand by ITAT — Sec 254(2A)
- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
$$
\text{Minimum deposit for stay} \;=\; 20\% \times \big(\text{disputed tax} + \text{interest} + \text{penalty} + \text{fee}\big)
$$
  — or the assessee furnishes security of an equivalent amount.
  - **Initial stay period:** up to **180 days**.
  - **Extension:** if ITAT cannot dispose of the appeal within 180 days for reasons **not attributable to the assessee**, it may extend the stay, but the **total stay (original + extensions) cannot exceed 365 days**.
  - Beyond 365 days, the stay stands automatically vacated — **even if the delay is due to the Department** — *subject to* the SC's reading down below.
- **Concept:** a partial-payment safeguard so recovery doesn't proceed while a bona fide appeal is pending, balanced against a hard outer time cap to prevent indefinite stays.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - ⚠️ VERIFY — the OCR cites *Pepsi Foods Ltd. (2021)* as a **Supreme Court** ruling; the landmark judgment reading down the third proviso to Sec 254(2A) (striking the automatic vacation of stay where delay is *not* attributable to the assessee) is generally attributed to the **Delhi High Court (2015)**, later followed/affirmed in subsequent rulings — confirm the exact forum/year before quoting in an answer.
  - Key holding (regardless of forum): the automatic-vacation-of-stay proviso applies **only if the delay in disposal is attributable to the assessee**; if the delay is the Department's fault, the stay does not automatically lapse at 365 days.
  - Fee for a stay application to ITAT: **₹500**.

### Difference in powers — JC(A)/CIT(A) vs ITAT
| Power | JC(A)/CIT(A) | ITAT |
|---|---|---|
| Enhance the assessment | Yes | No |
| Reduce/confirm the assessment | Yes | Yes |
| Cancel the assessment | Yes | Yes |
| Set aside & remand to AO for fresh assessment | No (except Sec 144 orders, w.e.f. 1.10.2024) | Yes |
| Condone delay | Yes | Yes |
| Make further inquiries | Yes | Yes |
| Rectify its own order | Yes — Sec 154 | Yes — Sec 254(2) |
| Review its own order | No | No |
| Admit additional grounds of appeal | Yes | Yes |
| Admit additional evidence | Yes (conditions apply) | Yes (conditions apply) |
| Grant stay of demand | Yes | Yes |
| Award costs for a frivolous appeal | No | Yes |
| Reject the appeal | Yes | Yes |
- **Concept:** JC(A)/CIT(A) has *enhancement* power (can worsen the assessee's position) that ITAT lacks; ITAT alone can remand generally and award costs.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** neither forum can **review** its own order — only **rectify** an apparent mistake; do not conflate the two powers.

### Additional Evidence before Appellate Authorities
- **Key rule(s) — JC(A)/CIT(A) may admit additional evidence where:**
  - the AO rejected evidence produced by the assessee;
  - the AO completed assessment without giving an opportunity to produce the evidence;
  - the AO demanded such evidence but the assessee could not produce it for sufficient cause; or
  - the AO never asked for it, but it was relevant and the assessee could not produce it for sufficient cause.
- **Key rule(s) — ITAT may admit additional evidence where:**
  - it is satisfied the income-tax authorities decided the case without giving sufficient opportunity to the assessee to produce evidence; or
  - ITAT itself requires the additional evidence/documents to enable it to pass its order.
- **Concept:** additional evidence is the exception, not the rule — appellate authorities must record satisfaction on one of the above grounds before admitting it.

### Appeal Filing Fees — JC(A)/CIT(A) vs ITAT
| Assessed income slab | JC(A)/CIT(A) fee | ITAT fee |
|---|---|---|
| Up to ₹1,00,000 | ₹250 | ₹500 |
| More than ₹1,00,000 up to ₹2,00,000 | ₹500 | ₹1,500 |
| More than ₹2,00,000 | ₹1,000 | 1% of assessed income, subject to **min. ₹5,000 and max. ₹10,000** |
| Any other case (no assessed total income, e.g. TDS-default/penalty-only orders) | ₹250 | ₹500 |
| Appeal filed by the Department | — | No fee |
| Cross objections (Form 36A) | — | No fee |
| Stay of demand application to ITAT | — | ₹500 |
- **Key formula:**
$$
\text{ITAT fee (income} > ₹2\text{ lakh)} = \operatorname{clip}\big(1\% \times \text{Assessed Total Income},\ ₹5{,}000,\ ₹10{,}000\big)
$$
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** the department never pays a filing fee at any forum; do not apply the % formula to the JC(A)/CIT(A) slab — that fee is a flat ₹1,000 above ₹2 lakh.

### Appeal to High Court — Sec 260A & 260B
- **Key rules:**
  - Appeal lies to the HC only if it involves a **substantial question of law**.
  - **Time limit:** 120 days from the date on which the order appealed against is received.
  - Form, fees, and procedure are governed by the **Code of Civil Procedure, 1908**.
  - HC has an **inherent power to review** its own order — *Meghalaya Steels Ltd. (2015)(SC)*; grounds for review per *Sunil Vasudeva v. Sundar Gupta (2019)(SC)*: discovery of new/important evidence not earlier available despite due diligence, or a mistake/error apparent on the face of the record, or any other sufficient reason — but **not** mere repetition of an overruled argument or a minor/inconsequential error.
- **Concept:** the HC's jurisdiction is confined to law, not fact — it must itself **formulate** the substantial question of law and decide only on that (*A.A. Estate Pvt. Ltd. (2019)(SC)*).
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - A cryptic ITAT order that doesn't engage with the merits does not, by itself, raise a substantial question of law for the HC — *Ritha Sabapathy (2019)(Mad.)*.
  - Delay in filing the HC appeal cannot be condoned merely because a Sec 254(2) rectification application was pending before ITAT — *Spinacom India (P.) Ltd. [2018](SC)*.
  - HC can go into ALP/transfer-pricing determination as a question of law where ITAT failed to follow the Sec 92–92F TP guidelines, including comparability/filter selection — *SAP Labs India Pvt. Ltd. [2023](SC)*.

### Appeal to Supreme Court — Sec 261 & 262
- **Key rules:**
  - Appeal lies against an HC order.
  - **Time limit:** 90 days (governed by the Limitation Act, 1963 / Supreme Court Rules, since Sections 261/262 do not themselves prescribe a period).
  - SC has power to **review** its own order.
  - Form, fees, and procedure are governed by the **Code of Civil Procedure, 1908**.
- **Concept:** the final appellate forum; typically requires an HC certificate that the case is fit for appeal, or leave to appeal.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** don't confuse the 90-day SC limitation with the 120-day HC limitation — they are commonly swapped in exam answers.

### Sec 263 — Revision of Orders Prejudicial to the Interest of Revenue
- **Key rules:**
  - CIT/PCIT/CCIT/PCCIT may call for and examine the **record** of any proceeding where the AO's/TPO's order is both **(a) erroneous and (b) prejudicial to the interest of revenue**, and pass such revisional order as deemed fit — including enhancing, modifying, or cancelling the assessment and directing a fresh assessment (or a fresh order u/s 92CA).
  - **Opportunity of being heard** must be given to the assessee before passing the order.
  - **Time limit:** **2 years** from the end of the FY in which the original order sought to be revised was passed.
  - Order u/s 263 is **appealable to ITAT**.
  - **Partial merger:** matters already decided/considered in an appeal cannot be revised u/s 263, but other (non-appealed) matters in the same order can still be revised.
  - **"Record"** = everything on record at the time of examination by the revisional authority — not limited to what was on record when the AO/TPO passed the order (e.g., a valuation report received later can still be considered).
  - **Deemed erroneous & prejudicial (Explanation 2)** if, in the Commissioner's opinion:
    (i) the order was passed without making inquiries/verification that should have been made;
    (ii) relief was allowed without inquiring into the claim;
    (iii) the order was not made in accordance with any CBDT order/direction/instruction; or
    (iv) the order was not passed in accordance with a decision of the jurisdictional HC/SC prejudicial to the assessee, in the assessee's own case or any other person's case.
- **Concept:** a departmental safeguard against under-assessment/erroneous relief that damages revenue — distinct from Sec 264, which protects the assessee.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Where the reassessment covers only certain issues, the Sec 263 limitation for issues **not** covered by the reassessment runs from the **original assessment order**, not the reassessment order — *Industrial Development Bank of India Ltd. [2023](SC)*.
  - Once CIT(A)'s order on an issue is final and pending in appeal before ITAT, PCIT/CIT cannot invoke Sec 263 on that same issue (order merges with CIT(A)'s order) — *Fortaleza Developers (2015)(Bom.)*.
  - If proceedings are stayed by any court, the period from the stay to the date the certified copy of the vacating order is received is **excluded** from the 2-year limitation.

### Sec 264 — Revision of Other Orders (+ Sec 264A Faceless Revision)
- **Key rules:**
  - CIT/PCIT/CCIT/PCCIT may, **suo motu** or **on assessee's application**, revise any order (other than one covered by Sec 263) passed by the AO.
  - **Suo motu revision time limit:** 1 year from the date of passing of the AO's order.
  - **Application by assessee:** within 1 year from the date the assessee receives a copy of the order.
  - **Disposal time limit (where assessee applies):** within 1 year from the end of the FY in which the application was made.
  - An order **prejudicial to the assessee** cannot be passed u/s 264 — it is a taxpayer-protective revision.
  - **No appeal** lies against an order u/s 264.
  - Assessee can apply for revision u/s 264 **only if**: (i) the 30-day time limit to file appeal to JC(A)/CIT(A) has expired, or (ii) the assessee has waived the right of appeal in writing.
  - **Total merger:** an assessee cannot simultaneously pursue appeal and Sec 264 revision, even on different matters of the same order — one must be chosen.
  - **Sec 264A:** CG may notify a scheme for **Faceless Revision** of orders under both Sec 263 and Sec 264.
- **Concept:** a taxpayer's alternate, appeal-like remedy against orders that don't prejudice revenue, available only once the appeal route is foreclosed.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - If the order is subject matter of a pending appeal, it can be revised u/s 263 but **not** u/s 264.
  - Stay-period exclusion (as under Sec 263) applies equally to the Sec 264 limitation clock.

### Sec 158A — Avoiding Repetitive Appeals
- **Key rule:** where an identical question is already pending before the HC/SC for an earlier AY of the same assessee, and the same matter arises again for a subsequent year before the AO/JC(A)/CIT(A)/ITAT, the assessee may (instead of filing a fresh appeal) furnish a **declaration in Form No. 8** asking that the eventual HC/SC decision be applied to the current year. The authority may admit or reject this application.
- **Concept:** saves the assessee (and the system) the cost of parallel litigation on a point already sub judice at a higher forum.

### Sec 158AB — Identical Question of Law Pending Before HC/SC (Department-side)
- **Key rules:**
  - Where a question of law for an AY is already pending before the jurisdictional HC/SC in an earlier case decided **against the Department** (first case), and the **same question** is decided **in the assessee's favour** by JC(A)/CIT(A)/ITAT in a later case (second case), the **Collegium** may decide not to press the Department into filing a fresh appeal on that point immediately.
  - **"Collegium"** = 2 or more CCIT/PCCIT/CIT specified by CBDT.
  - On the Collegium's communication, CIT/PCIT directs the AO to file **Form No. 8A within 120 days** from receipt of the JC(A)/CIT(A)/ITAT order, stating that an appeal may be filed once the first case attains finality.
  - This deferral requires the **assessee's acceptance** that the question of law is identical; absent such acceptance, PCIT/CIT must file the appeal in the normal course.
  - If the first case is ultimately decided **in the Department's favour**, CIT/PCIT directs the AO to appeal — **to ITAT within 60 days**, **to HC within 120 days** — from the date the HC/SC order is received by CIT/PCIT.
- **Concept:** mirrors Sec 158A but from the Department's side — avoids duplicative departmental appeals while an identical legal question is already before a higher court.

### Sec 268A — Monetary Limits for Departmental Appeals
- **Key rule(s) — CBDT's current monetary (tax-effect) limits below which the Department will not file an appeal:**

| Forum | Monetary limit (tax effect) |
|---|---|
| ITAT | ₹60,00,000 |
| High Court | ₹2,00,00,000 |
| Supreme Court | ₹5,00,00,000 |

  - These limits are fixed by CBDT circular under Sec 268A to curb small-value litigation (current figures per CBDT Circular No. 5/2024 dated 15.03.2024, raising the earlier ₹50 lakh/₹1 crore/₹2 crore thresholds).
  - Non-filing of an appeal on an issue in one year/one assessee does **not** bar the Department from raising the same issue: (a) for the same assessee in another year, or (b) for another assessee in any year.
  - The assessee cannot argue that the Department has "accepted" a position merely because it did not appeal on that issue.
- **Concept:** an administrative litigation-management filter, not a substantive concession on the merits.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** the limits are **tax effect**, not total demand or total addition — compute tax effect (excluding interest/penalty unless the tax effect itself is only interest/penalty) before applying the threshold.

### Dispute Resolution Committee (DRC) — Sec 245MA
- **Key rules — constitution & composition:**
  - CG constitutes one or more DRCs, one for **every region of a Pr. CCIT**.
  - **Composition:** 3 members — **2 retired IRS officers** who held the post of CIT (or equivalent/higher) for **5 years or more**, plus **1 serving officer** not below the rank of CIT/PCIT.
  - **Term:** members appointed for **3 years**; decisions by **majority**; CG may remove a member after giving an opportunity of being heard.
  - The assessee has an **option** to opt in or out of DRC resolution.
- **Key rules — eligibility ("Specified Order"):**
  - An order specified by CBDT (draft order with variation u/s 144C(1); intimation u/s 143(1)/200A/206CB; assessment/reassessment order other than one passed on DRP directions; rectification order u/s 154 enhancing assessment/reducing loss; order u/s 201/206C(6A) treating a person as assessee-in-default).
  - **Aggregate amount of variation in the order ≤ ₹10 lakh.**
  - **Returned total income (if a return was filed) ≤ ₹50 lakh** for that year.
  - Order must **not** be based on a search (Sec 132)/requisition (Sec 132A), a survey (Sec 133A), or information received under a DTAA (Sec 90/90A).
  - **Ineligible persons:** those under preventive detention under COFEPOSA, 1974; those prosecuted and convicted under IPC/UAPA/NDPS Act/Benami Act/PMLA/Prevention of Corruption Act; those facing IT-authority-initiated prosecution (or already convicted on it); persons notified under the Special Courts (Securities Transactions) Act, 1992; and those with pending Black Money Act, 2015 proceedings for the relevant AY.
- **Key rules — application & timelines:**
  - Application in **Form No. 34BC**, within **1 month** of receiving the specified order, with a fee of **₹1,000**.
  - DRC screens the application (issuing a show-cause notice if minded to reject; hearing via video conference on request); if admitted, the assessee must, within **30 days**, submit proof of withdrawal of the pending CIT(A) appeal/DRP application (or confirm none is pending) — failing which the application may be rejected.
  - **DRC decision on the merits:** within **6 months from the end of the month in which the application is admitted** — DRC may (a) modify the variation favourably and grant penalty waiver/prosecution immunity, (b) retain the variation but still grant penalty waiver/immunity, or (c) make no modification at all — options (b) and (c) are deemed **not prejudicial** to the assessee.
  - **No appeal/reference** lies against the DRC-modified order (no CIT(A) appeal, no DRP reference).
  - **AO's follow-through (Sec 245MA(2A)):** AO must pass/modify the assessment/reassessment/recomputation order in conformity with the DRC's order **within 1 month from the end of the month in which the DRC order is received**.
  - **Immunity/penalty waiver:** granted on confirmation of payment of the demand, provided the assessee has paid tax due on returned income (if any) and cooperated with the DRC — **no immunity** if prosecution was already initiated before the application date; immunity is **withdrawn** (as if never granted) if conditions are later breached.
  - **Termination of proceedings:** DRC may terminate (after hearing the assessee) for non-cooperation, failure to respond to notices, concealment/false evidence, or failure to pay the demand — and must intimate the IT authority for further action.
- **Concept:** a faster, paper-based (video-conferencing for hearing), small-ticket alternative to the JC(A)/CIT(A) appeal route, trading finality (no further appeal) for speed and potential penalty/prosecution relief.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Both the ₹10 lakh (variation) and ₹50 lakh (returned income) caps must be satisfied — failing either makes the order ineligible for DRC.
  - DRC route and CIT(A)/DRP route are mutually exclusive once the DRC application is admitted — the assessee must withdraw the parallel appeal/DRP application.
  - Distinguish DRC (Sec 245MA, small-value, no further appeal, includes penalty/prosecution relief) from the DRP (Sec 144C, transfer-pricing/foreign-company disputes, no monetary cap, and whose directions are appealable).

### References
1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sections 246, 246A–251 (appeal to JC(A)/CIT(A)), 252–255 (ITAT, incl. 253(3)/(6), 254(2), 254(2A)), 260A–260B (High Court), 261–262 (Supreme Court), 263, 264, 264A (revision), 158A, 158AB (repetitive-appeal provisions), 268A (monetary limits for departmental appeals), and 245MA (Dispute Resolution Committee) — as amended up to Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024, for the CA Final May/Nov 2026 syllabus.
2. CBDT Circular No. 5/2024 dated 15.03.2024 — revised monetary limits for departmental appeals u/s 268A (ITAT ₹60 lakh / HC ₹2 crore / SC ₹5 crore).
3. Income-tax (Dispute Resolution Committee) Rules, 2022 (Notification-based scheme under Sec 245MA) — DRC constitution, Form 34BC application, and specified-order thresholds.
