4. ICAI Final Course Study Material — Direct Tax Laws & International Taxation, Chapter on Appeals and Revision / Dispute Resolution Committee (relevant assessment-year edition), used to cross-check time limits, fee slabs, and case-law summaries.
5. Case laws as cited inline: Pepsi Foods Ltd. (stay-of-demand third proviso to Sec 254(2A) — forum/year flagged for verification), Ritha Sabapathy (Mad.), Earnest Exports Ltd. (Bom.)/Lachman Dass Bhatia Hingwala (Delhi), Reliance Telecom Ltd. (2022)(SC), Meghalaya Steels Ltd. (2015)(SC), Sunil Vasudeva v. Sundar Gupta (2019)(SC), A.A. Estate Pvt. Ltd. (2019)(SC), Spinacom India (P.) Ltd. [2018](SC), Fortaleza Developers (2015)(Bom.), Industrial Development Bank of India Ltd. [2023](SC), SAP Labs India Pvt. Ltd. [2023](SC).

## 14. Miscellaneous Provisions, Penalties, Prosecutions & The Black Money Act, 2015
> **Where it fits:** the "clean-up" chapter — cash-transaction curbs (269SS/269ST/269T/269SU), deemed-income sections (68–69D), reporting/administrative provisions, the penalty & prosecution code of the Income-tax Act, and the parallel Black Money Act, 2015 for undisclosed foreign income/assets. High yield for objective-type and 4–6 mark questions.

### Cash Transaction Restrictions — Sec. 269SS, 269ST, 269T, 269SU

- **Key rule(s):**
  - **Sec. 269SS** — no person shall *take/accept* a loan, deposit, or advance in relation to immovable property, otherwise than by account payee cheque/DD/prescribed electronic mode, if the amount is **₹20,000 or more** (including the outstanding unpaid balance of earlier such loan/deposit/advance on that date).
    - Relaxed limit of **₹2,00,000** for deposits/loans between a **Primary Agricultural Credit Society (PACS)/Primary Co-operative Agriculture & Rural Development Bank (PCARD)** and its members.
    - Not applicable to: Government, Banking company/co-op bank, Post Office savings bank, Government company, persons with only agricultural income (both parties), corporations established under a Central/State/Provincial Act, and any class notified by CBDT.
  - **Sec. 269T** — no person shall *repay* a loan/deposit (with interest) or an advance in relation to immovable property otherwise than by account payee cheque/DD/prescribed electronic mode, if the amount is **₹20,000 or more** (including outstanding balance on that date). Exceptions similar to 269SS (excluding the PACS/agriculturist carve-outs).
  - **Sec. 269ST** — no person shall *receive* an amount of **₹2,00,000 or more**, otherwise than by account payee cheque/DD/prescribed electronic mode:
    (a) in aggregate from a person in a day; or (b) in respect of a single transaction; or (c) in respect of transactions relating to one event/occasion from a person.
  - **Sec. 269SU** — a person carrying on business with turnover **exceeding ₹50 crore** in the immediately preceding year must provide facility for accepting payment through prescribed electronic modes (RuPay Debit Card, UPI, UPI QR Code — Notification 105/2019).
- **Penalties:**

$$\text{Penalty u/s } 271D \, (\text{for } 269SS \text{ default}) = 100\% \text{ of the loan/deposit/advance}$$
$$\text{Penalty u/s } 271E \, (\text{for } 269T \text{ default}) = 100\% \text{ of the amount repaid in contravention}$$
$$\text{Penalty u/s } 271DA \, (\text{for } 269ST \text{ default}) = 100\% \text{ of the amount received}$$
$$\text{Penalty u/s } 271DB \, (\text{for } 269SU \text{ default}) = ₹5{,}000 \text{ per day of continuing failure}$$

- Levying authority: Joint Commissioner; **w.e.f. 1.4.2025 (Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024) shifted to the Assessing Officer** for 271D, 271DA, 271DB and 271E.
- No penalty u/s 271DA if the person proves reasonable cause for the contravention.
- **Concept:** These sections plug cash-based tax evasion at the loan/deposit/receipt stage; the counterparty giving/repaying cash, and the recipient receiving cash, both attract independent code sections.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Aggregate the ₹20,000 test with the *outstanding unpaid* balance of prior loans/deposits between the same two persons — a fresh ₹15,000 cash loan can still violate 269SS if an old ₹10,000 balance is unpaid.
  - 269ST tests three independent limbs (per day/per transaction/per occasion) — splitting one bill into cash instalments across several days still violates limb (c) (single "occasion", e.g. a wedding) — *Mr Kejriwal hospital bill* type facts.
  - Case law: cash advances between a firm and its own partner are not necessarily hit by 269SS if bona fide (*V. Sivakumar* (Mad.)); repayment of loan by book/adjustment entry does not violate 269T if genuine (*Triumph International Finance* (Bom.)); genuineness/bona fides can constitute "reasonable cause" against 271D/271E (*Muthoot Financiers* (Del.)).
- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Account payee cheque/DD | Cheque/DD crossed "A/c Payee" — cannot be endorsed to a third party |
| Advance in relation to immovable property | Any advance (whether or not it becomes refundable) taken in connection with transfer of an immovable property |

### Deemed Income — Sec. 68 to 69D

- **Key rule(s):**
  - **Sec. 68 (Cash credit):** unexplained sum credited in books → deemed income of that PY. For a **loan/borrowing**, the explanation is deemed unsatisfactory unless *both* the assessee and the creditor (in whose name the credit is recorded) explain nature & source satisfactorily. For a **closely held company's share application money/capital/premium**, the resident share-subscriber must also explain source — *except* where the subscriber is a SEBI-registered Venture Capital Fund/Company.
  - **Sec. 69:** unexplained investments not recorded in books, with no/unsatisfactory explanation → deemed income.
  - **Sec. 69A:** assessee found owner of money/bullion/jewellery/valuable article not recorded in books, with no/unsatisfactory explanation → deemed income.
  - **Sec. 69B:** investment/acquisition amount recorded in books is *less* than actually spent, difference unexplained → deemed income of the excess.
  - **Sec. 69C:** unexplained expenditure → deemed income; such deemed income is **not allowed as a deduction under any head**.
  - **Sec. 69D:** amount borrowed/repaid on a *hundi* otherwise than by account payee cheque → deemed income of the borrower/repayer in the year of borrowing/repayment (no double taxation on subsequent repayment of an amount already taxed as income).
  - **Tax rate — Sec. 115BBE:**

$$\text{Tax on income u/s } 68\text{–}69D = 60\% + 25\% \text{ surcharge (on tax)} + 4\% \text{ HEC} = \textbf{78\%} \text{ effective}$$

  No deduction for any expenditure/allowance/set-off of loss is permitted against such income.
- **Concept:** These are anti-evasion deeming fictions shifting the onus onto the assessee to explain the nature and source of unrecorded credits/assets/expenditure; failure results in taxation at a steep flat 78% rate rather than slab/normal rates.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Sec. 68 has a *higher* bar for share capital/premium of closely held companies (post-2012 amendment) — even VC Fund/Company exception does not extend to the general "closely held company" onus.
  - Sec. 69C expenditure once deemed income can never be claimed as a deduction — a favourite trick MCQ.
  - Additional 10% penalty under **Sec. 271AAC** applies on tax payable u/s 115BBE(1) where such income is unexplained/not disclosed appropriately; note that **Sec. 270A does not apply once 271AAC is levied**.

### Certain Transfers to be Void & Provisional Attachment — Sec. 281, 281B

- **Key rule(s):**
  - **Sec. 281:** where tax/penalty/interest/fine **exceeding ₹5,000** is payable and the assessee charges or transfers any asset **exceeding ₹10,000** in value during the pendency of proceedings (till service of TRO notice), such charge/transfer is void against the tax claim — *unless* (a) it is of stock-in-trade of the business, or (b) made for adequate consideration without notice of the pending proceedings/sum due, or (c) with prior AO approval.
  - **Sec. 281B:** AO may provisionally attach any property of the assessee during pendency of assessment/reassessment proceedings, or for penalty u/s 271AAD where the penalty likely to be imposed exceeds **₹2 crore**, with prior approval of PCCIT/CCIT/PCIT/CIT (or PDGIT/DGIT/PDIT/DIT). Attachment is valid for **6 months** from the order, extendable up to **2 years**, or **60 days after completion of assessment proceedings**, whichever is later. Assessee may substitute a bank guarantee; AO must revoke provisional attachment within **15 days** of receiving it.
- **Concept:** Sec. 281 is a self-operating anti-avoidance rule protecting revenue's charge over assessee assets during litigation; Sec. 281B is a discretionary, higher-authority-sanctioned protective attachment power.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - A transfer void u/s 281 still requires the AO/Department to establish it through a civil suit under the Transfer of Property Act — the AO **cannot unilaterally declare a sale deed void** (*Manoj Kabra*, All. HC).
  - Remember the outer time cap for provisional attachment: 2 years OR 60 days post-assessment completion — **whichever is later**, not earlier.

### Reporting Obligations — SFT, AIS & Crypto Reporting

- **Key rule(s):**
  - **Sec. 285B:** film/OTT/event-management producers must file **Form 52A** with DGIT(Systems) within **60 days from end of PY**, disclosing payments **exceeding ₹50,000** in aggregate to each engaged person.
  - **Sec. 285BA — Statement of Financial Transaction (SFT):** specified reporting persons (banks, registrars, companies issuing shares/bonds, mutual fund trustees, property registrars, tax-audit assessees, etc.) must file SFT by **31st May** following the FY. Key thresholds: cash deposits/withdrawals in current accounts ≥ **₹50 lakh**; cash deposits in other accounts / time deposits / share & bond subscriptions / buybacks / MF units / forex sale ≥ **₹10 lakh**; cash payment for bank drafts/pre-paid instruments ≥ **₹10 lakh**; credit card bill payments ≥ **₹1 lakh cash** or **₹10 lakh** other mode; immovable property transactions ≥ **₹30 lakh** (or SDV ≥ ₹30 lakh); cash receipt for sale of goods/services by a tax-audit assessee > **₹2 lakh**.
  - **Sec. 285BB:** Annual Information Statement (AIS) to be uploaded in Form 26AS within **3 months from end of the month** the information is received.
  - **Sec. 285BAA** *(inserted by Finance Act 2025, w.e.f. AY 2026-27)*: prescribed reporting entities to report crypto-asset transactions in the prescribed form/manner; defective statement correctable within **30 days**; inaccuracies discovered later to be corrected within **10 days**.
  - **Penalties:**

$$\text{Sec. 271FA (delay in SFT filing)} = ₹500/\text{day up to notice expiry}; \; ₹1{,}000/\text{day thereafter}$$
$$\text{Sec. 271FAA (inaccurate SFT)} = ₹50{,}000 \; (+\, ₹5{,}000 \text{ per reportable account if inaccuracy traceable to account holder})$$

- **Concept:** This is the Department's data-gathering net (specified high-value transactions) feeding pre-filled returns and AIS/AS-26 — distinct from TDS/TCS reporting.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - SFT limit is applied **separately** to deposits and withdrawals (₹50 lakh each), and reporting person must aggregate across **all accounts of like nature** held by the same person during the FY.
  - Loan repayment instalments to an NBFC/HFC — **each instalment is a separate "single transaction"**, not aggregated (CBDT clarification) — a common trap for 269ST-type reasoning carried into SFT MCQs.

### Authorised Representative & Validity of Proceedings — Sec. 288, 292B, 292BB

- **Key rule(s):** Sec. 288 lists eligible Authorised Representatives — employee, bank officer (of the bank where assessee has a/c), legal practitioner, Chartered Accountant, holders of CBDT-recognised accountancy qualifications (CS/CMA etc.), commerce/law graduates from CBDT-approved universities, and any other prescribed person.
  - **Sec. 292B:** a return/assessment/notice/summons is not invalid merely for a mistake, defect, or omission if it is, in substance, in conformity with the Act's intent.
  - **Sec. 292BB:** if the assessee has appeared/co-operated in proceedings, notice is deemed validly served (and the objection that it was not served/served late/served improperly is barred) — **unless the objection is raised before completion of assessment/reassessment**.
- **Concept:** Curative/deeming provisions protecting revenue proceedings from technical challenge, subject to the assessee's timely objection right.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Sec. 292B does **not** cure a jurisdictional defect — issuing a notice on a non-existent amalgamated entity is void ab initio, and mere participation does not cure it (*Maruti Suzuki India Ltd.*, SC).
  - Sec. 292BB does **not** cure non-issuance of a mandatory notice u/s 143(2) even with full participation (*Laxman Das Khandelwal*, SC) — 292BB cures defects in *service*, not complete *non-issuance* of a jurisdictional notice.

### Penalty for Under-Reporting/Misreporting of Income — Sec. 270A, 270AA, 273A

- **Key formula(s):**

$$\text{Penalty (under-reporting)} = 50\% \times \text{Tax payable on Under-Reported Income (URI)}$$
$$\text{Penalty (mis-reporting)} = 200\% \times \text{Tax payable on URI}$$

$$\text{First assessment: } URI = \text{Assessed income} - \text{Returned income (or Basic Exemption Limit if no return filed)}$$

$$\text{Reassessment: } URI = \text{Reassessed income} - \text{Income assessed/reassessed in the immediately preceding order}$$
$$\text{Tax on URI (reassessment)} = \text{Tax on (URI + last assessed income)} - \text{Tax on last assessed income}$$

  Losses claimed reduced/converted to income:
  $$URI = (\text{Loss claimed} - \text{Loss assessed/reassessed}) \; \text{or} \; (\text{Loss claimed} - \text{Income assessed/reassessed})$$
  — tax computed treating URI as if it were the total income.

  MAT/AMT cases (Sec. 115JB/115JC):
$$URI = (A-B) + (C-D)$$
  where A/B are total income assessed under general provisions before/after excluding URI, and C/D are deemed total income assessed under 115JB/115JC before/after excluding URI; if the URI in B and D are identical, it is **not counted twice** (excluded from D).
- **Key rule(s) — Mis-reporting instances (Sec. 270A(9)):** misrepresentation/suppression of facts; failure to record investments in books; unsubstantiated expenditure claims; false entries in books; failure to record receipts having a bearing on total income; failure to report an international transaction under transfer pricing.
  - **Exclusions from "under-reported income" (Sec. 270A(6)):** bona fide explanation with full disclosure; estimation-based additions where books are correct/complete but income can't properly be deduced; assessee's own lower self-estimated disallowance with full disclosure; TP additions in conformity with TPO's ALP where Sec. 92D documentation/disclosure was maintained.
  - **Sec. 270AA — Immunity from penalty (270A) & prosecution:** available only for **under-reporting** (not mis-reporting), if the assessee pays tax + interest per the demand notice within the time limit and does **not** file an appeal. Application to AO within **1 month** from end of month of receipt of order; AO to dispose within **3 months** from end of month of receipt of application, after hearing.
  - **Sec. 273A — Waiver/reduction of penalty by PCIT/CIT:** conditions — voluntary & full disclosure in good faith before detection, co-operation in enquiry, and payment of tax + interest in full. Relief available **only once in the assessee's lifetime**. ⚠️ VERIFY — OCR states CIT/PCIT can waive without higher approval where income is up to ₹5 lakh, and needs CCIT/PCCIT/DGIT approval above ₹5 lakh; this appears to be an administrative/circular-based monetary limit rather than a figure appearing in bare Sec. 273A text — confirm current CBDT instruction figure before quoting in an exam answer.
- **Concept:** Sec. 270A replaced the earlier concealment penalty (old Sec. 271(1)(c)) with a two-tier (under-reporting/mis-reporting) structure and a menu of statutory carve-outs plus an immunity route.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Immunity u/s 270AA is a one-way street — filing an appeal (even on an unrelated ground) after seeking immunity forfeits it; misreporting can **never** get 270AA immunity.

### General Penalty Code — Key Sections (271A–271K, 221)

- **Key rule(s):**

| Section | Default | Quantum | Who levies |
|---|---|---|---|
| 221(1) | Failure to pay self-assessment tax/demand/TDS/TCS | Up to amount of tax in arrears | AO |
| 271A | Failure to keep/maintain/retain books u/s 44AA | ₹25,000 | AO, JC(A), CIT(A) |
| 271AA / 271G | TP documentation defaults | 2% of transaction value | AO, CIT(A) |
| 271AAC | Deemed income u/s 68–69C not appropriately disclosed | 10% of tax u/s 115BBE | AO, JC(A), CIT(A) |
| 271AAD | False entry / omitted entry to evade tax | 100% of the false/omitted entry | AO, JC(A), CIT(A) |
| 271AAE | Trust/institution benefit to related person u/s 13(1) | 100% (1st violation) / 200% (subsequent) | AO |
| 271B | Failure to get accounts audited u/s 44AB | 0.5% of turnover (max **₹1,50,000**) | AO |
| 271BA | TP audit report (Form 3CEB) not furnished u/s 92E | ₹1,00,000 | AO |
| 271C | Failure to deduct/pay TDS incl. u/s 194B/194R/194S/194BA | 100% of tax not deducted/paid | JC [AO w.e.f. 1.4.2025] |
| 271CA | Failure to collect TCS | 100% of tax not collected | JC [AO w.e.f. 1.4.2025] |
| 271J | Incorrect info in report/certificate by CA/Merchant Banker/Registered Valuer | ₹10,000 per report | AO, JC(A), CIT(A) |
| 271K | Sec. 35/80G institution fails to file statement/certificate | ₹10,000 to ₹1,00,000 | AO |

- **Concept:** Consolidated table of standalone/procedural penalties distinct from the 270A income-concealment framework and the 269SS/ST/T cash-transaction penalties.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Sec. 271C: penalty is for **failure to deduct**, not for a delay in depositing tax already deducted — belated remittance after correct deduction is **not** penalisable u/s 271C (*US Technologies International*, SC).
  - 271AAC's 10% additional levy sits **on top of** (not instead of) the 78% tax under 115BBE, but Sec. 270A is expressly excluded once 271AAC applies to the same income.

### Prosecutions under the Income-tax Act — Sec. 275A to 278A

- **Key rule(s):**

| Section | Default | Punishment |
|---|---|---|
| 275A | Contravention of order of deemed seizure/restraint u/s 132(2) | Up to 2 years + fine |
| 275B | Failure to facilitate inspection of books u/s 132(1)(iib) | Up to 2 years + fine |
| 276 | Removal/concealment/transfer of property to thwart tax recovery | Up to 2 years + fine |
| 276B | Failure to pay TDS/TCS or ensure payment u/s 194B/194R/194S/194BA | 3 months to 7 years + fine |
| 276C(1) | Wilful attempt to evade tax/penalty/interest or under-report income | Evasion > **₹25 lakh**: 6 months–7 years; else 3 months–2 years, + fine |
| 276C(2) | Wilful attempt to evade payment of tax/penalty/interest | 3 months to 2 years + fine (court's discretion) |
| 276CC | Wilful failure to furnish ROI in due date u/s 139(1)/142(1)(i)/148 | Evasion > ₹25 lakh: 6 months–7 years; else 3 months–2 years, + fine |
| 276D | Wilful failure to produce accounts/documents u/s 142(1)/142(2A) | Up to 1 year + fine |
| 277 | False statement in verification | Evasion > ₹25 lakh: 6 months–7 years; else 3 months–2 years, + fine |
| 277A | Falsification of books/documents to abet tax evasion | 3 months to 2 years + fine |
| 278 | Abetment of false return | Evasion > ₹25 lakh: 6 months–7 years; else 3 months–2 years, + fine |
| 278A | Second/subsequent offence u/s 276B, 276BB, 276C(1), 276CC, 277, 278 | 6 months to 7 years + fine (each subsequent offence) |

- **Concept:** Custodial-liability layer over and above the penalty code — reserved for *wilful* defaults; the ₹25 lakh threshold determines the severity band under most evasion-linked sections.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - **276CC exceptions:** no prosecution if the return u/s 139(1) is furnished before expiry of the AY, or an updated return u/s 139(8A) is furnished within its time limit, or tax payable by a non-company assessee (net of TDS/TCS/advance tax/self-assessment tax paid before AY expiry) is **up to ₹10,000**.
  - Prosecution requires an actual/attempted tax liability — mere unearthing of an unaccounted transaction in a search does not automatically trigger prosecution unless a tax/penalty/interest liability is established (*D.K. Shivakumar*, Kar. HC).
  - CBDT administrative guidance: prosecution u/s 276B/276BB ordinarily **not** initiated if the TDS/TCS default does not exceed ₹25 lakh and delay is under 60 days, except habitual defaulters with Collegium (two CCIT/DGIT-rank officer) approval (*AT-Dev Prabha JV*, SC-noted CBDT circular position). Failure to furnish return not wilful → no 276CC prosecution (*Bhavecha Machinery*, MP HC).

### The Black Money Act, 2015 — Charge, Definitions & Scope

- **Key rule(s):**
  - Full title: **The Black Money (Undisclosed Foreign Income and Assets) and Imposition of Tax Act, 2015**; enacted 26.5.2015; applies to whole of India, **w.e.f. AY 2016-17**.
  - **Sec. 3 — Charging section:**

$$\text{Tax} = 30\% \times \text{Undisclosed Foreign Income \& Asset value (no slab, no deduction/exemption/set-off)}$$

    An undisclosed foreign asset is taxed in the **PY in which it comes to the notice of the AO** (irrespective of the year of acquisition).
  - **Sec. 2(2) — "Assessee":** a person resident in India (per Sec. 6, Income-tax Act) in the relevant PY, **or** a person who is resident but not ordinarily resident (RNOR)/non-resident in the PY but was resident either in the PY to which the undisclosed income relates, or in the PY in which the undisclosed foreign asset was acquired.
  - **Sec. 2(11)/2(12):** "Undisclosed asset located outside India" = a foreign asset (incl. financial interest in an entity) held by/beneficially owned by the assessee, for which no or an unsatisfactory explanation of source of investment is given. "Undisclosed foreign income & asset" = undisclosed foreign-source income + value of undisclosed foreign assets.
  - **Sec. 4 — Scope:** total undisclosed foreign income & asset = (i) foreign-source income not disclosed in a return filed u/s 139(1)/(4)/(5) of the Income-tax Act; (ii) foreign-source income where no return/belated/revised return was filed at all though required; (iii) value of any undisclosed foreign asset. Income already assessed/reassessed under specified Income-tax Act provisions (Sec. 29, 43C, 57, 59, 92C) is **not** re-included; conversely, income/asset taxed under the BMA is **not** again included under the Income-tax Act (mutual exclusivity).
  - **Sec. 5 — Computation:** no expenditure or set-off of loss against undisclosed foreign income. Where an asset is acquired partly from income already taxed ("white money") under the Income-tax Act or BMA, that portion is excluded from the current valuation:
    $$\text{Undisclosed value (immovable property)} = \text{Current FMV} - \left(\text{Current FMV} \times \frac{\text{White money invested}}{\text{Total cost of asset}}\right)$$
- **Concept:** A separate, parallel taxing code (not part of the Income-tax Act) exclusively for undisclosed *foreign* income/assets of residents, with a flat penal rate and its own procedural/penalty/prosecution machinery.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - The RNOR/NR "assessee" limb is frequently tested — a person NR in the year the asset is *discovered* can still be liable if he was **resident** in the year the asset was **acquired** or the income arose.
  - Procedural provisions (Sections 6–88) largely mirror the Income-tax Act machinery (search, assessment, appeals, recovery) — don't expect a wholly separate procedural code.

### Black Money Act — Valuation of Undisclosed Foreign Assets (Rule 3)

- **Key formula(s) — value = higher of Cost of Acquisition or FMV on valuation date (unless otherwise specified):**

$$\text{Bullion/jewellery/precious stone/artistic work} = \max(\text{Cost of Acquisition},\ \text{Net Realisable Value (NRV) on valuation date})$$
$$\text{Quoted shares/securities} = \max\Big(\text{Cost},\ \text{Average of lowest \& highest price on valuation date (or preceding trading day)}\Big)$$
$$\text{Unquoted equity shares} = \max\left(\text{Cost},\ \frac{(A + B - L)}{PE} \times PV\right)$$
$$\text{Unquoted shares/securities (non-equity)} = \max(\text{Cost},\ \text{NRV on valuation date})$$
$$\text{Immovable property} = \max(\text{Cost},\ \text{NRV on valuation date})$$
$$\text{Bank account} = \sum \text{deposits since account opening (or since prior BMA declaration, if any)}$$
$$\text{Interest in Firm/LLP/AOP/BOI} = \text{Net worth} (A+B-L),\ \text{first allocated by capital contribution ratio, balance by dissolution/PSR ratio}$$
$$\text{Any other asset} = \max(\text{Cost},\ \text{NRV on valuation date})$$

  Where A = book value of assets (excluding those separately valued under B, and excluding TDS/advance tax net of refund, and deferred expenditure); B = FMV of bullion/jewellery/shares/securities/immovable property per this Rule; L = book value of liabilities *excluding* paid-up equity capital, dividend-payment reserves, reserves/surplus (however named, even if negative, other than depreciation reserves), tax provision, provisions for unascertained liabilities, and contingent liabilities (other than cumulative preference dividend arrears); PE = total paid-up equity share capital; PV = paid-up value of the shares being valued.
  - **Rule 3(2) — asset transferred before valuation date:** $\max(\text{Cost},\ \text{Sale value})$; if transferred without/inadequate consideration: $\max(\text{Cost},\ \text{FMV on date of transfer})$.
  - **Rule 3(3):** where a new asset is acquired using sale proceeds of an old asset or bank withdrawal, the FMV of that old asset/bank balance is **not separately added again** (avoids double counting — the "roll-forward" rule).
  - **Rule 3(4)/3(5) — currency conversion:** RBI reference rate on the valuation date; if unavailable, convert to US$ first, then US$ to ₹ at RBI reference rate.
  - **Valuation date:** **1st July 2015** for assets declared under the one-time compliance window (Sec. 59); **1st April of the relevant PY** in all other cases.
- **Concept:** A codified, asset-class-wise FMV mechanism (broadly "higher of cost or current value"), with an anti-double-counting roll-forward rule for reinvested proceeds.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Always apply Rule 3(3) before finalising values when an asset has been "rolled over" (sale of Asset A → reinvested into Asset B) — the source asset's value is reduced by the amount reinvested, not counted twice.
  - "Established securities market" and "quoted share" definitions carry precise annual-trading-value (**>US$1 billion for 3 preceding calendar years**) and volume (**≥10% of average shares outstanding, traded on ≥60 business days**) tests — worth memorising as objective-type traps.

### Black Money Act — Penal Provisions (Sec. 41–45)

- **Key rule(s):**

$$\text{Sec. 41 — additional penalty} = 3 \times \text{Tax computed on undisclosed foreign income/asset (in addition to the tax itself)}$$
$$\text{Sec. 42 — failure to furnish return of foreign income/asset} = ₹10\text{ lakh}$$
$$\text{Sec. 43 — failure to furnish/inaccurate particulars of foreign asset in ROI} = ₹10\text{ lakh}$$
$$\text{Sec. 44 — default in payment of tax arrears} = 100\% \text{ of tax arrears}$$
$$\text{Sec. 45 — failure to answer/sign statement/produce documents (Sec. 8 summons)} = ₹50{,}000 \text{ to } ₹2\text{ lakh}$$

  - **Relief (inserted by Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024, w.e.f. 1.10.2024):** Sections 42 & 43 penalties **do not apply** to any foreign asset **other than immovable property** where the aggregate value of such asset(s) does not exceed **₹20 lakh**.
- **Concept:** Sec. 41's 300% additional-tax penalty (effectively ~120% of asset value on top of the 30% tax) is the headline exposure; Sec. 42/43 address non-disclosure/inaccurate-disclosure failures independent of whether tax was ultimately payable, now moderated by the ₹20 lakh de minimis carve-out for small foreign holdings (e.g., small foreign bank balances, modest ESOP/RSU holdings) — a relief measure widely publicised for genuine, low-value non-wilful omissions by resident individuals.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - The ₹20 lakh threshold under the 2024 amendment protects against Sec. 42/43 **only** — it does **not** exempt the asset from the Sec. 3 charge (30% tax) or the Sec. 41 penalty if undisclosed income/tax liability is otherwise established; and it **excludes** immovable property (i.e., an undisclosed foreign house, however small in value, does not get this relief).
  - Distinguish Sec. 41 (tax-linked, 3x tax) from Sec. 42/43 (flat ₹10 lakh, disclosure-failure linked, independent of quantum of tax) — a common conceptual mix-up in exam answers.

### References
1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sections 68–69D, 221, 269SS/269ST/269T/269SU, 270A, 270AA, 271A–271K, 273A, 275A–278A, 281, 281B, 285B, 285BA, 285BAA, 285BB, 288, 292B, 292BB, 115BBE (as amended up to Finance Act, 2025), consolidated per CA Bhanwar Borana's DT Compact Book (source concept-book material for this chapter).
2. The Black Money (Undisclosed Foreign Income and Assets) and Imposition of Tax Act, 2015, and Rule 3 of the Black Money Rules, 2015 (valuation of undisclosed foreign assets).
3. Finance Act, 2024 / Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024 — amendments shifting penalty-levying authority (271D/271DA/271DB/271E/271C/271CA) from Joint Commissioner to Assessing Officer (w.e.f. 1.4.2025) and inserting the ₹20 lakh de minimis threshold under Sections 42/43 of the Black Money Act (w.e.f. 1.10.2024).
4. Supreme Court/High Court rulings as cited inline: *PCIT v. Maruti Suzuki India Ltd.* (2019 SC), *Laxman Das Khandelwal* (2019 SC), *US Technologies International Pvt. Ltd.* (2023 SC), *V. Sivakumar* (2013 Mad.), *Triumph International Finance (I.) Ltd.* (2012 Bom.), *Muthoot Financiers* (2015 Del.), *D.K. Shivakumar* (2021 Kar.), *Bhavecha Machinery* (2010 MP).
5. ICAI Final Course Study Material — Direct Tax Laws & International Taxation, relevant chapters on Miscellaneous Provisions, Penalties, Prosecution, and the Black Money Act (for cross-checking statutory structure applicable to the current syllabus/AY).

## 15. GAAR, Taxation of VDA & Exempt Income

> **Where it fits:** Three distinct "closing" topics of the DT syllabus — GAAR (Chapter X-A, Sec 95–102 & 144BA) is the anti-abuse rule that can override a transaction's legal form (and even overrides DTAA); Sec 115BBH/194S tax the new asset class of Virtual Digital Assets (crypto/NFTs) at a flat, loss-ring-fenced 30%; and Sec 10 + Sec 14A govern what income escapes tax altogether and what expenditure gets disallowed for earning it.

---

### A. Tax Planning vs Avoidance vs Evasion vs Management

- **Key rule(s)/concept:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Tax Planning | Reducing tax liability by legitimately using concessions/exemptions in law (e.g., investment u/s 80C, reinvestment u/s 54/54EC) |
| Tax Avoidance | Taking undue advantage of loopholes/drafting gaps — follows the letter but kills the spirit of law (e.g., sale-and-leaseback of an asset to shift depreciation while retaining the asset) |
| Tax Evasion | Illegal reduction of tax via suppression of facts, falsification, fraud (e.g., booking bogus expenses) — attracts penalty/prosecution |
| Tax Management | Ensuring compliance/procedural obligations are met properly (e.g., timely advance tax to avoid interest, timely return filing for early refund) |

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - GAAR targets **tax avoidance** (legal form, abusive substance) — not evasion (which is dealt with under penalty/prosecution provisions), so don't conflate the two in a discussion answer.

---

### B. GAAR — Applicability (Sec 95) & Overriding Effect

- **Key rule(s):**
  - Chapter X-A (GAAR) provisions apply **in addition to, or in lieu of**, any other basis of determining tax liability; Specific Anti-Avoidance Rules (SAAR) — e.g., Sec 40A(2), Sec 94A, Sec 2(22)(e), Transfer Pricing provisions — continue to apply in their respective cases.
  - **GAAR overrides the DTAA** — Sec 95 opens with a non-obstante clause overriding conflicting provisions elsewhere in the Act (and treaty relief under Sec 90/90A).
  - GAAR is applicable **from AY 2018-19** onward.
  - **Monetary threshold:** GAAR provisions apply only where the **tax benefit, in aggregate, to all parties to the arrangement in a relevant previous year exceeds ₹3 crore** (prescribed under Rule 10U).
  - **GAAR not applicable to:**
    - A Foreign Institutional Investor (FII/FPI) which has invested in securities (listed/unlisted, with prior permission of the competent authority), **has not taken any benefit under a DTAA**, and is an assessee under the Act.
    - Income accruing to a non-resident from investment in **offshore derivative instruments** issued by an FII.

- **Concept:** Sec 95 is the "trigger" section — it declares that an arrangement *may* be declared an Impermissible Avoidance Arrangement (IAA) and its tax consequences re-determined under this Chapter; the actual test is in Sec 96/97, and the procedure is in Sec 144BA.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Non-obstante clause = GAAR prevails over *every* conflicting provision, including treaty benefits — a favourite trick statement in MCQs/theory.
  - The ₹3 crore threshold is tested **in aggregate across all parties**, not per party.

---

### C. Impermissible Avoidance Arrangement — IAA (Sec 96)

- **Key rule(s):** An arrangement is an IAA only if **both** limbs are satisfied:
  1. Its **main purpose, or one of the main purposes**, is to obtain a tax benefit; **AND**
  2. It does at least one of the following:
     - creates rights/obligations not ordinarily created between persons dealing at arm's length; **or**
     - results, directly or indirectly, in misuse or abuse of the provisions of the Act; **or**
     - is entered into/carried out in a manner not ordinarily employed for bona fide purposes; **or**
     - lacks commercial substance, or is **deemed** to lack commercial substance (per below).

- **Concept:** GAAR is a "purpose + effect" test — tax-benefit motive alone is not enough; one of the four abusive-effect conditions must also be present.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Remember it is "**main purpose or one of the main purposes**" — need not be the *sole* purpose for the arrangement to be caught.

---

### D. Deemed Lack of Commercial Substance (Sec 97)

- **Key rule(s):** An arrangement shall be **deemed to lack commercial substance** if:

| # | Situation | Illustration |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Substance differs significantly from legal Form | Transaction dressed up as "sale and lease-back" but is in substance a sham |
| 2 | Location of asset/transaction/residence chosen **only** to obtain tax benefit, with no substantial commercial purpose | A Ltd. (Netherlands) and B Ltd. (Hong Kong) route a transaction through conduit C Ltd. in a tax haven |
| 3 | Arrangement does not significantly affect business risk or net cash flow of any party but attributes a tax benefit | X Ltd. (in a tax-holiday zone) leases P&M from a sister concern at ₹4 crore and sub-leases it to another sister concern at ₹10 crore |
| 4(i) | **Round-tripping of funds** — a series of transactions transferring funds among parties with no substantial commercial purpose other than obtaining a tax benefit (direct nexus of funds, or the time/sequence of transfer, is irrelevant) | Group company borrows from market, routes it as interest-free loan to a sister concern, calling it "business purpose" |
| 4(ii) | Involvement of an **accommodating party** — a party whose main reason for participating is to (directly/indirectly) secure a tax benefit (irrespective of whether it is an associated person) | A Ltd. sells shares to subsidiary B Ltd. at a low price (booking a loss); B Ltd. sells in the market at a high price (booking a profit) — B Ltd. is the accommodating party |
| 4(iii) | Elements that **offset or cancel** each other | Cross-transfers under the Clubbing provisions |
| 4(iv) | Transaction routed through one/more persons to **disguise** value/location/source/ownership/control of funds | Share capital invested in an Indian company from Mauritius with the real source of funds undisclosed |

  - **Irrelevant** in deciding whether a transaction lacks commercial substance: (a) the period/time for which the arrangement exists; (b) the fact that taxes were paid (directly/indirectly) under the arrangement; (c) the fact that an exit route (including transfer of activity/business/operations) is built into the arrangement.
  - While treating a transaction as an IAA, tax authorities may **re-characterise**: equity as debt (or vice versa); capital receipt as revenue receipt (or vice versa); and expenditure/deduction/relief/rebate.

- **Concept:** Sec 97 gives the AO/PCIT a deeming fiction — even if a transaction looks commercially motivated, it is *deemed* to lack substance if it falls in any of the listed patterns.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Payment of tax under the arrangement does **not** save it from GAAR — a common distractor in MCQs.
  - ⚠️ VERIFY — OCR groups this content under a single "Sec 96" heading; per the Income-tax Act, the IAA definition is Sec 96 and the deemed-lack-of-commercial-substance rules are a **separate Sec 97** — treated separately above for accuracy.

---

### E. Consequences of an IAA (Sec 98)

- **Key rule(s):** Once an arrangement is declared an IAA, consequences are determined "as deemed appropriate in the circumstances of the case" and may include (illustrative, not exhaustive):
  - (a) disregarding, combining, or re-characterising any step/part/whole of the IAA;
  - (b) treating the IAA as if it had not been entered into/carried out;
  - (c) disregarding any accommodating party, or treating the accommodating party and another party as one and the same person (treating it as **benami**);
  - (d) treating connected persons as one and the same person for determining tax treatment of an amount (treating them as **benami** holding concerns);
  - (e) reallocating amongst the parties any accrual/receipt of a capital or revenue nature, or any expenditure/deduction/relief/rebate;
  - (f) re-characterising the place of residence of a party, or the location/status of an asset or transaction, other than as provided under the arrangement;
  - (g) looking through any arrangement by **disregarding a corporate structure** (lifting the corporate veil/disregarding the alter-ego).
  - The overall effect may be **denial of a tax benefit or of a treaty (DTAA) benefit**.

- **Concept:** Sec 98 is deliberately open-ended/illustrative so the tax authority can neutralise the tax advantage in whatever manner fits the abusive arrangement.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Exam answers should use the phrase "consequences shall be determined in such manner **as is deemed appropriate**" — the list in Sec 98 is illustrative, not exhaustive.

---

### F. Key Definitions (Sec 102)

- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Arrangement | Any step in, or part or whole of, a transaction/operation/scheme/agreement/understanding — covers arrangements whether legally enforceable or not |
| Associated Person — Individual | Same meaning as "relative" u/s 56(2)(x) |
| Associated Person — HUF/Company/Firm/AOP/BOI/others | Same meaning as under Sec 40A(2) (PGBP) |
| Tax benefit | (a) reduction/avoidance/deferral of tax under domestic law or a DTAA; (b) increase in a refund under domestic law/DTAA; (c) reduction in total income, or increase in a loss |
| Party | Includes a **Permanent Establishment (PE)** |

---

### G. Procedure — Sec 144BA & the Approving Panel

- **Key rule(s) — flow of the GAAR reference:**
  1. AO refers the matter to the **Principal Commissioner/Commissioner (PC/C)** at any stage of assessment/reassessment, based on material/evidence available, for declaring an arrangement an IAA.
  2. PC/C issues a notice to the assessee to submit objections/be heard within a specified period — ⚠️ VERIFY: the OCR states "not exceeding 60 days"; the statutory language in Sec 144BA is commonly cited as a **60-day** period for the assessee to respond — confirm the exact wording ("not less than"/fixed 60 days) against the bare Act before using it in a written answer.
  3. **If the assessee does not object** within time → PC/C issues such directions as deemed fit to declare the arrangement an IAA, and communicates the same to the AO in writing (copy to assessee).
  4. **If the assessee objects** and PC/C is **satisfied** with the explanation → no GAAR action; **if not satisfied** → PC/C refers the matter to the **Approving Panel (AP)**.
  5. AP gives the assessee an opportunity of being heard; may call for records, direct further inquiry by the PC/C, or require the assessee to furnish documents/evidence.
  6. AP **must issue directions** (declaring the arrangement an IAA or not, and specifying the previous years covered) within **6 months from the end of the month** in which the reference was received.
  7. AP's directions are **binding** on the assessee, the PC/C, and subordinate income-tax authorities; **no appeal lies against the AP's directions** themselves.
  8. AO completes the assessment per the AP's directions and Chapter X-A; **prior approval of the PC/C is mandatory** before passing an assessment order incorporating GAAR tax consequences.

- **Approving Panel — constitution:**
  - Constituted by the **Central Government**; may set up one or more panels.
  - **Composition:** 3 members, including a Chairperson:
    - Chairperson: a person who is, or has been, a **judge of a High Court**;
    - 1 member: an **IRS officer** not below the rank of Principal Commissioner/CIT/Chief CIT;
    - 1 member: an **academic or scholar** with special knowledge of direct taxes, business accounts, and international trade practices.
  - **Term:** ordinarily **1 year**; may be extended up to a total of **3 years**.

- **Concept:** This is a multi-layered check-and-balance — an assessee gets a hearing before the PC/C, and (if unsatisfied) a further, quasi-judicial hearing before the Approving Panel, before GAAR consequences are finally applied.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Directions of the AP are **not appealable** on their own — but the assessee can still challenge the **final assessment order** (incorporating the GAAR consequence) before appellate authorities.
  - Don't confuse the AP's composition (3 members) with other tax panels (e.g., Dispute Resolution Panel) which have a different composition.

---

### H. Sec 115BBH — Tax on Income from Transfer of VDA

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

$$
\text{Tax on income from transfer of VDA} = 30\% \times \left(\text{Sale consideration} - \text{Cost of acquisition}\right)
$$

  - Applicable **from AY 2023-24, i.e., w.e.f. 1 April 2022**.
  - **No deduction** for any expenditure or allowance is permitted (except **cost of acquisition** of the VDA); no other expense/allowance is deductible.
  - **No set-off** of loss on transfer of VDA against income from any other source, and such loss **cannot be carried forward** to subsequent years.
  - Loss from one VDA also cannot be set off against gain from another VDA (each VDA is *ring-fenced*, per CBDT clarification).

- **Concept:** VDA (crypto, NFTs, etc.) gains are taxed at a flat, high rate with no expense deduction (other than cost) and complete denial of loss set-off/carry-forward — a deliberately harsh, SAAR-style regime distinct from capital gains taxation.

- **Definitions ("Virtual Digital Asset" — Sec 2(47A)):**

| Included | Excluded (not treated as VDA) |
|---|---|
| Any information/code/number/token (not Indian or foreign currency) generated through cryptographic or other means, transferable/storable/tradable electronically | Gift cards/vouchers usable to obtain goods/services or a discount |
| Non-Fungible Token (NFT) or similar token | Mileage points/reward points/loyalty cards given without direct monetary consideration, redeemable only for goods/services/discount |
| Any other digital asset the Central Government may notify | Subscription to websites/platforms/applications |
| Crypto-asset — a digital representation of value relying on a cryptographically secured distributed ledger (or similar technology) to validate/secure transactions | NFT whose transfer results in transfer of ownership of an underlying **tangible** asset, where that transfer of ownership is legally enforceable |

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Cost of acquisition is the **only** permissible deduction — no brokerage, no exchange fee, no indexation.
  - Loss on VDA transfer is a dead loss for tax purposes — it cannot even be carried forward, unlike normal capital losses.

---

### I. Sec 194S — TDS on Payment for Transfer of VDA

- **Key rule(s)/thresholds:**

| Nature of Payment | Payer | Payee | Threshold | Rate |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Consideration for transfer of VDA | Any person | Resident | Consideration > ₹10,000 (in the FY) | 1% of consideration |

  - Effective **from 1 July 2022**.
  - **Specified persons** (payer being an **Individual/HUF**) — i.e., those with **no PGBP income**, or with business turnover/gross receipts **not exceeding ₹1 crore** (business) / **₹50 lakh** (profession) in the preceding FY — must deduct TDS only where consideration **exceeds ₹50,000** in the FY, and are **not required to obtain a TAN**.
  - Such a specified person (Ind/HUF) must pay the TDS within **30 days from the end of the month** of deduction, along with a statement in **Form 26QE**.
  - Where consideration is **wholly/partly in kind**, or exchanged against another VDA, and the cash component is insufficient to meet the TDS liability — the payer must ensure tax is paid on the consideration before releasing it.
  - If both **Sec 194-O** and **Sec 194S** apply to a transaction, TDS is deducted **only under Sec 194S**.

- **CBDT Guidelines (illustrative points):**
  1. TDS is computed on consideration **excluding GST/commission**.
  2. Where payment is routed through a **Payment Gateway**, the Payment Gateway itself need not deduct TDS u/s 194S (the actual buyer/exchange does).
  3. **Sec 194Q does not apply** where TDS has been deducted u/s 194S.
  4. Where the transaction is **outside an Exchange**, the buyer must deduct TDS on the seller's consideration.
  5. **Transactions through an Exchange** (e.g., WazirX):
     - If the buyer purchases VDA owned by another customer (seller) — the **Exchange** deducts TDS of the seller at the time of paying/crediting consideration.
     - If the buyer purchases VDA owned by the **Exchange itself** — the **buyer** deducts TDS of the Exchange, unless the Exchange contractually undertakes to pay the TDS to Government itself (in which case the buyer need not deduct).
  6. **VDA-to-VDA consideration** (e.g., BTC exchanged for DOGE): both parties are simultaneously buyer and seller — each must pay tax (1%) on their leg and furnish proof to the other before the exchange is completed. Alternatively, where routed through an Exchange, the Exchange deducts 1% TDS on **both legs** of the trade, converts non-primary-VDA TDS into a primary VDA (BTC/ETH/USDT/USDC) for ease of INR conversion, accumulates it over the day (00:00–23:59 hrs), and converts the accumulated balance into INR at the next day's opening market rate — with **no further TDS** on this VDA-to-VDA-to-INR conversion of the withheld tax itself.

- **Concept:** Sec 194S ensures the tax on crypto gains is collected at source, with detailed CBDT mechanics for exchange-routed and VDA-for-VDA trades where cash isn't directly available to withhold from.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Two different thresholds exist: **₹10,000** (general) vs **₹50,000** (specified person, i.e., small Ind/HUF) — a common exam trap.
  - Remember Form **26QE** (not 26QB) is specific to Sec 194S TDS by specified persons.

---

### J. Sec 10(1) — Agricultural Income

- **Key rule(s):**
  - Agricultural income from land situated **in India** is fully exempt u/s 10(1).
  - Per **Sec 2(1A)**, "agricultural income" includes:
    - (a) Rent/revenue from agricultural land (used for agricultural purposes);
    - (b) Income from sale of agricultural produce (subject to Rule 7, where the produce is processed before sale);
    - (c) Rent from a building in a rural area used as a dwelling house or store house (in connection with agricultural land);
    - (d) Income from a **nursery** (deemed agricultural income).

- **Key formula — Rule 7 (composite business: growing + processing + selling produce):**

$$
\text{Agricultural income} = \text{FMV of agricultural produce (as raw material)} - \text{Cost of cultivation of that produce}
$$

$$
\text{PGBP income} = \text{Sale value of the processed/final product} - \text{FMV of agricultural produce used as raw material} - \text{Further processing cost}
$$

- **Special composite-income Rules (agri : business split):**

| Rule | Activity | Agricultural income % | PGBP % |
|---|---|---|---|
| Rule 8 | Growing & manufacturing of Tea | 60% | 40% |
| Rule 7B(a) | Coffee — grown & cured | 75% | 25% |
| Rule 7B(b) | Coffee — grown, cured, roasted & grounded | 60% | 40% |
| Rule 7A | Growing & manufacturing of Rubber | 65% | 35% |

  - Memory tip: the **higher %** always represents the **agricultural income** component.

- **Concept:** Agricultural income is constitutionally kept outside the Union's direct tax net, but composite agro-processing businesses (tea/coffee/rubber) are statutorily split between exempt agricultural income and taxable PGBP income using fixed percentages.

- **Partial Integration (indirect taxation of agricultural income) — conditions (all must be satisfied):**
  - (i) Assessee is an **Individual, HUF, AOP, BOI, or AJP** (not a firm/company/co-op society/local authority);
  - (ii) **Net agricultural income exceeds ₹5,000**; and
  - (iii) **Non-agricultural income exceeds the basic exemption limit**.

- **Formula — Partial Integration computation:**

$$
\text{Net tax payable} = \text{Tax on (Non-agri. income + Agri. income)} - \text{Tax on (Agri. income + Basic exemption limit)}
$$

  i.e., step-by-step:
  - Non-agricultural income (Total Income) = **A**
  - Agricultural income = **B**
  - A + B = **C**; Tax on C = **D**
  - B + Basic exemption limit = **E**; Tax on E = **F**
  - **Net tax payable = D − F** (further reduced by rebate/surcharge/cess as applicable)

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Partial integration is a rate-determination mechanism only — agricultural income itself always **stays exempt**; only the applicable tax **rate/slab** effectively rises.
  - The ₹5,000 threshold applies to **net** agricultural income (after allowable expenses), not gross receipts.
  - Partial integration does **not** apply to a firm, company, co-operative society, or local authority — only to the five specified assessee categories.

---

### K. Sec 14A — Disallowance of Expenditure re: Exempt Income (Rule 8D)

- **Key rule(s):**
  - For computing income under the five heads, **no deduction** is allowed for expenditure incurred in relation to income that does not form part of total income (exempt income).
  - **Sec 14A applies only to income exempt under Chapter III of the Act** — it does **not** apply to deductions under **Chapter VI-A (Sec 80C–80U)**, since those are deductions from Gross Total Income, not exemptions.
  - By a clarificatory amendment (Finance Act 2022, effective **AY 2022-23**), Sec 14A applies **even where no exempt income has actually accrued/arisen/been received** by the assessee in the relevant PY (overriding the earlier judicial view, e.g., *Cheminvest* line of cases, that no exempt income = no disallowance).
  - **Manner of disallowance:**
    - Where the AO is **satisfied** with the correctness of the assessee's own computation of related expenditure — no further action.
    - Where the AO is **not satisfied** — expenditure attributable to exempt income is computed as per **Rule 8D**.

- **Key formula — Rule 8D (current, post-2016 simplified rule):**

$$
\text{Disallowance u/s 14A} = \text{Expenditure directly relating to exempt income} + 1\% \times \text{Average value of investments (income from which is/could be exempt)}
$$

  where the **average value of investments** = average of the **monthly average** of the opening and closing balances of such investments for the year.

  - **Cap:** the total disallowance under (a) + (b) above **cannot exceed the total expenditure actually claimed** by the assessee.

- **Concept:** Sec 14A/Rule 8D ensures that expenses (direct + a notional 1% overhead on exempt-yielding investments) which fund tax-exempt income are not allowed to reduce *taxable* income.

- **Worked illustration (per source):**
  - Total investment-related expenditure claimed: ₹2,00,000; directly attributable to exempt-income securities: ₹30,000; average value of investments yielding exempt income: ₹60,00,000.
  - Disallowance = ₹30,000 (direct) + 1% × ₹60,00,000 (= ₹60,000) = **₹90,000** disallowed.
  - Balance **₹1,10,000** (₹2,00,000 − ₹90,000) remains **allowed** as deduction (against taxable-income securities).

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Rule 8D today has only **two** components (direct expenditure + 1% of average investment) — the earlier (pre-June 2016) three-component formula with an interest-apportionment limb has been **removed**; don't reproduce the old formula.
  - No disallowance u/s 14A for income on which a Chapter VI-A deduction (80C–80U) is claimed — that income is still part of Total Income, merely deducted from Gross Total Income.
  - ⚠️ VERIFY — the case citation in source material ("Kribhco (2012)(Delhi)" — that Sec 14A applies only to income exempt under Chapter III) could not be independently confirmed this session; treat the **principle** (Sec 14A ≠ Chapter VI-A deductions) as settled law, but verify the exact case name/citation before quoting it in an answer.

---

### References

1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Chapter X-A (Sections 95–102) and Section 144BA, as amended up to Finance Act 2023/2024 (GAAR framework, threshold, and procedure).
2. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Section 2(47A) (definition of Virtual Digital Asset), Section 115BBH, and Section 194S, as inserted/amended by the Finance Act 2022.
3. CBDT Notification Nos. 74/2022 and 75/2022 dated 30 June 2022 (exclusions from the definition of VDA — gift cards, reward/loyalty points, subscriptions, and specified NFTs).
4. CBDT Circular No. 13 of 2022 dated 22 June 2022 (Guidelines under Section 194S(6) — TDS mechanics for VDA transactions, including Exchange and VDA-for-VDA scenarios).
5. Income-tax Rules, 1962 — Rule 7, Rule 7A, Rule 7B, Rule 8 (agricultural income computation) and Rule 8D (as substituted by the Income-tax (11th Amendment) Rules, 2016), and Rule 10U (GAAR monetary threshold).
6. Finance Act 2022 — clarificatory amendment to Section 14A (disallowance applies even absent exempt income in the relevant PY).

## 16. Tonnage Taxation, Taxation of Trust & Institutions, Tax Audit & Ethical Compliance

> **Where it fits:** three stand-alone "compliance & special-scheme" topics clubbed together — a presumptive scheme for shipping companies (Ch. XII-G), the exemption code for charitable/religious trusts (Sec. 2(15), 10(23C), 11–13, 115BBC, 115BBI, 115TD), and the audit/reporting discipline every large assessee (including trusts) must satisfy (Sec. 44AB, Form 3CD).

### 1. Tonnage Taxation Scheme — Eligibility & Computation

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

$$ \text{Tonnage Income} = \text{Daily Tonnage Income} \times \text{Number of days the ship is operated in the P.Y.} $$

Daily tonnage income slabs (Sec. 115VG):

| Net tonnage of qualifying ship/inland vessel | Daily Tonnage Income |
|---|---|
| Up to 1,000 tons | ₹70 for each 100 tons |
| >1,000 up to 10,000 tons | ₹700 + ₹53 for each 100 tons (of the excess over 1,000) |
| >10,000 up to 25,000 tons | ₹5,470 + ₹42 for each 100 tons (of the excess over 10,000) |
| >25,000 tons | ₹11,770 + ₹29 for each 100 tons (of the excess over 25,000) |

- Tonnage is rounded off to the nearest multiple of 100 tons.
- Eligibility: Indian company (POEM in India), engaged in operating ships/inland vessels, owning **at least one qualifying ship**; scheme is **optional**.
- "Qualifying ship": sea-going ship/vessel or inland vessel of **≥15 net tonnage**, excluding pleasure craft, fishing vessels, factory ships, harbour/river ferries, offshore installations, and ships used mainly for providing goods/services normally provided on land.
- Company must **not charter in more than 49%** of the net tonnage of qualifying ships it operates — breach disqualifies the scheme for that year only.
- Incidental income exempt only up to **0.25% of turnover from core activities**; excess is taxed under normal provisions.

- **Concept:** Presumptive/notional income scheme (Ch. XII-G) — income is deemed on a per-tonnage-per-day basis regardless of actual profit, so no expense, deduction, or loss set-off is allowed against it; also outside MAT.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - No deductions/loss set-off against tonnage income — a common trap in MCQs.
  - Tonnage income is **not** subject to MAT u/s 115JB.
  - Opting out within 10 years of opting in bars re-entry into the scheme for the next 10 years — a strict lock-out, test this in "can company re-opt" questions.
  - Separate books of account + a CA's report (furnished by the Sec. 44AB due date) are mandatory conditions, not optional.

### 2. Tonnage Tax Reserve Account (TTRA) — Creation, Utilisation & Withdrawal

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

$$ \text{Minimum annual credit to TTRA} = 20\% \times \text{Book Profit (computed as per Sec. 115JB) from core \& eligible incidental activities} $$

$$ \text{Taxable amount on shortfall} = \text{Relevant Shipping Income} \times \frac{\text{Shortfall in credit to TTRA}}{\text{Minimum reserve required to be credited}} $$

- Reserve usable **only** to acquire a new ship, within **8 years** from credit.
- Amount not utilised within 8 years → deemed income of the **9th year**.
- Ship transferred within **3 years** from the end of the P.Y. of acquisition → proportionate amount deemed income in the year of transfer.
- Failure to create TTRA for **2 consecutive P.Y.s** → tonnage scheme rendered invalid from the **3rd P.Y.**
- Any amount mis-utilised → proportionate income taxable under normal provisions.

- **Concept:** TTRA is the "lock-in" mechanism ensuring shipping companies actually reinvest into fleet capacity to keep enjoying the concessional tonnage-based tax; failure at any stage claws back the benefit.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Students often confuse the **8-year utilisation window** with the **3-year transfer restriction** and the **10-year opt-out lock** — keep all three time limits distinct in memory.

- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| TTRA | Tonnage Tax Reserve Account — a statutory reserve out of book profit, credited annually, ring-fenced for new ship acquisition |
| Book Profit | Same meaning as under Sec. 115JB |

### 3. Charitable Purpose & Trust Registration — Sec. 2(15), 12A/12AB

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - Sec. 2(15) "charitable purpose": relief of the poor, education, yoga, medical relief, preservation of environment, preservation of monuments/places/objects of artistic or historic interest, and advancement of any other object of general public utility (GPU).
  - GPU advancement is **not** charitable if it involves trade/commerce/business activity **unless** aggregate receipts from such activity do **not exceed 20% of total receipts** of that year.
  - CBDT clarification: crossing 20% only denies exemption **for that year** — registration is not to be cancelled merely for that reason; promotion of games & sports is charitable.

- Registration timelines u/s 12AB (w.e.f. 1.4.2021):

| Case | Application timing | Grant timeline | Validity |
|---|---|---|---|
| Existing 12A/12AA trust migrating | Form 10A, by 30.06.2021 (extended to 30.06.2024) | 3 months from end of month of application | 5 years, no inquiry |
| New trust — provisional registration | Form 10A, ≥1 month before start of relevant P.Y. | 1 month from end of month of application | 3 years (provisional), no inquiry |
| Provisional → final registration | Form 10AB, 6 months before expiry or 6 months from start of activity, whichever earlier | 6 months from end of quarter of application | 5 years, with inquiry |
| Renewal of 12AB registration | Form 10AB, 6 months before expiry | — | 5 years, with inquiry |
| Modification of objects | Form 10AB, within 30 days of adoption | — | 5 years, with inquiry |
| Registration inoperative u/s 11(7) (re-approval) | Form 10AB, 6 months before start of relevant A.Y. | 6 months from end of month of application | 5 years, with inquiry |

- ⚠️ VERIFY — Finance Act 2025 amendment (w.e.f. 1.4.2025): where a trust's total income (before Sec. 11/12 exemption) does **not exceed ₹5 crore** in each of the two P.Y.s preceding the year of application, registration/approval (other than provisional) is valid for **10 years instead of 5 years**. Cross-check the exact ₹5 crore threshold and effective date against the Finance Act 2025 text/CBDT notification before quoting in the exam.
  - Delay in filing application for registration may be condoned by CIT/PCIT for reasonable cause (Finance Act 2024, w.e.f. 1.10.2024).
  - W.e.f. 1.10.2023, a trust that has commenced activities but never claimed exemption can skip provisional registration and directly apply for final registration in Form 10AB.

- **Concept:** No trust/institution can claim exemption u/s 11/12 without a valid, subsisting registration u/s 12AB; the registration regime is now time-bound (not perpetual) and self-renewing only on fresh application.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - "Specified violation" (grounds for cancellation under Sec. 12AB) includes: income applied for non-objects, business income not incidental/no separate books, application for private religious purposes or a particular religious community/caste, non-genuine activity, non-compliance with other laws, or false information in the application.
  - Registration u/s 12AA/12AB becomes **inoperative** the day the trust is approved u/s 10(23C)(iv)/(v)/(vi)/(via) or notified u/s 10(23EA)/10(23EC)/10(23ED)/10(46) — a trust cannot claim both simultaneously.

### 4. Exemption u/s 11 — Application of Income & Accumulation

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

$$ \text{Income exempt u/s 11(1)} = \text{Corpus Donation} + 15\% \text{ of Gross Income (standard deduction/set-apart)} + \text{Income applied for charitable/religious purposes in India (out of remaining 85\%)} $$

- If the 85% cannot be applied in the current P.Y.:
  - **Income not received (accrual basis):** file **Form 9A** at least **2 months before** the Sec. 139(1) due date declaring the income will be applied in the year of receipt or the next year — deemed applied in the current year. If not applied within that window, taxable **@30% u/s 115BBI** in the year of receipt.
  - **Any other reason** (e.g., bumper year-end donation): file **Form 9A**, income deemed applied if actually applied in the **immediately next year**; else taxable @30% u/s 115BBI in that next year.
- **Sec. 11(2) — accumulation:** 85% not applied but set apart is exempt if: Form 10 filed (stating purpose & period, max **5 years**) at least 2 months before the Sec. 139(1) due date, invested in Sec. 11(5) modes, and not donated to another trust. (Period during which a court order prevents application is excluded from the 5-year count.)
- **CBDT Circular No. 6/2023:** deemed application/accumulation is not denied merely because Form 9A/10 was filed after the "2 months before due date" mark, as long as it is filed on or before the Sec. 139(1) due date itself.
- Donation to another registered trust/institution = application, **except** if given as that recipient's corpus.
  - Donation to another trust as application **capped at 85%** of the amount donated (FA 2023, w.e.f. AY 2024-25) — the remaining 15% is not treated as application.
- Sec. 40A(3)/40A(3A) (cash payment >₹10,000 to a person in a day, otherwise than by account-payee cheque/DD/ECS) and Sec. 40(a)(ia) (30% disallowance for TDS default) apply while computing "application," mirroring PGBP rules.
- Corpus applied is not application in the year applied; if redeposited into Sec. 11(5) modes for the corpus within **5 years**, it becomes application in the year of redeposit (to the extent redeposited).
- Amount applied from a loan/borrowing is not application; on repayment from subsequent income within **5 years**, the repayment is application in the year of repayment.
- Excess application of an earlier year **cannot be carried forward and set off** (FA 2021, w.e.f. AY 2022-23).
- Any sum "payable" is treated as applied only when **actually paid**, irrespective of the accounting method followed (FA 2022).
- Explanation 3A: donations for repair/renovation of a temple/mosque/gurdwara/church notified u/s 80G(2)(b) may be treated as corpus donation if used only for repair/renovation, not further donated, kept separately identifiable, and invested per Sec. 11(5) — ⚠️ VERIFY the "FA 22 / w.e.f. AY 21-22" tag in the source; the AY precedes the cited Finance Act, which is internally inconsistent — cross-check against the actual Finance Act (likely FA 2023).

- **Concept:** Sec. 11 grants exemption in three layers — corpus (always out), 15% flat set-aside, and the remaining 85% only if actually applied (or validly deferred via Form 9A/10) for charitable/religious purposes in India.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Form 9A and Form 10 are both due **2 months before** the Sec. 139(1) due date — a favourite date-based MCQ trap.
  - Application to another trust's **corpus** is never treated as application by the donor trust.
  - Remember the **85%-cap-at-85%** rule on inter-charity donations (only 85% of amount donated counts as application) — do not confuse with the trust's own 85%/15% split.

### 5. Denial of Exemption — Sec. 13 (Specified Persons & Prohibited Investments)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - Exemption u/s 11/12 denied (to the extent of violation) if: income used for private religious purposes; income benefits a particular religious community/caste; income benefits a "specified person"; or funds invested/deposited otherwise than in Sec. 11(5) modes.
  - **"Specified person" u/s 13(3)** includes: author/founder; a person who donated **>₹1 lakh in the P.Y. or aggregate >₹10 lakh up to the end of the P.Y.**; if founder/donor is an HUF, its members; trustee/manager; relative (as per Sec. 56(2)(x)) of the above; and any concern in which such persons have substantial interest.
  - **Sec. 13(6):** where an educational/medical trust provides such facility to a specified person, the **FMV of the facility** is treated as the trust's income and is not eligible for Sec. 11/12 exemption.
  - **Sec. 13(10):** where commercial receipts exceed 20% of gross receipts (GPU trusts), or books not maintained/audited, or return not filed on time — taxable income is computed by allowing only revenue expenditure (not from corpus/loan, no double-claim of depreciation, not a donation) actually incurred for the trust's objects in India; no other deduction/loss set-off allowed.

- **Concept:** Sec. 13 is the anti-abuse filter — even a validly registered trust loses exemption (fully or to the extent of the tainted income) if it benefits insiders or breaches the safe-investment discipline.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - The Sec. 13(3) donor threshold (**>₹1 lakh in the year OR >₹10 lakh cumulative**) was revised by Finance Act 2022 — do not use the older flat ₹50,000 figure from pre-amendment material.
  - Violation under Sec. 13(1) taxes only the **tainted portion**, not the trust's entire income (except where Sec. 13(10) special computation applies).

- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| Sec. 11(5) modes | Government securities, UTI units, notified bank/PO deposits, PSU bonds/shares, immovable property, infrastructure debt instruments, etc. — the exhaustive "safe investment" list for trust funds |

### 6. Anonymous Donations (Sec. 115BBC) & Specified Income (Sec. 115BBI)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

$$ \text{Tax @ 30\% u/s 115BBC} = \text{Anonymous Donations} - \max\Big(5\% \times \text{Total Donations (incl. corpus \& Govt. grant)},\ ₹1,00,000\Big) $$

- Wholly religious trusts: anonymous donations **not taxable** u/s 115BBC (still subject to Sec. 11/12 generally).
- Wholly charitable trusts: anonymous donations **taxable** u/s 115BBC.
- Partly religious + partly charitable trusts: **not taxable**, **except** where the donation carries a specific direction that it be used for an educational/medical institution or hospital run by the trust — then taxable.
- Balance income (after the above carve-out) taxed at normal rates, subject to Sec. 11/12.

$$ \text{Specified income taxable @ 30\% u/s 115BBI} = \begin{cases} \text{Income accumulated in excess of 15\% without specific provision} \\ \text{Deemed income under Explanation 1 to Sec. 11(1) (Form 9A/10 default)} \\ \text{Deemed income under Sec. 11(3)} \\ \text{Income applied for benefit of a specified person u/s 13(1)} \\ \text{Income not invested per Sec. 11(5) u/s 13(1)} \\ \text{Income applied outside India} \end{cases} $$

- Sec. 115BBI income is computed **without any deduction** for expenditure, allowance, or loss set-off.

- **Concept:** Both sections are flat 30% "penal" charges layered on top of the normal Sec. 11/12 computation — designed to tax specifically the anonymous-donation risk and the trust's own compliance defaults, without diluting them via expense deductions.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** In computation problems, keep Sec. 115BBC and Sec. 115BBI amounts **outside** the normal-rate income column and add them back at the end as separate 30%-rate lines (see standard problem format: Gross Receipts → less 15% set-aside → less applications/accumulation → Income at normal rates; then add anonymous donation @30% and Sec. 115BBI income @30%).

### 7. Sec. 10(23C) — Universities, Hospitals & Educational/Medical Institutions

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Wholly/substantially Govt.-financed** (Govt. grant **>50%** of total receipts) university/educational institution/hospital existing solely for education/medical relief, not for profit: **fully exempt** [Sec. 10(23C)(iiiab)/(iiiac)].
  - **Not Govt.-financed**, but existing solely for education/medical relief, not for profit, with **aggregate annual receipts up to ₹5 crore**: **fully exempt** [Sec. 10(23C)(iiiad)/(iiiae)].
  - If a person runs both an educational/university institution and a hospital/medical institution, the **₹5 crore limit applies to their aggregate receipts** combined.
  - Larger institutions require **CIT/PCIT approval** [Sec. 10(23C)(iv)/(v)/(vi)/(via)] — conditions mirror Sec. 11/12/12A/12AB/13/115BBC/115BBI.
  - W.e.f. 1.10.2024, fresh approval under Sec. 10(23C)(iv)/(v)/(vi)/(via) is discontinued — all trusts/institutions must apply for registration under **Sec. 12AB only**.

- **Concept:** Sec. 10(23C) is a parallel exemption code (mainly for large universities/hospitals) largely harmonised with the Sec. 11–13 trust regime rather than a genuinely separate scheme.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips — landmark rulings:**
  - **New Noble Educational Society (2022) SC:** "solely" for education means **all** objects must relate to education (stricter than "predominantly"); incidental business profits u/s 11(4A) are allowed only if the business itself relates to education (e.g., textbook sales, bus/hostel facilities) — renting out premises to outsiders for their own seminars is not "incidental."
  - **Ahmedabad Urban Development Authority (2022) SC:** whether an activity is "trade/commerce/business" under the Sec. 2(15) proviso is examined **year-on-year** based on receipts and whether charges are cost-based or significantly marked up; crossing 20% in one year doesn't permanently taint the trust.
  - **St. Peter's Educational Society (2016) SC:** institutions need not run only "recognised" courses to qualify u/s 10(23C)(vi); incidental profit doesn't disqualify a genuine educational institution.

### 8. Exit Tax on Accreted Income — Sec. 115TD/TE/TF & Rule 17CB

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

$$ \text{Accreted Income} = \text{Aggregate FMV of Total Assets (on specified date)} - \text{Total Liabilities} $$

$$ \text{Exit Tax u/s 115TD} = \text{Accreted Income} \times \text{Maximum Marginal Rate (MMR)} $$

- ⚠️ VERIFY — the source states MMR = **34.944% (30% + 12% surcharge + 4% cess)**. This matches the MMR structure applicable when the highest AOP/individual surcharge slab was 12% (broadly, pre-FY2016-17 rates). Under the surcharge slabs in force for several recent Finance Acts (10%/15%/25%/37% based on income slabs, with 37% for income >₹5 crore), the MMR commonly used for AOP/trust taxation (and hence Sec. 115TD) computes to **30% + 37% + 4% cess ≈ 42.744%**. Confirm the MMR percentage applicable for the relevant P.Y. against the current Finance Act's Part I / Part III rate schedule before using either figure in an exam answer.
- Triggers for exit tax: (a) conversion into a form ineligible for registration; (b) merger into an entity without similar objects/registration; (c) non-distribution of assets on dissolution to another registered trust within **12 months** from the end of the month of dissolution.
- Sec. 12AC (FA 2024, w.e.f. AY 2025-26): exit tax does **not** apply on merger if the transferee trust has similar objects, is itself registered u/s 12AA/12AB or approved u/s 10(23C), and prescribed conditions are fulfilled.
- Exit tax payable within **14 days** of the trigger event (e.g., appeal period lapsing / appellate order confirming cancellation, end of P.Y. for object-modification defaults, date of merger, or expiry of the 12-month asset-transfer window).
- Interest for delay: **1% per month (or part) u/s 115TE**, from the 15th day until actual payment.
- Non-payment: trust/institution (or its principal officer/trustee) is deemed an "assessee in default" u/s 115TF; on asset transfer to a non-charitable recipient on dissolution, the recipient too is an assessee in default, but liability is capped at the value of assets received.
- Assets/liabilities **excluded** from accreted income: those from agricultural income, and those acquired before the trust's registration became effective (with a look-back to the earliest P.Y. if benefit u/s 11/12 was already allowed pre-registration), and assets transferred to another registered trust within 12 months of dissolution.
- **Rule 17CB — FMV of unquoted equity shares:**

$$ \text{FMV per equity share} = \frac{A + B - L}{PE} \times PV $$

  where A = book value of all other assets (net of tax paid less refund, and unamortised deferred expenditure); B = FMV of bullion/jewellery/precious stones/artistic work/shares/securities/immovable property; L = book value of liabilities (excluding paid-up equity capital, dividend set apart, reserves other than depreciation reserve, tax provisions, unascertained-liability provisions, and most contingent liabilities); PE = total paid-up equity capital; PV = paid-up value of the shares being valued.
  - Quoted shares: average of lowest & highest price on a recognised stock exchange on the valuation date (or the last trading day, if no trading on that date).
  - Immovable property: **higher of** stamp duty value (SDV) or FMV.
  - Business undertaking: **A + B − L** (undertaking-level, similar mechanics as the share formula without dividing by PE/PV).

- **Concept:** Sec. 115TD is the "exit tax"/"death tax" on charitable trusts — it claws back, at MMR, the accumulated wealth of a trust that stops being charitable (converts, merges into a non-similar entity, or fails to hand over assets to another charity on dissolution), in addition to any regular income tax otherwise payable.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Exit tax is payable **even if no other income tax is payable** by the trust that year (Sec. 115TD(4)).
  - Once tax is paid on FMV, that FMV becomes the **cost of acquisition** for any subsequent transfer of the asset.

### 9. Tax Audit — Sec. 44AB, Applicability & Turnover Computation

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Business:** audit compulsory if turnover/gross receipts **> ₹1 crore**; enhanced to **> ₹10 crore** if cash receipts **and** cash payments each do not exceed **5%** of the respective totals during the year (a non–account-payee cheque/DD counts as cash for this test).
  - **Specified profession:** audit compulsory if gross receipts **≥ ₹50 lakh**.
  - **Presumptive-scheme overrides:** audit compulsory where the assessee claims income **lower than the deemed profit** under Sec. 44AD/44ADA and total income exceeds the basic exemption limit; also compulsory for lower income claimed under Sec. 44AE/44BB/44BBB.
  - **Non-applicability:** persons declaring income u/s 44AD/44ADA (within the scheme); income of the nature covered u/s 44B (shipping business of non-residents) and 44BBA (aircraft operation by non-residents).

$$ \text{Penalty u/s 271B (failure to get accounts audited)} = \min\Big(0.5\% \times \text{Turnover/Gross Receipts},\ ₹1,50,000\Big) $$

- **Turnover computation nuances:**
  - Deduct trade/cash discount shown in the invoice; do **not** deduct a cash discount for early payment (financing charge, unrelated to turnover).
  - Deduct turnover-linked rebates (quantity-based) and trade-nature special rebates; a commission-nature rebate is **not** deducted.
  - Deduct sale value of goods returned, even if from an earlier year's sales.
  - Sale proceeds of shares/securities held as **investment** are excluded from turnover; if held as **stock-in-trade**, they are included.
  - Where an assessee runs multiple businesses, turnovers are **aggregated** for the audit threshold test — except turnover of a business covered u/s 44B/44BBA, which is excluded from the aggregate.

- **Concept:** Sec. 44AB compels a CA's independent verification of books once an assessee crosses defined scale thresholds, feeding structured data (Form 3CD) to the tax department for risk-based scrutiny.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** the audit report itself must be furnished **1 month before** the Sec. 139(1) due date — do not confuse the *audit report* due date with the *return-filing* due date.

### 10. Tax Audit Report — Forms 3CA/3CB/3CD & Key Sec. 3CD Clauses (Ethical Compliance)

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

| Form combination | When used |
|---|---|
| 3CA + 3CD | Assessee's accounts already audited under another law (e.g., Companies Act 2013, LLP Act 2008) |
| 3CB + 3CD | Assessee's accounts not audited under any other law |

- **Revised TAR:** may be revised (optionally, multiple times) if a post-report payment necessitates recomputation of disallowance u/s 40 or 43B; the revised report must be obtained from a CA and furnished **before the end of the relevant A.Y.**
- Selected Form 3CD clauses students must recall cold:
  - **Clause 8A:** whether the assessee has opted for Sec. 115BA/115BAA/115BAB/115BAC/115BAD/115BAE — auditor verifies the relevant Form (10-IB/10-IC/10-ID/10-IF/10-IEA) was actually furnished.
  - **Clause 17:** immovable property transferred below stamp duty value — reporting under Sec. 43CA/50C.
