- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** For a company/other-than-individual, don't jump straight to POEM as a rigid single test — POEM is only one factor considered under MAP.

### MTC Article 5 — Permanent Establishment (OECD vs UN)

- **Key rules — Basic rule (Article 5(1)):** A PE exists only if, **cumulatively**: there is an enterprise; carrying on a business; through a place of business; at the enterprise's disposal; that is **fixed** (a distinct place with a degree of permanence); and the business is wholly/partly carried on through it.
  - **Article 5(2)** — PE "includes especially": place of management, branch, office, factory, workshop, and a mine/oil-gas well/quarry/other extraction site.
  - **Construction/installation PE:**
    - **OECD Model:** a building site, or construction/installation project, is a PE only if it lasts **more than 12 months**.
    - **UN Model:** wider — also covers **assembly/installation** projects and **supervisory activities** connected thereto, and the threshold is a shorter **6 months**.
  - **Service PE (UN Model only, absent in OECD):** furnishing of services (including consultancy) through employees/personnel, if such activities continue for a period(s) aggregating **more than 183 days in any 12-month period** commencing/ending in the relevant fiscal year. (Under OECD, such presence, if any, must be tested only under the general Article 5(1) rule.)
  - **Agency PE (both Models):** a dependent agent who **habitually concludes contracts**, or habitually plays the principal role leading to conclusion of contracts routinely concluded without material modification by the enterprise, creates a PE.
  - **Insurance PE (UN Model only, Article 5(6)):** an insurance enterprise of a CS is deemed to have a PE in the other CS (except for reinsurance) if it collects premiums, or insures risks situated, in that other State through a person.
- **Concept:** UN Model is consistently the "lower-threshold, source-friendlier" version of Article 5 versus OECD — 6 months vs 12 months, plus Service PE and Insurance PE clauses that OECD lacks entirely.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** A favourite comparison question — tabulate OECD vs UN differences (12 vs 6 months; no Service PE vs 183-day Service PE; no Insurance PE vs Article 5(6)).

### MTC Article 7 — Business Profits & Force of Attraction (FOA)

- **Key rules:**
  - Business profits are taxable **only in the Residence State**, unless the enterprise has a **PE** in the Source State — then Source State's right to tax is triggered.
  - **OECD Model:** once PE exists, Source State taxes **only profits attributable to that PE**.
  - **UN Model — limited Force of Attraction rule:** once a PE exists in the Source State, Source State may also tax profits from: (a) that PE; (b) **sales in that State of goods/merchandise of the same or similar kind** as sold through the PE; and (c) **other business activities of the same or similar kind** as carried on through the PE — even if not routed through the PE.
- **Concept:** FOA (UN only) widens the Source State's taxing net beyond the PE's own transactions to "same or similar kind" activities/sales in that State.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** OECD = strict PE-attribution only; UN = PE-attribution **plus** limited FOA — don't apply FOA under an OECD-style treaty.

### MTC Articles 11, 12, 12A, 12B — Interest, Royalties, FTS & Automated Digital Services

- **Key rules:**
  - **Article 11 (Interest):** Residence State has the primary right to tax; Source State also has a right to tax (usually on **gross basis**). If the **beneficial owner** is a resident of the other CS, the Source State's tax cannot exceed a specified % of the gross interest — **OECD Model caps this at 10%**; **UN Model leaves the % to bilateral negotiation**. Penalty charges for late payment are **not** "interest" for this Article.
  - **Article 12 (Royalties):**
    - **OECD:** royalties arising in Source State, beneficially owned by a Residence-State resident, are taxable **only in the Residence State** (exclusive right).
    - **UN Model:** departs from this — Source State **may also tax** royalties, but if beneficial owner is a Residence-State resident, the Source State's tax is capped at a bilaterally-negotiated %.
    - OECD's definition of "royalties" **excludes**: (a) rentals for films/tapes for radio/TV broadcasting; (b) equipment rentals (industrial/commercial/scientific equipment).
  - **Article 12A (UN only, inserted 2017) — Fees for Technical Services (FTS):** No OECD equivalent. Para 1: FTS may be taxed in Residence State (not exclusively). Para 2: Source State may tax per its domestic law, subject to a max-rate cap (bilaterally negotiated) if beneficial owner is a resident of the other CS.
  - **Article 12B (UN only, inserted 2021) — Income from Automated Digital Services (ADS):** No OECD equivalent. Para 1: taxable in Residence State (not exclusively). Para 2: Source State may tax per domestic law, capped at a bilaterally-negotiated % if beneficial owner is resident of the other CS. Para 6 lists covered services — online advertising, supply of user data, online search engines, online intermediation platforms, social media platforms, digital content services, online gaming, cloud computing, standardised online teaching. Para 7: Article 12B does **not** apply if the payment already qualifies as "royalty" (Art. 12) or "FTS" (Art. 12A).
- **Concept:** Progression of UN-only source-taxing articles: Royalties (12) → FTS (12A, 2017) → ADS (12B, 2021) — each expands developing-country/Source-State taxing rights that OECD's Model does not grant at all.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** OECD's 10% interest cap is a specific, testable number; royalty/FTS/ADS caps are **not fixed** by either Model — always "bilaterally negotiated," a common trick in MCQs asking for "the" percentage.

### MTC Article 13 — Capital Gains

- **Key rules:**
  - Right to tax capital gains may be **exclusive to Residence State**, or **shared** between Residence and Source States, depending on the asset (immovable property, PE assets, ships/aircraft, shares, etc.); gain is **computed as per domestic law**.
  - **Shares (updated, both Models now identical):** Source State gets the right to tax if **more than 50% of the value of the shares**, at any time during the **preceding 365 days**, is derived from **immovable property situated in that Source State**.
- **Concept:** This is the treaty analogue of India's domestic "indirect transfer" (Sec 9(1)(i)) substantial-value test, but under the treaty the look-back is a rolling **365-day** window and the threshold is **>50%**.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Don't confuse the treaty's 365-day/50% share-value test with any domestic-law threshold — they are tested as a harmonised OECD/UN rule.

### MTC Article 14 — Independent Personal Services (UN Model only)

- **Key rules:** Article 14 exists **only in the UN Model** (deleted from OECD — such income is now taxed as "Business Profits" under OECD Article 7).
  - Income from professional/independent-character services of a resident of a CS is taxable **only in that State**, **except**:
    (a) if he has a **fixed base regularly available** to him in the other CS — only income attributable to that fixed base is taxed there; or
    (b) if his stay in the other CS is **≥ 183 days in any 12-month period** commencing/ending in the fiscal year concerned — only income from activities performed there is taxed there.
  - "Professional services" includes: independent scientific, literary, artistic, educational/teaching activities, and independent activities of physicians, lawyers, engineers, architects, dentists and accountants.
- **Concept:** UN Article 14's "fixed base" and "183-day" tests mirror the PE/Service-PE logic of Article 5, but for individual professionals rather than enterprises.

### MTC Article 21 — Other Income

- **Key rules:**
  - **OECD:** exclusive right to tax "other income" (income not covered by any other Article) is with the **Residence State**.
  - **UN Model — Article 21(3):** adds that the **Source State may also tax** such other income.
  - **Article 21(2) (both Models):** if the income is effectively connected with a **PE** in the other CS, it is taxed under **Article 7** (Business Profits) instead.
  - **UN Model only:** if effectively connected with a **fixed base**, taxed under **Article 14** (Independent Personal Services) instead.
- **Concept:** Article 21 is the residuary/mop-up Article — always check first whether the income is "effectively connected" to a PE/fixed base, which redirects it to Article 7/14.

### MTC Articles 23A/23B, 25 & 26 — Elimination of Double Taxation, MAP & Exchange of Information

- **Key rules:**
  - **Articles 23A/23B:** Provide the **exemption method** and **tax credit method** respectively for eliminating double taxation (mirrors the two methods discussed at the start of this chapter).
  - **Article 25 — Mutual Agreement Procedure (MAP):** Where treatment by a CS is not in accordance with the treaty, competent authorities of both States resolve it by bilateral negotiation.

| Particular | OECD | UN |
|---|---|---|
| Requesting MAP | Taxpayer may approach **either** Contracting State | **Alt. A:** taxpayer must approach his own resident State. **Alt. B:** reference to arbitration as part of MAP — decision binding unless the directly-affected person rejects it |
| Time limit | **2 years** from when all info required by both States has been provided | **Alt. B:** arbitration may be initiated if unresolved within **3 years** of the case being presented |
| Who can request arbitration | Only the person who initiated the case | **Alt. B:** competent authorities of either State (taxpayer is then notified) |
| Departure from arbitration decision | No specific provision | **Alt. B:** competent authorities may jointly depart from the arbitration decision within **6 months** of it being communicated |

  - **Article 26 — Exchange of Information (EOI):** Governs what information CS's may exchange and how requests are made.
    - Importance: facilitates effective EOI; curtails cross-border tax evasion/avoidance; curtails capital flight (especially relevant for developing countries).
    - Common safeguards in both Models: a CS need not share confidential financial info unless confident it won't reach unauthorized persons; a CS may decline EOI for info protected by attorney–client privilege under its domestic law; however, a CS's own **lack of interest/use** for the information is **not** a valid ground to refuse EOI cooperation.
- **Concept:** Articles 23A/B are the *outcome* (how DT is eliminated); Article 25 is the *dispute-resolution* mechanism when treaty interpretation is disputed; Article 26 is the *information-sharing backbone* enabling both.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** The OECD-vs-UN MAP comparison table (2 years vs 3 years; who can request arbitration; 6-month departure window) is a frequently tested distinction question.

### References
1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sections 90, 90A, 91, 245N, 245P, 245Q, 245R, 245T, 245W, 245-OB (as amended, including Finance Act 2021 substitution of Authority for Advance Rulings with Board for Advance Rulings, effective 01-09-2021).
2. CBDT Circular No. 5/2004 dated 28-09-2004 — Taxation of BPO units in India (PE/business-connection guidance).
3. E-Advance Ruling Scheme, 2022 (CBDT notification) — faceless procedure before the Board for Advance Rulings.
4. OECD Model Tax Convention on Income and on Capital (condensed version) — Articles 1, 2, 4, 5 (12-month construction-PE threshold), 7, 11 (10% interest cap), 12, 13, 21, 23A/23B, 25, 26; corroborated via web reference on OECD/UN PE duration thresholds (en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_establishment).
5. UN Model Double Taxation Convention between Developed and Developing Countries — Articles 5 (6-month construction PE, 183-day Service PE, Article 5(6) Insurance PE), 7 (Force of Attraction), 12A (FTS, 2017 insertion), 12B (Automated Digital Services, 2021 insertion), 13, 14, 21, 25 (Alternative A/B MAP).
6. ICAI Final Course Study Material — Paper on International Taxation (DTAA, Advance Ruling, Model Tax Conventions chapters) — cross-referenced for structuring and standard fee/threshold figures.

⚠️ VERIFY — the exact current BOAR application fee slabs (₹10,000 / ₹2,00,000 / ₹5,00,000 / ₹10,00,000 per Sec 245Q read with the relevant Income-tax Rules/Form) and the OECD Article 25 "2-year" MAP timeline could not be cross-checked against a live, current-dated primary source in this session (web search budget was exhausted and several primary-source fetches returned 403/404); figures above match the source concept book and standard ICAI material but should be tallied against the latest CBDT notification/Finance Act text before the exam.

## 20. Application & Interpretation of Tax Treaties, BEPS & Latest Developments in International Taxation
> **Where it fits:** Ties together everything learnt in NR taxation, PE and Transfer Pricing — how a treaty is read, why base erosion happens, and how OECD's BEPS Action Plan / MLI / Two-Pillar Solution reshape India's international tax rulebook; a high-yield, concept-heavy area in CA Final DT/IT.

### Sources of International Tax Law & Double Taxation
- **Key rule(s):**
  - Sources of international tax law: (a) Multilateral International Agreements (MIA) — e.g., Vienna Convention on the Law of Treaties (VCLT), 1969; (b) DTAA (including protocols, MOUs, exchange-of-information agreements forming part of it); (c) Customary international law, general practices and judicial decisions.
  - Two connecting factors create taxing jurisdiction: **Residence** (home country taxes global income) and **Source** (host country taxes income arising there).
  - **Jurisdictional double taxation** — same income taxed twice in the hands of the *same* person by two states (residence + source overlap). Relief: DTAA, or, absent one, unilateral relief under **sec. 91**.
  - **Economic double taxation** — same income taxed in the hands of *two different* persons in two states (no identity of taxpayer, e.g., foreign DDT-equivalent tax + tax on dividend recipient).
- **Concept:** Distinguishes *why* double taxation arises (jurisdictional vs economic) so the correct relief provision (treaty Article vs sec. 91) is invoked.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Sec. 91 unilateral relief applies only where **no DTAA** exists with the other country, or where the DTAA is silent on that item of income.
  - Do not confuse "jurisdictional" (same taxpayer) with "economic" (different taxpayers) double taxation in written answers — examiners test this distinction directly.

### Types of DTAA, Need for Treaty & Neutrality Principles
- **Key rule(s):**
  - **Limited DTAA** — covers only specified income (e.g., India–Pakistan treaty limited to aircraft profits).
  - **Comprehensive DTAA** — covers substantially all heads of income (and sometimes wealth/gift tax).
  - Objectives of a tax treaty: allocate taxing rights; eliminate double taxation; ensure non-discrimination between residents/non-residents; resolve interpretational disputes; assist in cross-border tax collection.
  - **Capital Export Neutrality (CEN):** an investor's decision to invest at home vs abroad should not be distorted by tax.
  - **Capital Import Neutrality (CIN):** tax on residents and non-residents operating in the *same* market should be similar.
- **Concept:** CEN looks from the residence country's lens (outbound investment neutrality); CIN looks from the source country's lens (a level field for residents and non-residents competing there).
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Learn one example each for CEN/CIN — a common 2-mark theory question.

### Interpretation of Tax Treaties — Principles under Customary International Law
- **Key rule(s)/principles:**
  - **Golden Rule (Objective Interpretation):** ordinary/literal, contextual meaning; departed from only if it leads to absurdity.
  - **Subjective Interpretation:** common intention of contracting parties at the time of conclusion.
  - **Purposive Interpretation:** interpret to further the treaty's aims/objectives.
  - **Principle of Effectiveness:** interpret so the treaty has effect, not so it is rendered void.
  - **Contemporanea Expositio:** terms interpreted per their meaning at the time the treaty was concluded (not a universal principle — see Ambulatory approach below).
  - **Liberal Construction:** treaties construed liberally to carry out the parties' apparent intention.
  - **Integrated Approach (treaty as a whole):** treaty read as a whole; a term construed consistently wherever it recurs.
  - **Reasonableness and Consistency:** prefer the reasonable, consistent meaning; interpret in light of existing international law.
- **Concept:** Examiners test these as MCQ/short-note "match the principle to its name" — know the *name* + one-line meaning for each.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Don't merge "Contemporanea Expositio" (static, historical meaning) with "Ambulatory approach" (current meaning) — they represent opposite philosophies, discussed next.

### Ambulatory vs Static Approach & Extrinsic Aids
- **Key rule(s):**
  - **Static approach:** looks at the meaning of an undefined term as it stood **when the treaty was signed**.
  - **Ambulatory approach:** looks at the meaning **at the time the treaty provision is applied** (i.e., as per current domestic law) — favoured by all Model Commentaries, *except* where a radical amendment changes the fundamental sum-and-substance of the term.
  - Extrinsic aids permitted in treaty interpretation: interpretative protocols/resolutions/committee reports; subsequent agreements between parties; subsequent conduct of state parties; parallel (*in pari materia*) treaties; IFA (Netherlands) articles/reports; preamble; Mutual Agreement Procedure (MAP); OECD/UN Model Commentaries; foreign courts' decisions.
- **Concept:** Ambulatory is the default rule most countries (including India) follow for interpreting undefined treaty terms by reference to current domestic law (akin to Article 3(2) of the OECD Model).
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** State the caveat to the ambulatory approach explicitly in exams — a radical change in domestic law altering the term's basic character freezes interpretation to the static meaning.

### Protocol & the Most-Favoured-Nation (MFN) Clause
- **Key rule(s):**
  - **Protocol** — an integral, legally binding supplement/annexure to a treaty clarifying borderline issues (e.g., the MFN clause sits in the Protocol to the India–France treaty).
  - **MFN clause:** if India later signs a DTAA with a third state granting a *lower rate/narrower scope* of source taxation (dividend, interest, royalty, FTS) than under an existing treaty containing an MFN clause, that lower rate/narrower scope may get imported into the earlier treaty.
  - CBDT's administrative position — MFN benefit is available to the first (OECD) State only when **all** of the following are satisfied:
    1. The second treaty (with the third state) is entered into **after** the signature/entry-into-force of the treaty with the first state;
    2. The third state was **already an OECD member** at the time it signed its treaty with India;
    3. India has **limited its taxing rights** (rate or scope) in that second treaty; and
    4. A **separate notification under sec. 90(1)** has been issued by India importing the benefit into the treaty with the first state.
  - ⚠️ VERIFY — The Supreme Court, in *Assessing Officer (IT) v. Nestlé SA* (12 Oct 2023), upheld that a sec. 90(1) notification is a **mandatory pre-condition** for MFN benefit to apply under domestic law, and that "OECD membership" for condition (2) is tested **at the time of signing** the second treaty (not merely at any later date) — reversing the taxpayer-favourable Delhi HC view (Concentrix/Nestlé). Students should quote this ruling as the current settled law for CA Final 2026.
- **Concept:** MFN clause avoids inter-DTAA discrimination but, per the Supreme Court, does not operate automatically — a specific Indian notification is always needed.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** A very popular numerical/conceptual question — always test all four conditions cumulatively, and cite the Nestlé SC ruling for the "notification is mandatory" position.

### Vienna Convention on the Law of Treaties (VCLT), 1969 — Key Articles
- **Key rule(s):**

| Article | Rule |
|---|---|
| 26 | *Pacta sunt servanda* — every treaty in force binds the parties and must be performed in good faith |
| 27 | A party cannot invoke its internal (domestic) law to justify failure to perform a treaty |
| 28 | Non-retroactivity — treaties do not bind a party for acts that ceased before the treaty's entry into force |
| 29 | Territorial scope — binding on the entire territory of each party unless otherwise stated |
| 31 | General rule of interpretation — good faith, ordinary meaning, in context, in light of object & purpose; context includes text, preamble, annexures and related agreements/instruments |
| 32 | Supplementary means of interpretation — used only if Article 31 leaves the meaning ambiguous or leads to an unreasonable/absurd result |
| 33 | Treaties authenticated in 2+ languages — each text equally authoritative; where meanings differ, the reconciled meaning best serving the object & purpose prevails |
| 34 | A treaty creates neither obligations nor rights for a third state without its consent |
| 42 | Validity/continuance of a treaty impeachable only through the Convention itself |
| 60 | Material breach of a treaty entitles the other party to terminate/suspend it (special rules for multilateral treaties) |
| 61 | Supervening impossibility of performance permits termination/withdrawal (not if self-induced by the invoking party's own breach) |
| 62 | Fundamental change of circumstances (*rebus sic stantibus*) — narrow exception to terminate/withdraw, not available for boundary treaties or self-induced changes |
| 64 | Emergence of a new peremptory norm (*jus cogens*) voids and terminates a conflicting treaty |
- **Concept:** VCLT is the "constitution" governing how all treaties (including DTAAs) are interpreted, breached, suspended or terminated.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Article 31 (general rule) vs Article 32 (supplementary, used only as a fallback) is the most frequently tested pairing.

### BEPS — Meaning, Adverse Effects & the Three Pillars of Action Plans
- **Key rule(s):**
  - **BEPS** = tax planning strategies exploiting gaps/mismatches in tax rules to shift profits to low/no-tax locations with little real economic activity, eroding the tax base of the source/residence country.
  - Adverse effects: revenue loss + higher compliance costs for governments; under-funding of public investment in developing countries; unfairness (individuals bear higher relative burden); unfair competitive advantage to MNEs over domestic/family businesses.
  - The 15 BEPS Action Plans are structured around **3 pillars**: (i) coherence of domestic rules affecting cross-border activity; (ii) reinforcing substance requirements — aligning taxation with value creation; (iii) improving transparency and tax certainty.
- **Concept:** BEPS Action Plan (2015, G20/OECD, 15 Actions) is the umbrella project; the Multilateral Instrument (Action 15) and the Two-Pillar Solution (BEPS 2.0) are its implementation vehicles.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Memorise the 3-pillar classification — a recurring theory question asking to "classify" any given Action Plan under a pillar.

### BEPS Action Plans 1–7 (Digital Economy to Treaty Abuse/PE Avoidance)
- **Key rule(s):**

| Action Plan | Theme | Indian provision incorporated |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Address tax challenges of the digital economy (nexus via "significant digital presence", virtual PE, withholding tax, equalisation levy) | **Significant Economic Presence (SEP)** — sec. 9(1)(i) Expl. 2A; India also introduced **Equalisation Levy** (2016: 6% on specified online advertisement services; 2020: 2% on e-commerce supply of goods/services) |
| 2 | Neutralise Hybrid Mismatch Arrangements (HMA) — e.g., double deduction, deduction/no-inclusion, FTC misuse, participation-exemption misuse | Domestic anti-hybrid rules + treaty changes for dual-resident/transparent/hybrid entities (implemented via MLI Part II) |
| 3 | Strengthen Controlled Foreign Company (CFC) rules — CFC income (passive: interest/royalty/dividend/related-party income) deemed taxable in parent state even without distribution | India has **no dedicated CFC regime**; addressed indirectly via GAAR/POEM |
| 4 | Limit interest deductions/thin capitalisation — Fixed Ratio Rule (interest capped at a % of EBITDA), Group Ratio Rule, targeted rules for banks/insurers | **Sec. 94B** — restricts interest deduction to **30% of EBITDA** on interest paid/payable to an associated enterprise, applicable only where interest expenditure exceeds ⚠️ VERIFY — **₹1 crore**; excess disallowed can be carried forward 8 assessment years; banking/insurance business excluded |
| 5 | Counter harmful tax practices — low-tax IP regimes benefit only if IP is substantially developed (not merely registered) in that jurisdiction ("nexus approach"/patent box) | **Sec. 115BBF** — royalty income from a patent **developed and registered in India** by an eligible (resident) patentee taxed at a flat **10%** (plus surcharge/cess) on gross basis, no expenditure/Chapter VI-A deduction allowed |
| 6 | Prevent treaty abuse/treaty shopping — Preamble statement (treaty not for non-taxation via shopping), **LOB** (objective tests — legal form, ownership, activity, expenditure) and **PPT** (principal purpose test, a GAAR-type rule) | LOB example: India–Mauritius Protocol (2016) shell/conduit test — total operational expenditure below the prescribed threshold in the preceding 12 months denies treaty benefit; ⚠️ VERIFY — threshold is commonly cited as **₹27,00,000** (or MUR 15,00,000), not the ₹7,00,000 figure in some source notes |
| 7 | Prevent artificial avoidance of PE status — widen PE definition to cover commissionaire/agency arrangements (unless a genuine independent agent) and re-examine specific-activity exemptions | Reflected via India's MLI (Part IV) positions and expanded "dependent agent PE"/"business connection" tests |
- **Concept:** Actions 1–7 target the *mechanisms* MNEs use (digital nexus gaps, hybrids, CFC deferral, excess interest, harmful IP regimes, treaty shopping, artificial PE avoidance).
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - For the India–Mauritius LOB example: the **50% of domestic tax rate** on capital gains was a *transitional* concession only for shares acquired between 1.4.2017 and 31.3.2019 (subject to LOB) — from 1.4.2019 capital gains on Mauritius-route shares are fully taxable at domestic rates; shares acquired before 1.4.2017 remain fully grandfathered/exempt.
  - Sec. 94B is examined alongside Transfer Pricing chapter — remember it overrides sec. 36(1)(iii) interest deduction only for AE borrowings above the threshold.

### BEPS Action Plans 8–15 (Transfer Pricing, Measuring BEPS, Disclosure, Documentation, Dispute Resolution & MLI)
- **Key rule(s):**

| Action Plan | Core content |
|---|---|
| 8–10 | Align Transfer Pricing outcomes with value creation: (8) intangibles — prevent profit misallocation from mobile, hard-to-value IP; (9) risk — contractual risk allocation respected only if backed by actual decision-making/control; (10) other high-risk transactions — non-commercially-rational allocations, TP methods diverting profits, management-fee/HO-expense base erosion |
| 11 | Measuring & Monitoring BEPS — 6 indicators (e.g., MNE affiliates in low-tax countries report profit rates ~2× the group's worldwide average; royalty-to-R&D ratio in low-tax countries ~6× the average) |
| 12 | Mandatory disclosure of aggressive tax planning arrangements — design principles: clarity, cost-benefit balance, flexibility, accurate scheme identification, effective use of information |
| 13 | Re-examine TP documentation — mandates a **three-tier structure**: Master File, Local File, Country-by-Country (CbC) Report |
| 14 | Make dispute resolution effective — minimum standard to ensure full, good-faith implementation of **MAP** and timely resolution |
| 15 | Develop a Multilateral Instrument (MLI) to transpose treaty-related BEPS measures across all Covered Tax Agreements without bilateral renegotiation |
- **Definitions (Three-tier TP documentation, Action 13):**

| Document | Content |
|---|---|
| Master File | High-level standardised information on the MNE group's global business, structure and TP policies; filed with local tax administration |
| Local File | Detailed transactional information — related-party transactions, financials, comparability analysis, TP method selection — specific to that country |
| CbC Report | Country-wise revenue, profit before tax, tax paid/accrued and indicators of economic activity; filed by the ultimate parent in its residence jurisdiction and shared via automatic exchange of information |
- **Concept:** Action 13's CbCR (and the Pillar Two €750 million threshold, below) share the *same* revenue benchmark globally — €750 million consolidated group revenue.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Do not swap Master File (group-level) with Local File (entity/country-level) — a common examiner trap; CbCR filing obligation and threshold are examined together with sec. 286 in the TP chapter.

### The Multilateral Instrument (MLI) — Structure & Mechanics
- **Key rule(s):**
  - MLI has **7 Parts** and (per the OECD text) **39 Articles**; Articles 3–17 are the substantive provisions.

| Part | Coverage | Articles |
|---|---|---|
| I | Scope & Interpretation of terms | 1–2 |
| II | Hybrid Mismatches | 3–5 |
| III | Treaty Abuse | 6–11 |
| IV | Avoidance of PE Status | 12–15 |
| V | Improving Dispute Resolution | 16–17 |
| VI | Arbitration | 18–26 |
| VII | Final Provisions | 27–39 |
  - **Covered Tax Agreement (CTA):** a DTAA becomes "covered" only when **both** contracting states notify it to the OECD Depository as a CTA under the MLI — if only one party notifies, the MLI does not apply to that treaty.
  - **Compatibility clause:** bridges the MLI and the existing DTAA, letting parties choose which MLI provisions replace/supplement existing DTAA clauses, or leave the DTAA provision undisturbed.
  - **Reservation ("opt-out") clause:** a unilateral statement excluding/modifying a non-minimum-standard MLI provision; minimum-standard provisions cannot be reserved out of entirely.
  - **Mandatory minimum standards** (of the 4 BEPS minimum standards — Actions 5, 6, 13, 14 — only **Actions 6 (treaty abuse) and 14 (dispute resolution)** are embedded as MLI minimum standards; Actions 5 and 13 are implemented through domestic law instead).
  - **Entry into force:** first day of the month following expiry of **3 calendar months** from the date of deposit of the instrument of ratification (of the later-ratifying party).
  - **Effective date:** (a) for withholding taxes — 1st day of the next calendar year beginning on/after the date the MLI enters into force for both jurisdictions; (b) for other taxes — the taxable period beginning on/after expiry of **6 calendar months** from that entry-into-force date.
- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| CTA | A DTAA that both contracting parties have notified to the OECD Depository as covered by the MLI |
| Compatibility clause | Mechanism reconciling MLI provisions with the pre-existing DTAA text |
| Reservation | A party's unilateral opt-out from a non-minimum-standard MLI provision |
- **India's MLI journey:**

| Date | Event |
|---|---|
| 7 June 2017 | India signs the MLI |
| 25 June 2019 | India deposits its instrument of ratification with the OECD |
| 9 Aug 2019 | CBDT Notification No. 57/2019 gives effect to MLI provisions in India |
| 1 Oct 2019 | MLI enters into force for India |
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Both countries must notify the *same* DTAA as a CTA — e.g., if India notifies India–Mauritius as a CTA but Mauritius does not, the MLI does not modify that treaty at all.

### BEPS 2.0 — Two-Pillar Solution: Pillar One (Profit Allocation & Nexus)
- **Key rule(s):**
  - 137 countries/jurisdictions joined the Two-Pillar Solution Statement on **8 Oct 2021** (OECD/G20 Inclusive Framework).
  - **Pillar One (Amount A)** applies to MNE groups with global turnover **> €20 billion** and profitability **> 10%** (profit before tax ÷ revenue).
  - $$ \text{Amount A} = 25\% \times \big(\text{Group Profit} - 10\% \times \text{Group Revenue}\big) $$
  - Nexus/market revenue thresholds to establish a jurisdiction's right to Amount A: **≥ €1 million** where the jurisdiction's annual GDP **≥ €40 billion**; **≥ €250,000** where GDP **< €40 billion**.
  - Revenue sourcing rule: revenue is sourced to the end-market jurisdiction where goods/services are actually used/consumed.
  - **Amount B** simplifies baseline marketing & distribution transfer pricing for all taxpayers (a standardised, simplified TP outcome, not a formulary allocation).
- **Concept:** Pillar One reallocates a slice of an in-scope MNE's *residual* (super-normal) profit to market/consumer jurisdictions, breaking the century-old "no tax without physical presence" nexus rule.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Distinguish "Routine profit" (≤10% margin, stays with existing TP rules) from "Residual profit" (>10% margin, 25% of which is Amount A, reallocated by formula) — frequently tested as a numerical.

### BEPS 2.0 — Pillar Two: Global Minimum Tax (GloBE Rules) & STTR
- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - Pillar Two applies to MNE groups with (consolidated) revenue **≥ €750 million** (same threshold as CbCR).
  - $$ \text{ETR (jurisdictional)} = \frac{\text{Total Adjusted Covered Taxes of all Constituent Entities in the jurisdiction}}{\text{Net GloBE Income of the jurisdiction}} $$
  - $$ \text{Net GloBE Income} = \text{GloBE Income of all Constituent Entities} - \text{GloBE Losses of all Constituent Entities} $$
  - Minimum rate = **15%**. If jurisdictional ETR < 15%, it is a Low-Tax Jurisdiction (LTJ) and its entities are Low-Taxed Constituent Entities (LTCEs).
  - $$ \text{Top-up Tax Percentage} = \text{Minimum Rate } (15\%) - \text{ETR} $$
  - $$ \text{Excess Profit} = \text{Net GloBE Income} - \text{Substance-Based Income Exclusion (SBIE)} $$
  - $$ \text{Jurisdictional Top-up Tax} = \text{Excess Profit} \times \text{Top-up Tax Percentage} $$
  - **De-minimis exclusion:** no top-up tax where, for the jurisdiction, average GloBE Revenue **< €10 million** *and* average GloBE Income is a loss or **< €1 million**.
  - Priority of GloBE mechanisms: **QDMTT** (source/LTJ itself collects the top-up tax) → **IIR** (Income Inclusion Rule — parent/UPE jurisdiction collects if no QDMTT) → **UTPR** (Undertaxed Payment Rule — backstop; other group jurisdictions collect via denial of deduction if neither QDMTT nor IIR applies).
  - **Subject to Tax Rule (STTR):** a treaty-based rule (operates in priority to GloBE) letting a source/developing country tax specified related-party ("connected persons", >50% ownership/de facto control) payments — interest, royalties, distribution-rights fees, insurance/reinsurance premiums, guarantee/financing fees, equipment rental, service fees — where the recipient's nominal tax rate is below **9%**.
  - $$ \text{STTR Specified Rate} = 9\% - \text{Nominal Tax Rate in Resident State} - \text{Source Tax Already Allocated under Other Treaty Articles} $$
  - STTR applicability threshold: source-country covered income **> €1 million/year** (GDP ≥ €40 billion) or **> €250,000/year** (GDP < €40 billion).
- **Concept:** Pillar Two ensures every large MNE pays at least 15% effective tax in every jurisdiction it operates in; STTR is a narrower treaty override letting developing/source countries claw back tax on low-taxed outbound related-party payments, ahead of the GloBE mechanisms.
- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Top-up Tax % is computed on the *whole* Net GloBE Income, but applied only to *Excess Profit* (i.e., after deducting SBIE) — a favoured numerical twist in exams.
  - QDMTT > IIR > UTPR is the tested priority sequence — always start with whether the LTJ itself has a QDMTT.
  - ⚠️ VERIFY — As of the 2026 CA Final syllabus cut-off, India has **not yet enacted** domestic GloBE/QDMTT legislation; questions are expected to remain conceptual/OECD-framework based unless a Finance Act amendment is notified before the attempt.
  - India abolished the Equalisation Levy in stages: the 2% levy on e-commerce supply of goods/services was withdrawn effective **1 Aug 2024** (Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024), and the remaining 6% levy on online advertisement was withdrawn effective **1 Apr 2025** (Finance Act, 2025) — a direct consequence of India aligning with the Two-Pillar consensus (standstill/rollback of unilateral digital taxes).

### References
1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — sec. 90, sec. 90A, sec. 91, sec. 94B, sec. 115BBF, sec. 9(1)(i) Expl. 2A (Significant Economic Presence).
2. OECD, *Base Erosion and Profit Shifting (BEPS) — Action Plans 1–15* (Final Reports, 2015), OECD/G20 Inclusive Framework.
3. OECD, *Multilateral Convention to Implement Tax Treaty Related Measures to Prevent Base Erosion and Profit Shifting (MLI)*, 2016/2017; CBDT Notification No. 57/2019 dated 9 Aug 2019.
4. OECD/G20 Inclusive Framework, *Statement on a Two-Pillar Solution to Address the Tax Challenges Arising from the Digitalisation of the Economy*, 8 Oct 2021; OECD Pillar One/Pillar Two technical guidance (GloBE Model Rules, STTR).
5. Vienna Convention on the Law of Treaties (VCLT), 1969 — Articles 26–34, 42, 60–64.
6. Supreme Court of India, *Assessing Officer (IT) v. Nestlé SA* (12 Oct 2023) — on mandatory sec. 90(1) notification for invoking an MFN clause.
7. Protocol to the India–Mauritius DTAA (2016 amendment) — Article 27A (Limitation of Benefits/shell-conduit test).
8. ICAI, Final Course Study Material — Paper: Direct Tax Laws & International Taxation, relevant chapters on International Taxation/BEPS.

## 21. Foreign Tax Credit Rule, Conversion of Foreign Income & Remaining Case Laws

> **Where it fits:** Closing chapter of the International Taxation block — how double-taxed foreign income gets relieved through FTC (Rule 128), how that foreign income/tax is converted into ₹ (Rule 115/26), followed by a round-up of recent case laws, Sec 170A/89A reliefs, fresh CBDT circulars, the compounding-of-offences scheme, and Safe Harbour Rules (Sec 92CB) — all high-yield "current update" material for the exam.

### 1. Foreign Tax Credit (FTC) — Sec 90/90A/91 read with Rule 128

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**

$$
\text{FTC allowed (per source, per country)} = \min\Big(\text{Tax payable under the Income-tax Act on the doubly-taxed income},\ \text{Actual foreign tax paid/deducted}\Big)
$$

  - Where foreign tax paid **exceeds** the tax payable **as per the DTAA**, such excess is ignored.
  - FTC is computed **source-wise and country-wise** (not on aggregate foreign income).
  - **Year of credit:** the PY in which the corresponding income is offered to tax in India; if that income is offered across multiple years, FTC is claimed across those years in the **same proportion** as the income.
  - FTC is available against **income-tax + surcharge + cess** liability (including MAT/AMT), but **not** against interest, fee, or penalty. If FTC computed against MAT/AMT exceeds the FTC available under normal provisions, the excess is ignored.
  - **Disputed foreign tax:** allowed in the year of offering income only if the assessee, within **6 months** from the end of the month in which the dispute is finally settled, furnishes evidence of settlement and proof of payment of the disputed tax.
  - **Conversion rate:** TT buying rate (TTBR) of the State Bank of India as on the **last day of the month immediately preceding the month** in which the foreign tax was paid or deducted.

- **Concept:** FTC is India's unilateral/treaty-based relief mechanism so that income taxed abroad and again taxed in India (residence-based taxation) does not suffer double tax — the relief is capped at whichever of the two tax amounts is lower, so a taxpayer never gets more credit than India's own tax on that income.

- **Documents required (Rule 128):**
  - Form No. 67 — statement of income from the foreign country and foreign tax deducted/paid;
  - A certificate/statement of the nature of income and tax deducted/paid, from (a) the foreign tax authority, or (b) the person responsible for deduction, or (c) the assessee (self-certification permitted) — plus proof of payment (challan/online payment acknowledgement) where self-certified;
  - Proof of TDS where tax has been deducted.
  - **Timeline:** Form 67 and the certificate must be furnished **on or before the due date u/s 139(1)**. Rule 128(9) was **amended w.e.f. 1.4.2022** to relax this — the statement in Form 67 may now be furnished on or before the **end of the assessment year** relevant to the PY in which the income is offered/assessed to tax, provided the return for that AY has been furnished within the time allowed u/s 139(1) or 139(4). Where the return is furnished u/s 139(8A) (updated return), Form 67 (to the extent relating to income in the updated return) must be furnished on/before the date of filing that updated return.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Do not net foreign tax across different source countries — apply the lower-of rule country-by-country/source-by-source.
  - Remember FTC is available against MAT/AMT too — a frequently tested point.
  - The relaxed Rule 128(9) timeline (end of AY, not just due date u/s 139(1)) is a key recent amendment — quote it precisely.

- **Case law:**

| Case | Held |
|---|---|
| **Duraiswamy Kumaraswamy [2024] (Madras HC)** | Filing of Form 67 is **directory, not mandatory**. Where Form 67 was filed (though after the return, but before intimation u/s 143(1) was issued), FTC cannot be denied merely for the delay — Rule 128 only implements the Act and cannot override the substantive right to FTC. |

- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| FTC | Credit for tax paid/deducted in a foreign country on income also taxed in India, allowed against Indian tax liability u/s 90, 90A or 91 |

---

### 2. Conversion of Foreign Income into Indian Currency — Rule 115 & Rule 26

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - **Rule 115:** Foreign-currency income is converted to ₹ at the **TTBR as on the "specified date"**:

| Head of income | Specified date |
|---|---|
| (a) Salary | Last day of the month **immediately preceding** the month in which salary is due, or is paid in advance/arrears |
| (b) Interest on securities | Last day of the month immediately preceding the month in which the income is due |
| (c) IFHP, PGBP [other than (d)], and IFOS (excluding dividends and interest on securities) | Last day of the **previous year** of the assessee |
| (d) PGBP of a non-resident engaged in the business of operation of ships | Last day of the month immediately preceding the month in which such income is **deemed to accrue or arise** in India |
| (e) Dividends | Last day of the month immediately preceding the month in which the dividend is declared, distributed, or paid |
| (f) Capital gains | Last day of the month immediately preceding the month in which the capital asset is **transferred** |

  - **Proviso:** where the above income (payable in foreign currency) has suffered TDS under Rule 26, the specified date instead becomes the date on which tax was required to be deducted under the TDS chapter.
  - **Rule 26 (rate of exchange for TDS purposes):** for tax deductible on income payable in foreign currency — (i) to an assessee outside India, (ii) to a Unit of an IFSC, or (iii) by a Unit of an IFSC to an assessee in India — the rate is the **TTBR of that currency as on the date tax is required to be deducted** under the TDS chapter.

- **Concept:** Rule 115 governs conversion for computing income under the Act; Rule 26 is the parallel, narrower rule for converting the value on which TDS itself must be worked out — the two dates can differ (e.g., salary accrual date under 115 vs. TDS-deduction date under 26), and the proviso to Rule 115 resolves the clash in favour of the Rule 26 date wherever TDS applies.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Always use **TTBR** (TT buying rate), not TT selling rate or cash rate — a common trap in MCQs/numericals.
  - For capital gains, the specified date is linked to the **month of transfer**, not the month of receipt of consideration.
  - Don't confuse Rule 115 (income computation) with Rule 128 (FTC conversion — also TTBR, but keyed to the **month preceding the month of tax payment/deduction**, not to the income event).

- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| TTBR | Telegraphic Transfer Buying Rate — the rate adopted for conversion, as notified/published by SBI |

---

### 3. Remaining Case Laws — Capital vs. Revenue / Doctrine of Mutuality

- **Concept:** A cluster of settled principles: (i) whether an expense/receipt is capital or revenue depends on substance over form and the purpose it serves; (ii) mutuality exempts receipts among members of a common fund, but breaks down once the fund is exposed to third-party/commercial exploitation.

| Case | Held |
|---|---|
| **Honda Siel Cars India Ltd. [2017] (SC)** | Technical fee paid under a Technical Collaboration Agreement (TCA) to set up a joint venture in India is **capital expenditure** — the TCA's entire purpose was setting up the JV (full plant/machinery assistance), and the JV itself would cease to exist on termination of the TCA. (Where only a limited right to use know-how is obtained for a limited period to improve an *existing* business, the expenditure would be revenue.) |
| **Saurashtra Cement Ltd. [2010] (SC)** | Liquidated damages received from a plant supplier for delayed supply of machinery are a **capital receipt** — the damages were directly linked to procurement of a capital asset (the cement plant) and compensated for sterilisation of the profit-making apparatus, not for a loss in the ordinary course of business/profit-earning process. |
| **Venkatesh Premises Co-operative Society Ltd. [2018] (SC)** | Transfer charges, non-occupancy charges, common amenity fund charges, and similar charges collected from members and applied for members' benefit are **exempt under the doctrine of mutuality** (a person cannot make a profit out of himself). |
| **Madras Gymkhana Club [2010] (Mad.)** | Interest earned by a club from surplus funds placed as fixed deposits with **institutional (bank) members** does **not** satisfy the principle of mutuality and is **not exempt** on that ground. |
| **Secunderabad Club [2023] (SC)** | Mutuality applies to a club's surplus funds **up to the stage of deposit** in a member bank, but is **lost once deposited as an FD** — the bank can commercially lend those funds to third parties, rupturing the "privity of mutuality." Interest income on such FDs is taxable as income from other sources u/s 2(24), like any other income. (Facility given to members = mutuality; the same facility offered to non-members/public = commercial, mutuality lost.) |

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - Secunderabad Club effectively supersedes the "member-bank interest is always mutual" line of reasoning — always answer that FD interest with member banks is **taxable**, regardless of the bank being a member.
  - For capital vs. revenue questions, always tie the answer to *purpose* (creating/improving an enduring asset/business vs. running the existing business) — quote Honda Siel Cars for TCA/technical-fee fact patterns and Saurashtra Cement for compensation/damages fact patterns.

---

### 4. Remaining Case Laws — International Tax / TDS / Procedure

| Case | Held |
|---|---|
| **Trans Asian Shipping Services (P.) Ltd. [2016] (SC)** | A company "operates" a ship — and so is eligible for the Tonnage Tax Scheme (Sec 115VG) — even under a **slot charter / space charter / joint charter** arrangement (not just owned/wholly-chartered ships). "Deemed tonnage" u/s 115VG(4) covers slot-charter purchases; the requirement of producing a certificate for a qualifying ship does **not** apply where only slots (not the entire ship) are chartered. |
| **Johnson Matthey Public Limited Company [2024] (Delhi HC)** | **Guarantee fee** received by a foreign parent from its Indian subsidiaries is **not "interest"** either u/s 2(28A) or under Article 12(5) of the India–UK DTAA. "Interest" is confined to payments within the privity of a loan/debt contract; a guarantor is a stranger to that privity, so guarantee commission (compensation for a contingent risk of the subsidiary's default) falls outside "interest," "debt claims," and "service fee/charge in respect of moneys borrowed." |
| **Jupiter Capital Pvt. Ltd. [2025] (SC)** | **Reduction of share capital constitutes "transfer"** under the Income-tax Act — "extinguishment of any right" is of wide import and covers proportionate reduction in shareholding even where the face value and the overall percentage shareholding remain unchanged. Capital loss on such reduction is admissible. |
| **Travel Designer India Pvt. Ltd. [2025] (SC)** | Where a return filed u/s 139(1) is found defective and the assessee rectifies the defect within the time allowed, the corrected return **relates back** to the original date of filing u/s 139(1) — the limitation period for issuing notice u/s 143(2) (3 months from the end of the FY in which the return is furnished) runs from that original filing date, not the rectification date. |
| **IBS Software Services (P.) Ltd. [2025] (Ker.)** | Sec 144C(13)'s one-month time limit (from the end of the month in which DRP directions are received) for the AO to pass the final assessment order is **mandatory, not directory**; an order passed beyond this limit is invalid, regardless of any claimed absence of prejudice to the assessee. |
| **Frontier Information Tech Ltd. (Telangana HC)** ⚠️ VERIFY — exact citation/year not legible in source | Conversion of unpaid interest into **equity shares** amounts to "actual payment" u/s 43B — issuing shares discharges/extinguishes the interest liability, so it is not a mere book entry; deduction u/s 43B is allowable in the year of such conversion. (Consistent with the Supreme Court's reasoning in *M.M. Aqua Technologies* on conversion of interest into debentures.) |
| **Jindal Tractebel Power Co. Ltd. [2025] (Karn.)** | Bona fide reliance on a **reputed law firm's/CA firm's professional advice** that no TDS was deductible on payments to a foreign entity (income not taxable in India) constitutes "reasonable cause" u/s 273B — hence no penalty u/s 271C for non-deduction of TDS, absent mala fide intent or undue benefit. |

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - "Interest" under a DTAA vs. Sec 2(28A) is construed **contextually within the loan privity** — guarantee/comfort-letter fees are commonly examined distractors that do *not* qualify as interest (Johnson Matthey).
  - For share-capital reduction fact patterns, remember "transfer" is satisfied via **extinguishment of rights**, not just via a sale/exchange (Jupiter Capital), building on the older *Kartikeya V. Sarabhai* line of reasoning.
  - Recent (2025) SC/HC rulings above are current-year "hot" additions — expect at least one 4-6 mark case-law-based question from this set.

---

### 5. Sec 170A — Modified Return on Business Reorganisation

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - Where, before the date of an order of a High Court/Tribunal/Adjudicating Authority under the IBC 2016 sanctioning a **business reorganisation**, the successor has already furnished a return u/s 139 for an AY relevant to the PY to which the order applies, the successor must furnish a **modified return** (Form ITR-A, electronically) within **6 months** from the end of the month in which the order was issued.
  - **Completed assessments:** AO modifies the assessment/reassessment as per the modified return.
  - **Pending assessments:** AO completes the assessment/reassessment in line with the modified return.
  - "Business reorganisation" = amalgamation, demerger, or merger of business of one or more persons.

- **Concept:** Sec 170A lets a successor entity align its already-filed return with the terms of a court/tribunal-sanctioned restructuring (which often has retrospective effect), rather than needing a fresh assessment from scratch.

- **Example (from source):** A Ltd. merges into B Ltd. w.e.f. 1.4.2022 vide HC order dated 1.11.2023; B Ltd. had already filed its AY 2023-24 return on 30.10.2023 — B Ltd. must file its modified return for AY 2023-24 (limited to the terms of the HC order) on or before **31.5.2024** (6 months from the end of November 2023).

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** the 6-month clock runs from the **end of the month** of the order, not from the date of the order itself.

---

### 6. Sec 89A — Relief for Income from Retirement Benefit Account in a Notified Country

- **Key formula(s)/rule(s):**
  - Applies to a **"specified person"** — a person resident in India who opened a "specified account" in a notified country while he was a non-resident in India and a resident of that country.
  - **Notified countries:** Canada, USA, and UK.
  - **Specified account:** an account maintained by the specified person in a notified country for retirement benefits, where income from the account is **not taxed on accrual** by that country but only at the time of **withdrawal or redemption**.
  - **Option:** at the specified person's choice, such income (accruing in PY 2021-22 or later) may instead be included in the total income of the PY in which it is **taxed abroad on withdrawal/redemption** — deferring Indian taxation to match the foreign taxation point.
  - **Exclusions once option exercised:** the deferred-year income shall exclude amounts already taxed in India in an earlier PY, and amounts that were not taxable in India in the year of accrual because the person was NR/RNOR in that year or by virtue of a DTAA. Foreign tax on such income is ignored while computing FTC under Rule 128.
  - **Mechanics:** option exercised via **Form 10-EE**, electronically, on or before the due date u/s 139(1); once exercised for an account, it applies to **all subsequent years** and **cannot be withdrawn** (except where the person again becomes non-resident).
  - **Becoming NR again:** if the person becomes NR in a later "relevant PY" after having exercised the option, the option is deemed **never exercised from that relevant PY** — all income accrued in the specified account from the year the option was first exercised up to the year immediately before the relevant PY becomes taxable in the year immediately preceding the relevant PY, with tax payable by the due date of the ROI for the relevant PY.

- **Concept:** Sec 89A prevents mismatch/hardship where the account is taxed by the foreign country only at withdrawal but would otherwise be taxed by India on year-to-year accrual (e.g., US 401(k)/IRA-type accounts held by returning NRIs).

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** Note the three notified countries are exactly **Canada, USA, UK** — a favourite one-line objective question.

---

### 7. Recent CBDT Circulars & Notifications ⚠️ VERIFY — figures per source concept-book; cross-check against the live CBDT circular/notification text before the exam

- **Key rule(s):**
  - **Circular No. 15/2024** — monetary limits for waiver/reduction of interest u/s 220(2) (interest @1% p.m./part-month for delay beyond 30 days of demand notice):

| Authority | Waiver/reduction limit |
|---|---|
| CIT / PCIT | Up to ₹50 lakh |
| CCIT / DGIT | Above ₹50 lakh up to ₹1.5 crore |
| PCCIT | Above ₹1.5 crore |

  - **Notification No. 14/2025** — a non-resident having a liaison office in India must submit its annual activity statement to the AO within **8 months** from the end of the relevant financial year.
  - **Notification No. 123/2024** — Sec 194N (TDS on cash withdrawal) does **not** apply to foreign representations approved by the MEA — diplomatic missions, UN agencies, international organisations, consulates, and honorary consul offices — that are exempt from Indian tax under the Diplomatic Relations (Vienna Convention) Act, 1972 and the United Nations (Privileges and Immunities) Act, 1947.
  - **Circular No. 9/2025** — relief from higher TDS/TCS (Sec 206AA/206CC) where the deductee's/collectee's PAN was inoperative for non-linking with Aadhaar: for payments/credits between **1.4.2024 and 31.7.2025**, normal rates apply if PAN is made operative by **30.9.2025**; for transactions on/after **1.8.2025**, normal rates apply if PAN is made operative within **2 months** from the end of the relevant month.

- **Concept:** These are "current amendment" add-ons frequently tested as 1-2 mark objective/short-answer items in the DT paper's recent-updates section.

---

### 8. Compounding of Offences — New Guidelines vide Circular No. 4/2025 (w.e.f. 17.10.2024)

- **Key rule(s):**
  - **Meaning:** a mechanism sparing the defaulter major legal/prosecution consequences on payment of a specified sum; **all offences** under the Income-tax Act, 1961 are compoundable, either before or after initiation of prosecution proceedings.
  - **Application:** filed with the jurisdictional Pr.CCIT/CCIT/Pr.DGIT/DGIT, any time after the offence is committed (whether or not it has come to the Department's notice). A **"Consolidated Compounding Application"** covers offences for multiple years (assessees) or quarters (deductors).
  - **Non-refundable application fee** (adjustable against final compounding charges): **₹25,000** per single application; **₹50,000** per consolidated application.
  - Applicant must pay all outstanding tax (tax + surcharge + cess), interest (including interest u/s 220), penalty, and other dues related to the offence — any shortfall found on departmental verification must be paid within 30 days (extendable up to a max. of 3 months) of intimation, else the application is invalid.
  - Applicant must undertake to **withdraw related appeals**.
  - A defective application can be revived (without fresh fee) if cured within **1 month** of intimation of the defect.
  - **Compounding charges — repeat applications for the same offence type:** 2nd time = 1.2×, 3rd time = 1.4×, 4th time = 1.6×, and so on (base = tax + surcharge + cess; interest excluded).
  - **Late application** (filed more than 12 months after the prosecution complaint was filed): **50% extra** charges.
  - **Process timelines:**

| Step | Timeline |
|---|---|
| Rejection order (if not acceptable), with reasons | Preferably within 2 months from end of month of receipt of application |
| Intimation of approval + charges/liabilities (if acceptable) | Within 2 months from end of month of receipt |
| Payment of compounding charges | Within 1 month from end of month of intimation |
| Extension of payment: up to 6 months | Competent Authority (exceptional cases) |
| Extension: 6–12 months | Needs Pr.CCIT's written approval |
| Extension: 12–24 months | Needs CBDT Chairman/authorised Member approval |
| Extension: beyond 24 months | Not allowed |
| Final compounding order | Within 1 month from end of month of payment of charges |

  - All the above timelines are **administrative**, not statutory limitation periods.
  - **Co-accused/abettors** (e.g., directors of a company, karta of an HUF) may apply separately or jointly with the main accused; only a **single compounding charge** applies per offence — once paid by any one party, offences of both the main accused and co-accused stand compounded.

- **Concept:** Compounding offers an administrative escape from prosecution in exchange for payment of compounding charges (a multiple of the tax involved) — increasingly tested given the 2024 CBDT guideline overhaul.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:** remember the fee figures (₹25,000/₹50,000) are **application fees**, distinct from and adjustable against the eventual **compounding charges**.

---

### 9. Safe Harbour Rules — Sec 92CB read with Rule 10TD

- **Key rule(s):**
  - **Meaning:** circumstances in which income-tax authorities shall **accept the transfer price declared by the assessee** for an "eligible international transaction" entered into by an "eligible assessee," without a TP adjustment.

**(a) Software Development Services (SDS) / IT-enabled Services (ITES):**

| Value of international transaction | Minimum OP/OpEx margin |
|---|---|
| Up to ₹100 crore | 17% |
| > ₹100 crore up to ₹300 crore | 18% |

**(b) Knowledge Process Outsourcing (KPO) services** (applies only if total transaction value is up to ₹300 crore):

| Employee cost as % of operating expense | Minimum OP/OpEx margin |
|---|---|
| Less than 40% | 18% |
| 40% or more but less than 60% | 21% |
| 60% or more | 24% |

**(c) Intra-group loans, INR-denominated:** interest declared ≥ SBI's 1-year MCLR as on 1st April of the PY, **plus**:

| AE credit rating | Spread |
|---|---|
| AAA to A | +1.75% (175 bps) |
| BBB- / BBB / BBB+ | +3.25% (325 bps) |
| BB to B | +4.75% (475 bps) |
| C to D | +6.25% (625 bps) |
| No credit rating, and total INR loans to all AEs up to ₹100 crore (as on 31 March) | +4.25% (425 bps) |

**(d) Intra-group loans, foreign-currency denominated:** interest ≥ reference rate of the currency as on 30th September of the PY, plus a spread that varies by AE credit rating **and** by whether total loans to AEs are below/above ₹250 crore (as on 31 March) — ranging from **+1.50%** (AAA to A band, either slab) up to **+6.00%** (C+ to D/unrated, ≥₹250 crore slab).

**(e) Corporate guarantee:** minimum guarantee commission/fee of **1% per annum** on the guaranteed amount (explicit guarantee for borrowings of a wholly-owned NR subsidiary; excludes letters of comfort/implicit/performance guarantees).

**(f) Contract R&D relating to software development, or to generic pharmaceutical drugs:** minimum OP/OpEx **24%**, ⚠️ VERIFY — where transaction value is up to ₹300 crore (source states ₹300 crore; some editions of Rule 10TD list this ceiling at ₹200 crore — confirm the currently notified figure before the exam).

**(g) Manufacture and export of auto components:**

| Category | Minimum OP/OpEx |
|---|---|
| Core auto components (engine/powertrain, transmission/steering, suspension/braking, li-ion batteries for EV/hybrid) | 12% |
| Non-core auto components | 8.5% |

**(h) Receipt of low value-adding intra-group services:** safe harbour applies only if the total value (including mark-up) is **up to ₹10 crore** and the mark-up is **up to 5%** (excludes R&D, manufacturing, software/IT, KPO/BPO, purchasing, sales/marketing/distribution, financial transactions, natural-resource extraction, and insurance/reinsurance services).

- **Concept:** Safe Harbour gives eligible assessees in specified sectors a pre-agreed minimum margin/rate — if met, the declared transfer price is accepted outright, sparing both sides a full-blown TP scrutiny.

- **Procedure:**
  1. **Form 3CEFA** filed with the AO on/before due date u/s 139(1) (for the first AY, if opting for multiple years); the return of income for that AY must be filed before/along with Form 3CEFA. Option validity = period stated in the form **or 3 years, whichever is less**.
  2. **AO verification** — whether the assessee is an eligible assessee and the transaction is an eligible international transaction; if in doubt, AO refers to the **TPO within 2 months** from the end of the month of receipt of Form 3CEFA.
  3. **TPO** may call for documents/information; can declare the option **invalid** for failure to furnish information, or if the assessee/transaction is not eligible — via a **written, reasoned order** served on the assessee and AO.
  4. **Remedy before CIT:** assessee may object within **15 days** of the TPO's order; CIT decides within **2 months** from the end of the month of receipt of the objection.
  5. If the AO/TPO/CIT fails to act within the prescribed time, the **option is deemed valid**.

- **Pitfalls / exam tips:**
  - The **2nd proviso to Sec 92C(2)** (tolerance range) does **not** apply once safe harbour is opted for.
  - TP documentation (Sec 92D) and the accountant's report in Form 3CEB (Sec 92E) remain **compulsory even under safe harbour** — a commonly tested trap.
  - Safe harbour is **not available** if the AE is in a Notified Jurisdictional Area or a no-tax/low-tax country (highest tax rate < 15%) under Sec 94A.
  - Once the price is accepted under safe harbour, the assessee **cannot invoke MAP** under the DTAA for that transaction.
  - In numericals: first test whether the declared OP/OpEx margin meets the safe-harbour floor; if not, the **primary adjustment** = (required minimum margin × operating expense) − actual operating profit declared.

- **Definitions:**

| Term | Meaning |
|---|---|
| SDS | Building/maintaining business apps using existing tools, language conversion, feature addition, debugging, adaptation, user documentation — excludes any R&D (even contract R&D) |
| ITES | IT-enabled BPO services — back office, call centres, data processing/mining, insurance-claim processing, legal databases, medical transcription, translation, payroll, remote maintenance, revenue accounting, website services, etc. — excludes any R&D |
| KPO | Higher-end, IT-driven BPO requiring advanced analytical/technical skill — GIS, HR services, engineering & design, animation, financial analytics, market research |
| Intra-group loan | A fixed-term loan by a non-financial group company to a non-resident AE; open-ended credit lines/facilities do not qualify |
| Low value-adding intra-group services | Support-type services not core to the business, not creating unique intangibles, not carrying significant risk, and not shareholder/duplicate services |

---

## ⚠️ Formulas to double-check


**00. Basics, Tax Rates (AY 26-27) & Alternate Taxation Regimes (115BAA/BAB/BAC/BAD/BAE)**
- **Marginal relief on rebate (115BAC only)** — if Total Income exceeds ₹12,00,000 but does not exceed **≈ ₹12,70,588** (⚠️ VERIFY — OCR prints ₹12,70,585; recomputed break-even = 60,000 ÷ 0.85 + 12,00,000 = ₹12,70,588, small variance likely from rounding under Sec. 288A/288B): tax on such income is capped at the amount by which Total Income exceeds ₹12,00,000.

**01. Income from Capital Gains**
- ⚠️ VERIFY — the precise current interplay of Sec. 87A rebate denial with 112A/111A gains has seen conflicting CPC processing positions/litigation in recent assessment years; confirm against the applicable Finance Act/CBDT position for the specific exam attempt before relying on it in a numerical answer.

**03. Corporate Reorganisation: Liquidation, Buy-Back, Amalgamation & Demerger**
- ⚠️ VERIFY — the precise statutory wording of "net worth" for Sec. 49(2C)/2(19AA)(iv) purposes; some formulations reference Explanation 1 to Sec. 2(19AA), confirm exact phrase ("paid-up share capital and general reserves as appearing in the books of account of the demerged company immediately before demerger") against the bare Act before quoting verbatim in an answer.

**05. Income Computation & Disclosure Standards (ICDS)**
- | Provision for bad and doubtful debts (banks/PFIs) | ⚠️ VERIFY — allowed under a specific provision for banks/PFIs/NBFCs (commonly cited as Sec. 36(1)(viia); OCR source read "36(1)(viii)", which is the special-reserve section for long-term finance entities, not the bad-debts provision section — confirm the exact clause before quoting in an answer) |

**06. Taxation of Political Parties/Electoral Trust, Firm/LLP & AOP/BOI**
- ⚠️ VERIFY — The Electoral Bond Scheme referred to in the "except through electoral bonds" carve-out was struck down as unconstitutional by the Supreme Court (Association for Democratic Reforms v. Union of India, Feb 2024) and bonds are no longer issued; the statutory text of Sec 13A is unchanged, but candidates should note the scheme is currently non-operative in practice even though the section still references it.
- ⚠️ VERIFY — the OCR source shows transition-year dual rates ("20/12.5%", "15/20%", "10/12.5%") reflecting the mid-year rate change of 23-07-2024 relevant only to PY 2024-25 (AY 2025-26); for PY 2025-26 (AY 2026-27, the year tested in May/Nov 2026 attempts) a full year at the post-amendment rates (12.5% / 20% / 12.5%) should apply — confirm against the Finance Act applicable to the specific attempt before the exam.

**07. Taxation of Business Trust, Investment Fund & Securitisation Trust**
- | SPV | ⚠️ VERIFY — Commonly defined (per SEBI REIT/InvIT Regulations, referenced into the Explanation to Sec 10(23FC)) as an Indian company/LLP in which the Business Trust holds (or proposes to hold) controlling interest and not less than 50% of equity share capital/interest — exact percentage threshold should be cross-checked against the current SEBI Regulations text for the relevant AY |
- ⚠️ VERIFY — For transfers **before 23 July 2024** the rate was 10% in excess of a ₹1,00,000 threshold; confirm which rate regime applies to the specific transaction date in a problem.
- Other persons (e.g., trust/AOP/BOI form of fund) — **Maximum Marginal Rate (MMR)** — ⚠️ VERIFY — currently taken as **~39%** (30% + 25% surcharge + 4% cess) under the default tax regime; confirm the applicable surcharge slab for the relevant AY as MMR is a moving target tied to Finance Act surcharge rates.
- ⚠️ VERIFY — Best-recollected rates (differs from a source line suggesting a flat 10% for residents): **Resident individual/HUF payee — 25%; any other resident payee — 30%; NR (not company)/Foreign Company payee — Rate in force.** This should be cross-checked against the current bare-Act text of Sec 194LBC before relying on it in an exam answer, as the source material for this chapter states a flat 10% resident rate which does not match this reviewer's recollection of the statute.
- **Note on this chapter's verification:** Live web-search cross-checking could not be completed in this session (search budget exhausted before this chapter's queries ran); all figures above rely on the author's trained knowledge of the Income-tax Act and Finance Act amendments through early 2026, with residual uncertainty flagged inline via ⚠️ VERIFY tags (SPV shareholding threshold, MMR surcharge rate, and the Sec 194LBC resident TDS rate). Please cross-check flagged items against the current bare Act/Finance Act text before an exam.

**08. Minimum Alternate Tax (MAT) & Alternate Minimum Tax (AMT)**
- ⚠️ VERIFY — the OCR compresses domestic/foreign surcharge into "7%/2%" and "12%/5%"; reconstructed above as domestic-co./foreign-co. pairs matching the standard company surcharge slabs — cross-check against the applicable Finance Act for the exam year before quoting in an answer.
- **Deductions:** amount withdrawn from a reserve (only if the reserve was originally created through the P&L route); income exempt u/s 10/11/12; deferred tax; depreciation (excluding depreciation attributable to asset revaluation); ⚠️ VERIFY — profit of a "sick industrial company" (this SICA-linked exemption predates repeal of the Sick Industrial Companies Act and may not survive on the current syllabus in this form — the operative current relief is the IBC-linked item below); transfer from revaluation reserve to the extent of depreciation on revalued assets; brought-forward business loss / unabsorbed depreciation, in **full**, for a company against which a CIRP application stands admitted under Sec 7/9/10 of the IBC, 2016, or whose Board has been suspended/reconstituted by the Tribunal on a Central Government application u/s 241–242 of the Companies Act, 2013 (subsidiary test: holding company holds >50% of nominal equity value); brought-forward loss and unabsorbed depreciation for other companies restricted to the **lower of the two**; income already taxed as share of AOP/BOI income; income to a foreign company from capital gains on securities, or interest/dividend/royalty/FTS taxed at a rate **below 15%**; notional gain on exchange of SPV shares for business-trust units; actual loss on transfer of business-trust units; income by way of patent royalty taxable u/s 115BBF @10%.
- **Concept:** Sec 115JB(5) makes other Act provisions applicable to MAT computation; on this basis one Madras High Court view (⚠️ VERIFY — case name/citation as *Metal and Chromium Plater (P) Ltd. [2019] (Mad.)* per source notes, cross-check citation before quoting) holds that LTCG exempt u/s 54EC while computing normal total income should also be excluded from Book Profit, i.e., **MAT does not apply to such LTCG**. A contrary Kerala High Court view in *N.J. Jose & Co. (P) Ltd.* holds such exempt LTCG **must be included** in Book Profit, so MAT does apply.
- Note: Live web-source verification for this chapter could not be completed within this session (web-search quota was exhausted before chapter-specific queries ran); figures above rely on the author's trained knowledge of the Act and cited Finance Acts as of the current (2026 attempts) syllabus — items with residual uncertainty are flagged ⚠️ VERIFY inline and should be cross-checked against the Finance Act applicable for the relevant assessment year before an exam.

**09. Deductions: Sec 10AA (SEZ) & Chapter VI-A**
- ⚠️ VERIFY — Deduction is available only where the SEZ unit received necessary approval up to **31.03.2020** and began manufacture/production/services up to **31.03.2021** (the 31.3.2021 sunset reflects the one-year COVID extension under the Taxation and Other Laws (Relaxation of Certain Provisions) Act, 2020; confirm the exact wording against the current Finance Act text before quoting in an answer).
- | Bank branch (OBU) in SEZ | 100% of income for first 5 AYs, then 50% for next 5 AYs ⚠️ VERIFY — note claims this was enhanced to 100% for the next 5 AYs from AY 2023-24; confirm against the current Finance Act text before relying on this in an exam answer |

**10. Clubbing of Income & Set-off/Carry Forward of Losses**
- ⚠️ VERIFY — the OCR's illustrative numeric examples under Sec 79 (Example-1/2 shareholding patterns) are directionally consistent with the 51%-test logic as reproduced, but exact percentage figures in the source table should be cross-checked against the original if used for a numerical answer.
- \* ⚠️ VERIFY — **effective for amalgamations/successions on or after 1/4/2025**, the source states the "fresh 8 years" benefit is replaced by carry-forward for only the **remaining part of the original 8-year period** (i.e., no fresh lease of life). This aligns with a Finance Act 2025 change; confirm against the Finance Act 2025 text/CBDT notification before relying on it in a live exam answer, since it could not be freshly cross-checked against a primary source in this session.

**11. Advance Tax, TDS & TCS**

- Time limit for AO's order treating a person as assessee-in-default for **non-deduction**: within **6 years** from the end of the F.Y. in which payment/credit was made (⚠️ VERIFY — several ICAI/professional summaries note a longer **7-year** limit specifically for payments to non-residents u/s 195; confirm which limit your source material intends before quoting a single figure in an answer).
